Salah — Prayer

Wujub of Preceding Fatihah over Surah
Ruling on the order of recitation: Fatihah before surah is wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the order of recitation in prayer, identify the proof (muwazabah) that establishes it as wajib, and apply the correct remedy when the order is violated.

Core Idea
Preceding Fatihah over surah is wajib; omitting the order requires sajdah al-sahw, not repetition of prayer.

In prayer, surat al-Fatihah must be recited before any other Quranic recitation. The Hanafi school holds this order to be wajib, established by the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah). If one inadvertently begins with a surah, he must correct it and perform sajdah al-sahw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is the order of recitation: Fatihah before any other surah. The ruling is wajib.
Wajib means obligatory but not at the level of fard; omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw), not repetition of the prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is 'muwazabah' – the Prophet's constant practice of reciting Fatihah before the surah. In Hanafi usul, this indicates an obligation.
The dalil is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah, making the ruling wajib rather than fard.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does muwazabah prove wujub? The Prophet's continual adherence to this order shows it is a required element of prayer, not merely recommended.
If it were sunnah, occasional omission would not require sajdah al-sahw.
4
Note the consequence of violation
The text specifies that if one begins with a surah and remembers, he must recite Fatihah, then the surah again, and perform sajdah al-sahw for the delay of a wajib.
This is analogous to repeating Fatihah, which also requires sajdah al-sahw.
5
Distinguish from fard
Why is this not fard? Because the evidence (muwazabah) is zanni, not qat'i from Quran or mutawatir sunnah. Thus it is wajib, and the prayer remains valid even if the order is forgotten, as long as the wajib is compensated.
If it were fard, the prayer would be invalid without it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب تقديم الفاتحة على قراءة السورة للمواظبة حتى لو قرأ من السورة ابتداء فتذكر يقرأ الفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ويسجد للسهو كما لو كرر الفاتحة ثم قرأ السورة
And it is obligatory to present the Fatihah before the recitation of the surah due to constancy, so that if one began with the surah and remembered, he recites the Fatihah, then recites the surah and performs sajdah al-sahw, just as if he repeated the Fatihah and then read the surah.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This ruling establishes that the order of recitation in prayer is wajib: Fatihah must precede the surah. The proof is the Prophet's constant practice. If one inadvertently starts with the surah, upon remembering he must recite Fatihah and then the surah again, and perform sajdah al-sahw for the delay of the wajib. Similarly, if he repeats Fatihah, he also performs sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms
تقديم الفاتحة (taqdim al-fatihah): Reciting surat al-Fatihah before any other Quranic recitation in prayer.
المواظبة (al-muwazabah): The Prophet's constant and continual practice, used as evidence for obligation in Hanafi fiqh.
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, performed to compensate for a missing or delayed wajib in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person accidentally begins reciting a surah before Fatihah in prayer, what should he do?
A) Continue and ignore.
B) Recite Fatihah immediately and continue, no sajdah.
C) Recite Fatihah, then repeat the surah, and perform sajdah al-sahw.
D) Repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
The order of Fatihah before surah is wajib; violation requires correction and sajdah al-sahw.

Wujub of Including the Hard Nose in Sujud
Ruling on the obligatory part of the nose in sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on including the nose in sujud and explain why it is wajib based on the proof of muwazabah.

Core Idea
The hard part of the nose must touch the ground in sujud; omitting it invalidates the prayer.

In the Hanafi school, prostration (sujud) has specific requirements beyond just the forehead. This lesson clarifies the ruling on including the nose, specifically its hard, bony part. Understanding this obligation is essential for the validity of salah, as neglecting it renders the prayer invalid according to the correct view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
State the ruling: it is wajib to include the hard part of the nose with the forehead in sujud. Identify the proof: the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah) on this action.
2
Understand the evidence
The proof is the Prophet's muwazabah – his continuous and habitual performance. In Hanafi usul, muwazabah indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is evidence to the contrary.
The text uses the phrase 'للمواظبة عليه' (due to constancy upon it).
3
Note the ikhtilaf
There is disagreement within the Hanafi school and with other schools. Some Hanafi say it is not required if there is an excuse; the correct view is that it is wajib even then. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not require nose contact at all.
The text says 'على الصحيح' (according to the correct view), indicating the relied-upon position.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is wajib. If a person prostrates only on the nose (without the forehead) or only on the forehead (without the nose), the prayer is invalid.
Exception: if there is a valid excuse like a forehead wound, then only the nose suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب ضم الأنف أي ما صلب منه للجبهة في السجود للمواظبة عليه ولا تجوز الصلاة بالاقتصار على الأنف في السجود على الصحيح
And it is obligatory to include the nose, i.e., the hard part of it, with the forehead in prostration due to constancy upon it, and prayer is not permissible by limiting to the nose in prostration according to the correct view.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This ruling concerns the obligatory elements of sujud. The forehead alone is not sufficient; the hard (bony) part of the nose must also touch the ground. This is wajib due to the Prophet's constant practice. If one prostrates only on the nose (the soft part?) without the forehead, the prayer is invalid according to the correct view, unless there is an excuse (like a wound on the forehead).

Key Terms
الأنف الصلب (al-anf al-sulb): The hard, bony part of the nose (the bridge).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person prostrates only on the soft part of the nose (the tip) and not on the hard part?
A) Valid, because soft part is part of the nose.
B) Invalid, because only the hard part is wajib.
C) Valid but makruh.
D) Requires sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi prayer, the hard part of the nose must touch the ground in sujud; neglecting it invalidates the prayer unless there is a valid excuse.

Wujub of Order Between the Two Prostrations
Ruling on sequence: second sajdah must occur before other actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the order between the two sajdahs, explain why it is wajib, and apply the remedy if the order is missed.

Core Idea
The second sajdah must immediately follow the first; omitting it requires a compensatory prostration, not invalidating the prayer.

In this lesson, we examine a specific element of the prayer that is often misunderstood: the obligation to perform the two prostrations in sequence without any intervening action. The Hanafi school holds this order to be wajib, established by prophetic constancy (muwazabah). We will see what happens if a person forgets and performs the second sajdah out of order or misses it entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the order (tartib) between the two sajdahs in each rak'ah. The ruling is wajib, meaning it is obligatory but not a pillar.
Wajib differs from fard; missing it does not invalidate the prayer if compensated.
2
Understand the requirement
The second sajdah must be performed before any other action in that rak'ah, such as standing, sitting, or moving to the next rak'ah.
This applies to both fard and nafl prayers.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is muwazabah (the Prophet's constant practice). In Hanafi usul, constancy indicates obligation.
The proof is zanni in both thubut and dalala.
4
Determine the consequence of missing
If the second sajdah is missed, it must still be performed later, and the subsequent actions (like final sitting) must be repeated.
The earlier sitting is invalidated because it occurred before the sajdah was completed.
5
Apply the remedy
Even if one remembers after the final tashahhud, he should prostrate the missed sajdah and then repeat the sitting and tashahhud before salam.
This ensures the correct sequence is restored.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب مراعاة الترتيب فيما بين السجدتين وهو الإتيان بالسجدة الثانية في كل ركعة من الفرض وغيره قبل الإنتقال لغيرها أي لغير السجدة من باقي أفعال الصلاة للمواظبة فإن فات يسجدها ولو بعد القعود الأخير ثم يعيد القعود
And it is obligatory to observe the order between the two prostrations, which is performing the second prostration in every rak'ah, whether fard or other, before moving to something other than it, i.e., to other than the prostration from the remaining actions of prayer, due to constancy. If it is missed, he prostrates it even after the final sitting, then repeats the sitting.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This ruling establishes that in each rak'ah, the two sajdahs must be performed in order without intervening actions. The second sajdah must directly follow the first, before any other action like standing or sitting. The proof is prophetic constancy. If one forgets and misses the second sajdah until after the final sitting (qa'dah), he must perform it later and then repeat the sitting and tashahhud, as the earlier sitting is invalidated.

Key Terms
الترتيب بين السجدتين (al-tartib bayna al-sajdatayn): The obligation to perform the second sajdah immediately after the first in the same rak'ah before any other action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgets the second sajdah in a rak'ah and only remembers after the final tashahhud, what should he do?
A) Nothing, the prayer is valid.
B) Perform the sajdah now, then repeat tashahhud and salam.
C) Repeat the entire prayer.
D) Perform sajdah al-sahw only.

Key Takeaway
The order between the two sajdahs is wajib; if missed, it must be performed later, and the subsequent actions repeated.

Wujub of Itmi'nan in Pillars
Ruling on tranquility in ruku' and sujud, with ikhtilaf on qawmah and jalsah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on itmi'nan in ruku' and sujud, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on qawmah and jalsah, and identify the mufta-bihi position.

Core Idea
Itmi'nan in prayer positions is wajib, supported by the hadith of the one who prayed badly.

This passage addresses a classic dispute within the Hanafi school: is tranquility (itmi'nan) during the prayer pillars obligatory or merely recommended? The author presents a spectrum of opinions—from fard to sunnah—and then clarifies the strongest view based on the evidence. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for proper prayer practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the positions under dispute
The passage discusses itmi'nan in ruku', sujud, qawmah (standing after ruku), jalsah (sitting between prostrations), and the act of rising from ruku. Note which are pillars and which are wajibat.
Ruku' and sujud are pillars; qawmah and jalsah are considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
2
Note the three views on itmi'nan in ruku' and sujud
Abu Yusuf said it is fard, al-Jurjani said sunnah, and Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said wajib. The author declares the correct view (fi al-sahih) as wajib.
Wajib is the middle position, between fard and sunnah.
3
Extend the analysis to qawmah and jalsah
Al-Karkhi held itmi'nan in these positions as sunnah, but the evidence (dalil) from the hadith of the one who prayed badly and the Prophet's constancy indicates obligation. Later scholars like Ibn al-Humam and Ibn Amir Haj confirmed it as wajib.
This extension is a later tarjih, not found in zahir al-riwaya.
4
Examine the dalil
The hadith of al-musi' salatahu contains an implicit command (amr dimni) to perform itmi'nan in all positions. The Prophet's constancy (muwazabah) also indicates obligation.
The command is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala, hence the ruling is wajib, not fard.
5
Conclude with the mufta-bihi
The later preferred view (mufta-bihi) is that itmi'nan is wajib in all positions: ruku', sujud, qawmah, jalsah, and rising from ruku. This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.
This view is considered 'sawab' (correct) by Ibn al-Humam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب الإطمئنان وهو التعديل في الأركان بتسكين الجوارح في الركوع والسجود حتى تطمئن مفاصله في الصحيح لتكميل الركن لا سنة كما قاله الجرجاني ولا فرض كما قاله أبو يوسف. ومقتضى الدليل وجوب الإطمئنان أيضاً في القومة والجلسة والرفع من الركوع للأمر في حديث المسيء صلاته، وللمواظبة على ذلك كله وإليه ذهب المحقق الكمال بن الهمام وتلميذه ابن أمير حاج وقال أنه الصواب
And it is obligatory to have tranquility, which is the adjustment in the pillars, by calming the limbs in bowing and prostration until his joints are still, according to the correct view, to complete the pillar, not sunnah as al-Jurjani said, nor fard as Abu Yusuf said. And the requirement of the evidence is the obligation of tranquility also in the standing after bowing (qawmah) and the sitting between prostrations (jalsah) and the rising from bowing, due to the command in the hadith of the one who prayed badly, and due to constancy upon all that. And to this went the muhaqqiq Kamal ibn al-Humam and his student Ibn Amir Haj, and he said that it is correct.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligation of itmi'nan (tranquility/steadiness) in the pillars of prayer. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (on the takhrij of al-Karkhi), it is wajib in ruku' and sujud to the extent that the joints settle (approximately the time for one tasbih). It is not sunnah (as al-Jurjani said) nor fard (as Abu Yusuf said). However, the apparent meaning of the evidence (dalil) - the hadith of the one who prayed badly and the Prophet's constancy - also requires itmi'nan in the standing after ruku (qawmah), the sitting between sajdahs (jalsah), and the act of rising from ruku. This view is preferred by Kamal ibn al-Humam and his student. The text notes that the dispute is not in zahir al-riwaya, but the later scholars lean toward it being wajib in all these positions.

Key Terms
الإطمئنان (al-itmi'nan): Stillness of the limbs in prayer positions so that the joints settle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view of later Hanafi scholars, what is the ruling on itmi'nan in the qawmah (standing after ruku')?
A) Sunnah
B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Itmi'nan in the pillars of prayer is wajib according to the majority of Hanafis; later scholars confirmed its obligation in all positions including qawmah and jalsah.

Wujub of First Sitting (Qa'dah Ula)
Ruling on first sitting with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the first sitting, identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and apply the consequence of its omission (sajdah al-sahw).

Core Idea
The first sitting is wajib, not fard — omitting it requires sajdah al-sahw, not repetition.

The first sitting (qa'dah ula) after the second rak'ah in prayers of three or four rak'ahs is a frequently discussed element. While some schools consider it fard, the Hanafi school holds it to be wajib, but with internal differences regarding nafl prayers. This passage clarifies the sahih position and the practical implications of the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
According to the sahih view and zahir al-riwaya, the first sitting is wajib in all prayers (fard, wajib, nafl). This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani based on istihsan.
Wajib means omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw).
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad (in another view) and Zufar hold it is fard in nafl prayers by qiyas. Al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi consider it sunnah.
The disagreement stems from different methods: istihsan vs qiyas.
3
Compare the proofs
The sahih view relies on istihsan (preferring prophetic practice over analogy). The opposing view uses qiyas (comparing nafl to fard).
Istihsan is preferred in Hanafi usul when there is a stronger practice.
4
Determine the operative ruling
The mufta bihi is wajib. This means if a person forgets the first sitting, they continue and perform sajdah al-sahw at the end. Deliberate omission makes the prayer makruh tahrimi.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in nafl, if first sitting is omitted, some would say the prayer is invalid (if fard), but Hanafi says it is valid with sajdah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب القعود الأول في الصحيح ولو كان حكماً وهو قعود مقدار قراءة التشهد بأسرع ما يكون لا فرق في ذلك بين الفرائض والواجبات والنوافل استحساناً عندهما وهو ظاهر الرواية والأصح وقال محمد وزفر والشافعي هو فرض في النوافل وهو القياس واختار الكرخي والطحاوي استنانه وأكثر المشايخ يطلقون عليه إسم السنة إما لأن وجوبه ثبت بالسنة أو لأن
And the first sitting is obligatory according to the correct view, even if it is virtual, and it is a sitting of the amount of reciting the tashahhud in the quickest manner. There is no difference in that between fara'id, wajibat, and nawafil, by istihsan according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and it is the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya) and the most correct. And Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i said: it is fard in nawafil, and that is qiyas. And al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi chose that it is sunnah, and most mashayikh call it sunnah, either because its obligation is established by sunnah or because...
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of the first sitting (qa'dah ula) in prayer, where one recites tashahhud. According to the correct view in the Hanafi school, it is wajib in all prayers (fard, wajib, nafl). This is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) based on istihsan, and it is in the zahir al-riwaya. Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (Imam Muhammad) himself, along with Zufar and al-Shafi'i, held it to be fard in nafl prayers, which is qiyas. Al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi considered it sunnah. The majority of later scholars call it sunnah, possibly because its obligation is derived from sunnah (prophetic practice) or for another reason. The mufta bihi view is that it is wajib according to the sahih.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qu'ud al-awwal): The first sitting after the second rak'ah in prayers of three or four rak'ahs, where tashahhud is recited.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that abandons qiyas for a stronger evidence or necessity.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that extends a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a nafl prayer, according to the Hanafi school's sahih view, the first sitting is:
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Optional

Key Takeaway
The first sitting is wajib in all prayers per the Hanafi school, and its omission necessitates sajdah al-sahw.

Obligations of the Latecomer (Masbuq) in Completing Missed Rak'ahs
Explaining the wajibat for the latecomer regarding tashahhud and standing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two wajibat for the masbuq in his qada and identify the evidence from the Prophet's continuous practice.

Core Idea
For the masbuq, tashahhud in every sitting except the last is wajib, and standing for the next rak'ah must be immediate.

The latecomer (masbuq) completes his missed rak'ahs after the imam's taslim. This passage from Maraqi al-Falah, with al-Tahtawi's hashya, clarifies two key obligations: reciting tashahhud in every sitting except the final one, and standing promptly for the next rak'ah. The evidence is the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazaba), which in Hanafi usul indicates wujub. The hashya also explains the consequences of adding an extra action forgetfully.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two wajibat
Read the matn: the first wajib is reciting tashahhud in the first sitting (and by extension, every sitting except the last); the second is standing for the third rak'ah without delay after tashahhud.
The hashya clarifies that 'first' means all non-final sittings.
2
Understand the evidence
The proof is 'al-muwazaba' — the Prophet's continuous practice. In Hanafi usul, this indicates wujub (obligation) at the level of sunnah mu'akkada.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i view that these are sunnah.
3
Recognize the definition of 'first'
Al-Tahtawi explains that 'first' (al-awwal) in this context means every sitting that is not the final one. For a masbuq with multiple missed rak'ahs, there can be multiple such sittings, all wajib for tashahhud.
Example: masbuq who catches one rak'ah of Maghrib has two missed rak'ahs — he will have one sitting (after the first missed rak'ah) which is wajib for tashahhud.
4
Determine the ruling for extra actions
If the masbuq unintentionally adds an action equivalent to a pillar (e.g., saying 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad') after tashahhud, he must perform sajda al-sahw. If done intentionally, the prayer becomes makruh tahrimi.
The hashya emphasizes that the addition is only problematic if it delays the standing for the next rak'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسبوق فيما يقضيه ولو جلس الأول تبعاً للإمام المواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وسجوده للسهو لما تركه، وقام ساهياً (و) يجب قراءة التشهد فيه أي في الأول وقوله (في الصحيح) متعلق بكل من القعود وتشهده وهو احتراز عن القول بسنيتهما أو سنية التشهد وحده للمواظبة (و) يجب (قراءته) أي التشهد في الجلوس الأخير أيضاً للمواظبة (و) يجب (القيام إلى الركعة (الثالثة من غير تراخ بعد قراءة التشهد حتى لو زاد عليه بمقدار أداء ركن ساهياً يسجد للسهو لتأخير واجب القيام للثالثة

(1) المؤكدة في معنى الواجب وهذا لا يقتضي رفع الخلاف ولا يرد ما لو سبق الإمام المسافر الحدث، واستخلف مقيماً حيث كانت القعدة الأولى فرضاً في حقه لأنه لعارض الإستخلاف أفاده السيد، ثم إن الأولى ،حذف قوله في الصحيح لتصريح المصنف به بعد قوله: (ولو كان حكماً فيه إشارة إلى أنه أراد بالأول ما ليس بآخر فالمسبوق بثلاث في الرباعية ثلاث قعدات والواجب منها ما عدا الأخير. قاله السيد وفيه أن الأول فرض بمقتضى المتابعة وقول الشرح وهو قعود المسبوق فيما يقضيه يفيد أن الواجب ما انفرد المسبوق بقضائه فقط فليتأمل. قوله : (ويجب قراءة التشهد فيسجد للسهو بترك بعضه ككله كما في الدر. قوله : (أي في الأول) المراد به كما سبق ما عدا الأخير على ما فيه فإنه قد يتكرر مراراً قوله : (للمواظبة) علة لقوله ، ويجب قراءة التشهد قوله حتى لو زاد عليه أي على التشهد قوله: (بمقدار أداء ركن الخ) على الصحيح وبينوه بما إذا قال: اللهم صل على محمد ولم يذكره الشرح تباعداً عما يوهم المنع من ذكر الصلاة عليه وقوله ساهياً إحترز به عن العمد فإن الصلاة تكون به مكروهة تحريماً. قوله : (بمقدار أداء ركن ساهياً يسجد للسهو) وقيل يسجد بزيادة حرف.
The latecomer in what he performs (qada), even if he sits the first sitting following the imam, due to the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazaba), and he prostrates for forgetfulness for leaving it, and he stands forgetfully. And it is obligatory to recite tashahhud in it, i.e., in the first, and his statement 'in the correct [view]' relates to both the sitting and his tashahhud, and it is a precaution against the statement that both are sunnah or that tashahhud alone is sunnah due to the continuous practice. And it is obligatory to recite it (the tashahhud) in the last sitting as well, due to continuous practice. And it is obligatory to stand for the third rak'ah without delay after reciting tashahhud, such that if he adds to it [by performing an action] equivalent to performing a pillar forgetfully, he prostrates for forgetfulness due to delaying the obligatory standing for the third [rak'ah].
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah outlines the wajibat (obligatory acts) for a masbuq (one who catches part of the prayer with the imam) when he completes his missed rak'ahs after the imam's taslim. The Hashiya of al-Tahtawi comments on several points. First, the masbuq must recite the tashahhud in his first sitting (the one he performs after the imam finishes). This is wajib, not sunnah, based on the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazaba). The commentator clarifies that 'first' refers to every sitting except the final one; for example, if a masbuq catches one rak'ah of a four-rak'ah prayer, he will have three qadas, with two sittings: the first (which is wajib for tashahhud) and the last (which is also wajib). If he misses part of the tashahhud, he must prostrate for forgetfulness. Second, he must stand for the third rak'ah immediately after the tashahhud without any delay. If he adds an action equivalent to a pillar (e.g., saying 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad' forgetfully), he must do sajda al-sahw. The hashya notes that this addition is only a problem if done forgetfully; if intentional, the prayer becomes makruh tahrimi. The overall authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah as it is a standard Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joins the prayer after the imam has already begun, and completes his missed rak'ahs after the imam's taslim.
المواظبة (al-muwazaba): The continuous practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) which in Hanafi usul indicates wujub (obligation) at the level of sunnah mu'akkada or wajib.
سجود السهو (sajda al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for an omission or addition in prayer that does not invalidate it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on reciting tashahhud in the first sitting for a masbuq (latecomer) according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is sunnah
B) It is wajib
C) It is fard
D) It is mubah

Key Takeaway
The masbuq must recite tashahhud in every non-final sitting and stand immediately for the next rak'ah; both are wajib based on the Prophet's continuous practice, requiring sajda al-sahw if omitted forgetfully.

Obligation of Reciting Salam Twice in Prayer
Detailing the wajib nature of the two salams and related issues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of salams in prayer, explain the evidence from continuous practice, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the second salam.

Core Idea
Salam twice is wajib in the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's continuous practice.

This lesson examines the legal ruling on the salam in prayer. The Hanafi school holds that uttering salam twice to the right and left is wajib, established by the continual practice of the Prophet. However, there is an intra-Hanafi difference of opinion on whether the second salam is wajib or sunnah. We will explore the evidence and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the utterance of salam in prayer. Determine the hukm level: wajib.
The salam is a wajib act, not a rukn.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is 'continuous practice' (muwazaba). This is a sunnah-based proof, specifically the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.
Muwazaba refers to the Prophet's consistent practice.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., in al-Fath) consider the second salam sunnah. Identify which view is considered 'al-ashahh' (most correct).
The text states that 'twice' is the most correct.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Tahtawi and the later scholars prefer that both salams are wajib. The relied-upon position for fatwa is wajib.
This is the operative ruling.
5
Apply to joining the prayer
If someone joins after the first salam but before 'alaykum, the prayer is invalid. This shows the importance of the complete salam.
The joining issue highlights the integral nature of the salam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يجب لفظ (السلام) مرتين في اليمين واليسار للمواظبة

قوله : (مرتين) هو الأصح وقيل الثانية سنة كما في الفتح، ثم الخروج من الصلاة بسلام واحد عند العامة، وقيل بهما كما في مجمع الأنهر ، فلو إقتدى به بعد لفظ السلام الأول قبل عليكم لا يصح عند العامة، وقيل: إن أدركه بعد التسليمة، الأولى قبل الثانية فقد أدرك معه الصلاة كما السراج، واعلم أن السلام واجب للصلاة ذات الركوع والسجود، فلا . يرد صلاة الجنازة ولا سلام سجود السهو والشكر على القول به حموي، وفي ذكر الشكر نظر لأن سلام له كسجود التلاوة وفي الزاهدي ان سلام الجنازة سنة .اهـ. قوله : (في اليمين واليسار) يشعر أن الإلتفات فيهما واجب للمواظبة والنص بخلافه .

فرع: لو أتى بلفظ آخر لا يقوم مقام السلام، ولو كان بمعناه كما في مجمع الأنهر.
قوله: الحديث ابن مسعود (دون عليكم الحصول المقصود بلفظ السلام دون متعلقه ويتجه الوجوب بالمواظبة عليه أيضاً
And it is obligatory to utter the salam twice, to the right and left, due to continuous practice. His statement: (twice) is the most correct, and it is said the second is sunnah as in al-Fath. Then exiting the prayer with one salam is the view of the general scholars, and it is said with both as in Majma' al-Anhur. So if someone joins him after the first utterance of salam before 'alaykum, it is not valid according to the general scholars, and it is said: if he catches him after the first taslima before the second, he has caught the prayer with him as in al-Siraj. Know that salam is wajib for prayers that have ruku' and sujood, so the janazah prayer is exempted, nor the salam of sajda al-sahw and shukr according to the view of al-Hamawi. In mentioning shukr there is consideration because its salam is like that of tilawa, and in al-Zahidi, the salam of janazah is sunnah. His statement: (to the right and left) suggests that turning in them is wajib due to continuous practice, but the text is contrary. Branch: If one says another wording, it does not substitute for salam, even if it has the same meaning, as in Majma' al-Anhur. His statement: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'without alaykum, the desired is achieved by the word salam without its adjunct, and the obligation is directed by continuous practice as well.'
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This lesson covers the wajib nature of salam in prayer. The hashya explains that saying salam twice is the correct view (al-ashahh) and some say the second is sunnah. The exit from prayer with one salam is the view of the general scholars, but others say two. It then discusses the fiqh of joining after the salam, and states that salam is wajib for prayers with ruku' and sujood, not for janazah or sajda al-sahw. The hashya also addresses the wording of salam, that if one says something else, it does not substitute. The evidence is the Prophet's continuous practice. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
السلام (al-salam): The utterance of 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' to exit the prayer.
الإلتفات (al-iltifat): Turning the face to the right and left when saying salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Twice
C) Once for the imam, twice for the follower
D) None, it is sunnah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that uttering salam twice to the right and left is wajib, based on the Prophet's continuous practice; omitting the second salam requires compensation.

Wajib Acts in Prayer: Taslim, Qunut, Takbirs, and Recitation Rulings
Detailed enumeration of wajib acts with proofs and intra-school differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on key wajib acts in prayer (taslim, qunut, 'Id takbirs, opening takbir, jahr/israr) and identify the proofs and intra-school differences for each.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, many prayer acts are wajib due to the Prophet's constant practice (muwāẓabah), not due to an explicit Quranic command — a distinction that determines whether sajdah sahw is required for omission.

This passage from Hāshiyat al-Ṭaḥṭāwī details several acts that the Hanafi school considers wajib in prayer. While fard acts are established by definitive proofs, wajib acts are established by evidence that is slightly less certain, such as the Prophet's continuous practice. The text clarifies the rulings for taslim, qunūt, the takbīrs of the two 'Ids, the opening takbīr, and the rules for reciting aloud (jahr) or silently (isrār), including notable differences between Abū Ḥanīfa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Extract the first wajib ruling: taslim
Find the statement that taslim is not fard but wajib. Note the proof: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (without 'alaykum) and the Prophet's constant practice.
The text says 'ولم يكن فرضاً' (it was not fard) and then 'ويتجه الوجوب بالمواظبة عليه' (obligation is directed by constant practice).
2
Analyze the qunut ruling and the ikhtilaf
Identify that according to Abu Hanifa, qunut in witr is wajib, and the takbir of qunut is also wajib. Contrast with the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who consider witr itself as sunnah.
The text says 'عند أبي حنيفة' and 'وعندهما هو كأوتر سنة' (according to them it is like witr, i.e., sunnah).
3
Examine the takbirs of 'Id and the opening takbir
Understand that each additional takbira in 'Id prayer is wajib; omitting it requires sajdah sahw. Also, the opening takbir must be 'Allahu Akbar' due to constant practice, though there is a dispute on using other words.
The text says 'وكل تكبيرة منها واجبة يجب بتركها سجود السهو' (each takbira is wajib; leaving it requires sajdah sahw).
4
Map the jahr and israr rules
List which prayers require the imam to recite aloud (jahr): Fajr, first two of Maghrib and Isha, Jumu'ah, 'Id, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan. List which require silent recitation (israr): Zuhr, Asr, third/fourth rak'ahs, and daytime nafl. Note the dispute on whether jahr/israr are wajib or sunnah.
The text says 'ويجب جهر الإمام' and 'ويجب الإسرار' but later mentions a view that they are sunnah.
5
Relate to the overall principle of muwāẓabah
Synthesize that the common thread across these rulings is that the Prophet's continuous practice (muwāẓabah) raises an act to the level of wajib. This principle distinguishes Hanafi fiqh and explains why sajdah sahw is required for omission.
The text repeatedly uses 'للمواظبة' (due to constant practice) as the proof.

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi details multiple wajib acts in prayer according to the Hanafi school, with proofs and intra-school differences. The text begins by stating that taslim (saying 'al-Salamu 'alaykum') is not fard (obligatory at the level of Quranic command) but becomes wajib due to the Prophet's constant practice. Proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet did not mention it in teaching prayer. Then it discusses qunut in witr: according to Abu Hanifa, reciting qunut is wajib, and the takbir of qunut is also wajib, while the two companions consider witr itself as sunnah. Next, it covers the takbirs of the two 'Ids: each takbira is wajib, and omitting one requires sajdah sahw. The wording of the opening takbir must be 'Allahu Akbar' due to constant practice; there is a difference of opinion on whether starting with other words is makruh. The takbir of ruku' in the second rak'ah of 'Id is wajib because it is connected to the additional takbirs. Then the text outlines when the imam must recite aloud (jahr): in Fajr, first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha (even if makeup), Jumu'ah, 'Ids, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan. Silent recitation (israr) is wajib in Zuhr, Asr, the third/fourth rak'ahs of Maghrib/Isha, and daytime nafl. The commentary notes that if the imam omits jahr in Jumu'ah and 'Ids, he does not perform sajdah sahw to avoid fitna, and some say jahr and israr are sunnah, not wajib. The passage ends with the origin of jahr and israr: the Prophet initially recited aloud, but when the polytheists abused him and the Quran, Allah revealed the verse to neither recite too loudly nor too softly, leading to the current rules.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunūt): A specific supplication recited in the third rak'ah of Witr prayer; by extension, any supplication recited in that position.
تكبيرات العيدين (takbīrāt al-ʿīdayn): The additional takbirs (saying 'Allahu Akbar') recited in the 'Id prayer: three in each rak'ah before recitation in the first rak'ah and after recitation in the second.
جهر (jahr): Reciting audibly enough for others (at least one person) to hear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the basis for considering taslim (saying 'al-Salamu 'alaykum') as wajib rather than fard?
A) A Quranic verse explicitly commands it.
B) The Prophet's continuous practice (muwāẓabah) on it.
C) Consensus (ijma) of the Companions.
D) Analogy with the opening takbir.

Key Takeaway
Many prayer acts are wajib not because of an explicit command but due to the Prophet's constant practice (muwāẓabah); omitting them requires sajdah sahw, not repetition of the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Obligation of Loud and Quiet Recitation in Salah
Explains obligation and details of loud/quiet recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on jahr and israr in the daily prayers, identify the Quranic evidence, and explain the basis for the Maliki disagreement at Arafah.

Core Idea
Loud and quiet recitation are wajib based on the Prophet's practice and the verse 'seek a middle path.'

This lesson covers the obligation of loud (jahr) and quiet (israr) recitation in the five daily prayers, based on the continuous practice of the Prophet and the guidance of Surah al-Isra 17:110. We will also examine the rationale for the rule and a notable inter-madhhab difference with Imam Malik regarding prayers combined at Arafah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayers requiring jahr and israr
From the text, list the prayers where the imam must recite loudly (Fajr, first two of Maghrib/Isha, Friday, Eid, Tarawih, Witr in Ramadan) and those where he must recite quietly (Zuhr, Asr, later rak'ahs of Maghrib/Isha, daytime nafl).
Note that the ruling applies to the imam; the munfarid has a separate rule.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The text cites Quran 17:110 and the Prophet's interpretation: being loud at night and quiet by day.
The verse commands moderation, and the Prophet's practice provides the specific application.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The verse does not specify which prayers; the Prophet's sunnah clarifies. The Hanafi school sees this as establishing wujub because the Prophet consistently followed this pattern.
Some scholars consider it sunnah, but the dominant Hanafi view is wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Imam Malik at Arafah
Imam Malik holds that both Zuhr and Asr are recited loudly when combined at Arafah. The Hanafi response is that the combination does not change the nature of the prayers; quiet remains wajib.
The Prophet's practice at Arafah was quiet, as mentioned in the text.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi because it is based on the specific sunnah and the general principle that daytime prayers are quiet.
The Maliki view is respected as a legitimate ikhtilaf.

The Book of Salah. (With the recitation of) the two rak'ahs of Fajr and the recitation of the first two of the two evening prayers (Maghrib and Isha) even if makeup, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did so. And it is obligatory to recite loudly in the Friday prayer, the two Eid prayers, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan, upon the imam, due to continuity, and loudness means making others hear. And it is obligatory to recite quietly (which is making oneself hear, according to the correct view, as previously mentioned) in all rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr, even if combined at Arafah, and quietly in the later parts of the two evening prayers: the third of Maghrib and the fourth of Isha, and quietly in the supererogatory prayers of the day, due to continuity. From: The highest of loudness: Hamawi from al-Khazanah said: It is preferable not to exert oneself in loudness but to the extent of ability, because making some of the people hear suffices. (Bahr, Nahr) And it is recommended to be loud according to the congregation; if he exceeds the need of the congregation, he has done wrong, just as if a praying person is loud in dhikr. (Qahistani from Kashf al-Usul) And this is more appropriate than what is in al-Zahidi from Abu Ja'far: that whenever the imam or individual increases in loudness in a loud prayer, it is better, as long as he does not exert himself or harm others, even if he exceeds the need of the follower. His saying: (The first two of the two evening prayers) with fatha on the first ya' and kasra on the second for grammatical liberty, and the noon is dropped due to idafah. The second is called 'first' considering that they are a pair, and 'evening' is dominant over Maghrib because the principle is to give precedence to the more frequent. His saying: (In the Friday prayer and the two Eids) but if he omits it in them, he does not perform sajdah al-sahw, because it is dropped in Friday and the Eids to avoid fitnah. And it is said: i.e. loudness and quietness are sunnah, so sajdah al-sahw is not required by omitting them, because they are not the objective; the objective is recitation. (Zaylai) And what is in al-Qahistani from al-Qadi can be derived from this saying, that the imam has a choice in loudness beyond the obligatory prayers, even witr or Eid, but loudness is better, and it is stated in al-Hidayah that he has a choice in the supererogatory of the night, analogizing to the obligatory for the individual (end). And it is possible that it is a detailed statement. His saying: (And Witr in Ramadan, whether he performs it before Tarawih or after, even if he omits them, as in al-Durr from al-Anhar, and it is restricted to Ramadan because praying it in congregation outside of it is a reprehensible innovation (makruh), as in al-Halabi (Majma'), and loudness is not required for an innovation). His saying: (And quietness is obligatory. They said: It does not harm if some words are heard occasionally, due to the hadith of Abu Qatadah in the two Sahihs, that the Prophet used to recite al-Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs and would sometimes let us hear a verse. And because a little loudness or quietness cannot be avoided, especially at the beginnings of breaths. (al-Fath) And in the later parts of al-Halabi from Kifayat al-Sha'bi: He recites quietly unless there is an excuse, such as someone talking or being overcome by sleep, so he raises his voice to ward off sleep and speech (end). And in al-Qahistani: If he is loud to clarify a word, there is nothing upon him (end). His saying: (even if combined at Arafah) He pointed to the disagreement of Imam Malik (may Allah be pleased with him and with them all), for he says to recite loudly in both. And if the author had said 'even if the two combined at Arafah' it would be clearer. And the basis of loudness and quietness is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to recite loudly in all prayers in the beginning, and the polytheists would harm him and tell their followers: When you hear him recite, raise your voices with poetry and rhymes, and counter him with idle talk until you overcome him. So he would fall silent, and they would revile the One who sent down the Quran and the one to whom it was sent down. Then Allah revealed: {And do not recite loudly in your prayer nor quietly} [al-Isra: 110], meaning: do not be loud in all your prayer nor completely quiet, but seek a middle path: be loud in the night prayer and quiet in the day prayer. So after that, he would recite quietly in Zuhr and Asr because they were prepared to harm him in those, and loudly in Maghrib because they were busy eating, and in Isha and Fajr because they were sleeping, and in Friday and the two Eids because he established them in Madinah, and the disbelievers had no power. And his saying 'and in Fajr because they were sleeping' – the reason for Fajr is clear, and for Isha that the sunnah is to delay it until a third of the night. This is apparent in winter; in other seasons, the excuse for it is like Maghrib, as it appears. His saying: (The individual praying an obligatory prayer has a choice in what the imam recites loudly in) – if he wishes, he recites loudly because he is his own imam, but he should not exaggerate in loudness like the imam because he does not make others hear. His loudness in this way is better so that the performance resembles the congregation. And apparently, even if it is a makeup during the day, as in al-Kafi and others. But al-Hidayah chose that he must recite quietly due to lack of congregation and time, and this was discussed in Ghayat al-Bayan. His saying: (And in what he makes up, etc.) is conjoined to his saying 'in what the imam recites loudly in', and there is an indication that he is an individual in that respect, and it is so because he is an individual in what he makes up. They said: He makes up the beginning of his prayer in sayings and the end in actions. His saying: (in Friday and the two Eids, and likewise in what was preceded in other loud prayers). His saying: (like one who prays supererogatory at night) and loudness is better as long as he does not disturb a sleeping person, and similar to a sick person or one studying knowledge. This is said by al-Sayyid, quoting from his father's handwriting. His saying: (And he does not wake the half-asleep; the half-asleep is the one sleeping). His saying: (If he omits the surah in one rak'ah of the first two of Maghrib, etc.) i.e. intentionally or forgetfully, as in al-Nahr. And the apparent meaning is that if he omits it in both rak'ahs, he makes up a surah for only one of them because there is no place to make up the second. Know that if he did not recite anything in the first pair, he recites al-Fatihah and a surah in the second pair, reciting them loudly according to their statement, and he performs sajdah al-sahw. This is in al-Khaniyya. His saying: (Obligatorily according to the most correct view) – this is what is in al-Tabyin and the commentaries of al-Hidayah, but al-Asl stated it as recommended and relied upon in al-Fath and al-Burhan. Then, on the view of obligation, it is said that al-Fatihah is also obligatory, and it is said not. In al-Bahr and al-Nahr: The preference is for non-obligation, as is the principle. His saying: (Loudly with both according to the most correct view) – this was chosen by the author of al-Hidayah, because reciting both loudly changes the quality of al-Fatihah from quiet (which is nafl) and reciting both quietly changes the quality of the surah from loud (which is wajib), and changing the quality of nafl is lighter than changing the quality of wajib. And Ibn Sama'ah narrated from the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) to recite the surah loudly only, and this is the choice of Fakhr al-Islam, who said it is correct. Shaykh al-Islam made it the apparent answer, and al-Khaniyya affirmed it, and al-Tamartashi authenticated it. And this does not necessitate...
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a super-commentary expanding on the rulings of jahr (loud recitation) and israr (quiet recitation) in salah. It begins by stating that reciting loudly in the first two rak'ahs of Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha, even in makeup prayers, is based on the Prophet's practice. The obligation of jahr is explicitly placed on the imam for Friday, Eid, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan, as these are congregational prayers where the imam must make others hear. For quiet recitation (israr), it is obligatory in Zuhr, Asr, the later rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, and in daytime nafl prayers, following the Prophet's consistent practice. The commentary then clarifies that the imam should not strain himself in jahr; it suffices that some of the congregation can hear. Exceeding the need is blameworthy. A subtle point: some scholars held that jahr and israr are only sunnah, not wajib, so omission does not require sajdah al-sahw. However, the dominant view is that they are wajib. The passage then delves into the disagreement with Imam Malik regarding jahr in combined prayers at Arafah – the Hanafi position is israr. The historical context is given: initially the Prophet recited aloud in all prayers, but the polytheists disturbed him, so Allah revealed the verse (17:110) commanding moderation. After that, the Prophet adopted the pattern of israr in daytime prayers and jahr in nighttime ones. The passage then addresses the individual praying alone (munfarid): he has a choice in prayers where jahr is normally required, because he is his own imam. However, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: according to al-Hidayah, he must recite quietly if making up a prayer during the day, due to the absence of congregation and the time. The final section discusses a scenario where a person omits the surah in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib or Isha. According to the most correct view, he must recite it in the later rak'ahs with jahr, even if it means changing the quiet recitation of Fatihah. But there is disagreement: some say he recites only the surah loudly, not the Fatihah, to minimize change. The commentary weighs the positions, noting that changing the quality of a nafl (quiet Fatihah) is lighter than changing a wajib (loud surah). Fiqh lesson: This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of balancing textual evidence (hadith and verse), the principle of istihsan (preferring the lighter change), and the respect for the established patterns of the Prophet's prayer. The key takeaway is that jahr and israr are determined by the nature of the prayer and the circumstances, with specific rulings for the imam, the individual, and the one making up prayers.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation that makes others hear; required in specific prayers for the imam.
الإسرار (al-israr): Quiet recitation sufficient to hear oneself; obligatory in Zuhr, Asr, and later rak'ahs.
المنفرد (al-munfarid): One praying alone, not in congregation; has choice in jahr/israr for obligatory prayers normally recited loudly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which situation does the Hanafi school require quiet recitation even though the prayer is combined at Arafah?
A) Both prayers loudly
B) Both prayers quietly
C) Zuhr quietly, Asr loudly
D) Zuhr loudly, Asr quietly

Key Takeaway
Jahr and israr are wajib for the imam in specified prayers, with the Quranic verse and Prophetic practice as the basis; the Maliki ikhtilaf at Arafah does not affect Hanafi practice.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Individual (Munfarid) and Omission of Surah
Discusses munfarid choice and surah omission compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the choice given to the individual praying alone regarding jahr, and state the correct procedure when a surah is omitted in the first two rak'ahs.

Core Idea
The individual has a choice to recite loudly or quietly in jahr prayers, but must make up an omitted surah with jahr in the later rak'ahs.

This lesson addresses two nuanced cases: the person praying alone (munfarid) and the scenario where the surah is omitted in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib or Isha. In the Hanafi school, the munfarid has flexibility, while the omission of the surah triggers a specific compensation that involves loud recitation even in quiet portions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the rule for the munfarid
The text states that the munfarid has a choice to recite loudly or quietly in prayers where the imam normally recites loudly (e.g., Fajr). He is like his own imam.
This applies to obligatory prayers normally recited loudly; quiet prayers remain quiet even for the munfarid.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on qada
Al-Hidayah says that in qada during the day, the munfarid must recite quietly. Other authorities allow choice.
This difference affects practice; the mufta bihi is that choice is acceptable but quiet is better.
3
Study the case of omitting surah
If the surah is omitted in the first two rak'ahs, the person must recite it in the later rak'ahs, and according to the most correct view, recite both Fatihah and surah loudly.
This changes the normal quiet recitation of Fatihah to loud.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf on which parts are loud
Some scholars (Fakhr al-Islam, al-Tamartashi) say only the surah should be recited loudly, not Fatihah, to minimize change.
The dominant view is that both are loud, but the preferred view is to recite only the surah loudly.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The view of Fakhr al-Islam (loud with surah only) is considered the most sound and is the preferred fatwa.
The student should follow this view to avoid unnecessary change.

الجهر، وهي واجبة وتغيير صفة النفل أخف من تغيير صفة الواجب، وروى ابن سماعة عن الشيخين الجهر بالسورة فقط، وهو اختيار فخر الإسلام قال وهو الصواب، وجعله شيخ الإسلام الظاهر من الجواب وبه جزم في الخانية، The Book of Salah. (With the recitation of) the two rak'ahs of Fajr and the recitation of the first two of the two evening prayers (Maghrib and Isha) even if makeup, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did so. And it is obligatory to recite loudly in the Friday prayer, the two Eid prayers, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan, upon the imam, due to continuity, and loudness means making others hear. And it is obligatory to recite quietly (which is making oneself hear, according to the correct view, as previously mentioned) in all rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr, even if combined at Arafah, and quietly in the later parts of the two evening prayers: the third of Maghrib and the fourth of Isha, and quietly in the supererogatory prayers of the day, due to continuity. From: The highest of loudness: Hamawi from al-Khazanah said: It is preferable not to exert oneself in loudness but to the extent of ability, because making some of the people hear suffices. (Bahr, Nahr) And it is recommended to be loud according to the congregation; if he exceeds the need of the congregation, he has done wrong, just as if a praying person is loud in dhikr. (Qahistani from Kashf al-Usul) And this is more appropriate than what is in al-Zahidi from Abu Ja'far: that whenever the imam or individual increases in loudness in a loud prayer, it is better, as long as he does not exert himself or harm others, even if he exceeds the need of the follower. His saying: (The first two of the two evening prayers) with fatha on the first ya' and kasra on the second for grammatical liberty, and the noon is dropped due to idafah. The second is called 'first' considering that they are a pair, and 'evening' is dominant over Maghrib because the principle is to give precedence to the more frequent. His saying: (In the Friday prayer and the two Eids) but if he omits it in them, he does not perform sajdah al-sahw, because it is dropped in Friday and the Eids to avoid fitnah. And it is said: i.e. loudness and quietness are sunnah, so sajdah al-sahw is not required by omitting them, because they are not the objective; the objective is recitation. (Zaylai) And what is in al-Qahistani from al-Qadi can be derived from this saying, that the imam has a choice in loudness beyond the obligatory prayers, even witr or Eid, but loudness is better, and it is stated in al-Hidayah that he has a choice in the supererogatory of the night, analogizing to the obligatory for the individual (end). And it is possible that it is a detailed statement. His saying: (And Witr in Ramadan, whether he performs it before Tarawih or after, even if he omits them, as in al-Durr from al-Anhar, and it is restricted to Ramadan because praying it in congregation outside of it is a reprehensible innovation (makruh), as in al-Halabi (Majma'), and loudness is not required for an innovation). His saying: (And quietness is obligatory. They said: It does not harm if some words are heard occasionally, due to the hadith of Abu Qatadah in the two Sahihs, that the Prophet used to recite al-Fatihah in the last two rak'ahs and would sometimes let us hear a verse. And because a little loudness or quietness cannot be avoided, especially at the beginnings of breaths. (al-Fath) And in the later parts of al-Halabi from Kifayat al-Sha'bi: He recites quietly unless there is an excuse, such as someone talking or being overcome by sleep, so he raises his voice to ward off sleep and speech (end). And in al-Qahistani: If he is loud to clarify a word, there is nothing upon him (end). His saying: (even if combined at Arafah) He pointed to the disagreement of Imam Malik (may Allah be pleased with him and with them all), for he says to recite loudly in both. And if the author had said 'even if the two combined at Arafah' it would be clearer. And the basis of loudness and quietness is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to recite loudly in all prayers in the beginning, and the polytheists would harm him and tell their followers: When you hear him recite, raise your voices with poetry and rhymes, and counter him with idle talk until you overcome him. So he would fall silent, and they would revile the One who sent down the Quran and the one to whom it was sent down. Then Allah revealed: {And do not recite loudly in your prayer nor quietly} [al-Isra: 110], meaning: do not be loud in all your prayer nor completely quiet, but seek a middle path: be loud in the night prayer and quiet in the day prayer. So after that, he would recite quietly in Zuhr and Asr because they were prepared to harm him in those, and loudly in Maghrib because they were busy eating, and in Isha and Fajr because they were sleeping, and in Friday and the two Eids because he established them in Madinah, and the disbelievers had no power. And his saying 'and in Fajr because they were sleeping' – the reason for Fajr is clear, and for Isha that the sunnah is to delay it until a third of the night. This is apparent in winter; in other seasons, the excuse for it is like Maghrib, as it appears. His saying: (The individual praying an obligatory prayer has a choice in what the imam recites loudly in) – if he wishes, he recites loudly because he is his own imam, but he should not exaggerate in loudness like the imam because he does not make others hear. His loudness in this way is better so that the performance resembles the congregation. And apparently, even if it is a makeup during the day, as in al-Kafi and others. But al-Hidayah chose that he must recite quietly due to lack of congregation and time, and this was discussed in Ghayat al-Bayan. His saying: (And in what he makes up, etc.) is conjoined to his saying 'in what the imam recites loudly in', and there is an indication that he is an individual in that respect, and it is so because he is an individual in what he makes up. They said: He makes up the beginning of his prayer in sayings and the end in actions. His saying: (in Friday and the two Eids, and likewise in what was preceded in other loud prayers). His saying: (like one who prays supererogatory at night) and loudness is better as long as he does not disturb a sleeping person, and similar to a sick person or one studying knowledge. This is said by al-Sayyid, quoting from his father's handwriting. His saying: (And he does not wake the half-asleep; the half-asleep is the one sleeping). His saying: (If he omits the surah in one rak'ah of the first two of Maghrib, etc.) i.e. intentionally or forgetfully, as in al-Nahr. And the apparent meaning is that if he omits it in both rak'ahs, he makes up a surah for only one of them because there is no place to make up the second. Know that if he did not recite anything in the first pair, he recites al-Fatihah and a surah in the second pair, reciting them loudly according to their statement, and he performs sajdah al-sahw. This is in al-Khaniyya. His saying: (Obligatorily according to the most correct view) – this is what is in al-Tabyin and the commentaries of al-Hidayah, but al-Asl stated it as recommended and relied upon in al-Fath and al-Burhan. Then, on the view of obligation, it is said that al-Fatihah is also obligatory, and it is said not. In al-Bahr and al-Nahr: The preference is for non-obligation, as is the principle. His saying: (Loudly with both according to the most correct view) – this was chosen by the author of al-Hidayah, because reciting both loudly changes the quality of al-Fatihah from quiet (which is nafl) and reciting both quietly changes the quality of the surah from loud (which is wajib), and changing the quality of nafl is lighter than changing the quality of wajib. And Ibn Sama'ah narrated from the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) to recite the surah loudly only, and this is the choice of Fakhr al-Islam, who said it is correct. Shaykh al-Islam made it the apparent answer, and al-Khaniyya affirmed it, and al-Tamartashi authenticated it. And this does not necessitate...
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a super-commentary expanding on the rulings of jahr (loud recitation) and israr (quiet recitation) in salah. It begins by stating that reciting loudly in the first two rak'ahs of Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha, even in makeup prayers, is based on the Prophet's practice. The obligation of jahr is explicitly placed on the imam for Friday, Eid, Tarawih, and Witr in Ramadan, as these are congregational prayers where the imam must make others hear. For quiet recitation (israr), it is obligatory in Zuhr, Asr, the later rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, and in daytime nafl prayers, following the Prophet's consistent practice. The commentary then clarifies that the imam should not strain himself in jahr; it suffices that some of the congregation can hear. Exceeding the need is blameworthy. A subtle point: some scholars held that jahr and israr are only sunnah, not wajib, so omission does not require sajdah al-sahw. However, the dominant view is that they are wajib. The passage then delves into the disagreement with Imam Malik regarding jahr in combined prayers at Arafah – the Hanafi position is israr. The historical context is given: initially the Prophet recited aloud in all prayers, but the polytheists disturbed him, so Allah revealed the verse (17:110) commanding moderation. After that, the Prophet adopted the pattern of israr in daytime prayers and jahr in nighttime ones. The passage then addresses the individual praying alone (munfarid): he has a choice in prayers where jahr is normally required, because he is his own imam. However, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: according to al-Hidayah, he must recite quietly if making up a prayer during the day, due to the absence of congregation and the time. The final section discusses a scenario where a person omits the surah in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib or Isha. According to the most correct view, he must recite it in the later rak'ahs with jahr, even if it means changing the quiet recitation of Fatihah. But there is disagreement: some say he recites only the surah loudly, not the Fatihah, to minimize change. The commentary weighs the positions, noting that changing the quality of a nafl (quiet Fatihah) is lighter than changing a wajib (loud surah). Fiqh lesson: This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of balancing textual evidence (hadith and verse), the principle of istihsan (preferring the lighter change), and the respect for the established patterns of the Prophet's prayer. The key takeaway is that jahr and israr are determined by the nature of the prayer and the circumstances, with specific rulings for the imam, the individual, and the one making up prayers.

Key Terms
المنفرد (al-munfarid): One praying alone, not in congregation; has choice in jahr/israr for obligatory prayers normally recited loudly.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory prayer.
ترك السورة (tark al-surah): Omission of the additional surah after Fatihah in the first two rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an imam in Maghrib forgets the surah in the first rak'ah, what must he do in the third rak'ah according to the most correct Hanafi view?
A) Recite Fatihah quietly
B) Recite Fatihah and surah loudly
C) Recite surah only loudly
D) Recite Fatihah loudly and surah quietly

Key Takeaway
The munfarid has a choice in jahr prayers, but when making up an omitted surah, loud recitation of the surah is required; the dominant view is to recite only the surah loudly to minimize change.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Ruling for the Munfarid on Loud Recitation (Jahr)
Explains the choice and recommendation for the munfarid regarding jahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a munfarid regarding jahr and identify the recommended practice.

Core Idea
The munfarid has a choice to recite loudly or silently; the optimal is minimal jahr to avoid disturbing sleepers.

When a person prays a fard prayer alone (munfarid) in a prayer where the imam normally recites loudly (jahr), he is given a choice. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies that he may recite loudly or silently, and it is recommended to keep the volume low so as not to disturb others, especially when making up missed prayers or performing voluntary night prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is recitation of the munfarid in a prayer where the imam normally recites loudly. The ruling is mubah (permissible) with a choice (mukhayyar).
2
Understand the scope
The choice applies to fard prayers made up (qada), Friday and Eid prayers, and voluntary night prayers (tahajjud).
3
Note the recommended practice
The munfarid is advised to use the minimum loudness sufficient for himself, following the Prophetic practice in tahajjud.
The reason is to avoid disturbing sleepers or others nearby.
4
Recognize the rationale
The recommendation to minimize volume is based on the hadith that the Prophet's recitation in tahajjud would not wake a deeply sleeping person but would alert one who is awake.
5
Compare with other schools
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require jahr for the munfarid; the Hanafi school grants a choice, making it easier in practice.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (valid difference of opinion).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على ذلك (والمنفرد) بفرض (مخير فيما يجهر) الإمام فيه وقد بيناه وفيما يقضيه مما سبق به في الجمعة والعيدين كمتنفل بالليل) فإنه مخير ويكتفي بأدنى الجهر فلا يضر نائماً لأنه جهر في التهجد بالليل وكان يؤنس اليقظان ولا يوقظ الوسنان
On that [basis] (the individual praying a fard prayer) (has a choice in what the imam recites loudly) and we have explained it, and regarding what he makes up from what preceded in Friday and the two Eids, like a voluntary night prayer, he has a choice and is content with the minimum of loudness, so it does not harm a sleeper because loudness in tahajjud at night used to wake the awake and not disturb the sleepy.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling for a person praying a fard prayer alone (munfarid) in a prayer where the imam normally recites loudly (jahr). The author explains that such a person has a choice to recite loudly or silently, but he is sufficient with the minimum loudness so as not to disturb others, especially sleepers. This is analogous to the voluntary night prayer (tahajjud) where the Prophet ﷺ would recite with moderate loudness. The passage also notes that this applies to making up missed prayers (qada) that were originally loud, and to Friday and Eid prayers. The key point is that the munfarid is like his own imam, so he may choose, but it is recommended to not exaggerate the loudness.

Key Terms
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying the prayer alone, not as part of a congregation.
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation in prayer, typically in Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, and Eid prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person praying a fard prayer alone in a loud prayer regarding recitation?
A) He must recite loudly.
B) He has a choice to recite loudly or silently.
C) He must recite silently.
D) He must recite moderately loud.

Key Takeaway
The munfarid is given a choice to recite loudly or silently, and is advised to keep the volume low to avoid disturbance.

Making Up Missed Surah in Loud Rak'ahs: Hanafi Dispute
Detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on making up a missed surah in the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, identify the proofs for each view, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Missed surah in first two rak'ahs: must it be made up loudly with Fatiha? Hanafis differ.

This lesson examines a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about what to do if one omits the surah (and possibly Fatiha) in the first two loud rak'ahs of Maghrib or Isha. The core ruling requires reciting it in the third of Maghrib or last two of Isha, but scholars disagree whether Fatiha must also be recited, whether it should be loud, and whether the obligation is wajib or mustahabb. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi jurists balance textual evidence, analogy, and practical compensation.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Identify the act (omission of surah in first two rak'ahs of Maghrib/Isha) and the claimed remedy: recite the surah in the next suitable rak'ah(s) with Fatiha, loudly, as an obligation according to the most correct view.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note three points of disagreement: (1) Is the qada wajib or mustahabb? (2) Must Fatiha also be recited? (3) Should it be loud or silent? Who holds which view (Imam Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, Imam Abu Hanifa)?
Imam Muhammad considered it mustahabb; Abu Yusuf denied qada altogether.
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the dalil for the majority: the principle that changing the attribute of a nafl (Fatiha's silence) is easier than changing the attribute of a wajib (surah's loudness). Then consider the counter-arguments: Abu Yusuf argued no evidence for qada of a wajib, and Muhammad preferred jahr for surah only.
Al-Marghinani used the 'easier change' reasoning.
4
Determine the tarjih
The mufta bihi position: according to Fakhr al-Islam and al-Tamartashi, the surah is recited loudly without Fatiha. This is the relied-upon view.
The text also mentions that if Fatiha was missed, it is not repeated; sajda al-sahw suffices.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a concrete case: someone omitted both surah and Fatiha in the first rak'ah of Maghrib. Use the mufta bihi ruling to determine what he must do.
He recites the surah loudly in the third rak'ah, but not Fatiha, and performs sajda al-sahw.

His statement: (If he omits the surah in) one rak'ah of the first two of Maghrib or all of the first two of Isha, (he recites it, i.e. the surah, as an obligation according to the most correct view) (in the last two of Isha and the third of Maghrib) (along with Fatiha, loudly according to the most correct view, and he gives precedence to the last two) of that, Isha: 'Neither recite loudly nor silently but seek a middle way' [al-Isra' 17:110] meaning do not recite your prayer entirely loudly nor entirely silently, but seek a middle way by reciting night prayers loudly and day prayers silently... (continues with detailed explanation of various opinions and rulings)
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage provides an in-depth treatment of the Hanafi ruling on making up missed recitation (surah and fatiha) in the loud rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha. The core ruling: if one omits the surah (or both surah and fatiha) in the first two rak'ahs, he must recite it in the third of Maghrib or the last two of Isha, along with Fatiha, and do so loudly. There is significant intra-Hanafi disagreement: some scholars (e.g., al-Marghinani) consider it wajib, while Imam Muhammad considered it mustahabb (recommended). Regarding loudness, there is disagreement whether both Fatiha and surah should be recited loudly or only the surah. The text presents the reasoning that since the surah is originally wajib to be loud, and Fatiha in that position is normally silent, changing Fatiha to loud is less problematic than changing surah to silent. Abu Yusuf's opinion is that the surah is not remade at all because a wajib cannot be made up without textual evidence. The commentary concludes with a preference for reciting the surah loudly without Fatiha, as chosen by Fakhr al-Islam. The passage also discusses the case of missing Fatiha: it is not repeated in the last two rak'ahs; instead, one performs sajda al-sahw. Detailed sub-rulings are given regarding sequence of recitation and what to do if one remembers late.

Key Terms
سورة (surah): The additional chapter recited after al-Fatiha in prayer.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory element of the prayer, here referring to reciting the surah in a later rak'ah.
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation; in this context, both Fatiha and surah are recited loudly when making up.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, what should one do if he omits the surah in the first rak'ah of Maghrib?
A) Repeat the entire prayer.
B) Recite the surah in the third rak'ah loudly, without Fatiha, and perform sajda al-sahw.
C) Recite both Fatiha and surah in the third rak'ah loudly.
D) Do nothing; the prayer is valid without compensation.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi view for making up a missed surah in the loud rak'ahs is to recite it loudly in the next suitable rak'ah without repeating Fatiha, and to perform sajda al-sahw.
