What Constitutes Catching the Virtue of the Opening Takbir?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on threshold for catching fadl al-tahrimah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the different Hanafi opinions on idrak fadl al-tahrimah and identify the chosen and correct views.

Core Idea
Catching the virtue of the opening takbir is not a single ruling; it is a subject of ikhtilaf with multiple positions.

When you join the imam late, do you still earn the full virtue of the opening takbir? The Hanafi school has several views on how much of the prayer you must catch. This passage from the Hashiya al-Tahtawi lists the range of opinions and identifies which are preferred.

Guided Path
1
List the opinions
Read the passage and extract all five opinions on what constitutes catching the virtue of the opening takbir.
The opinions range from catching up to thana' to catching the first rak'ah.
2
Identify the sources
Note which opinion is attributed to which Hanafi text (e.g., al-Haqa'iq, al-Nazm, al-Khulasa, al-Mudmarat).
This helps understand the weight of each opinion.
3
Determine the tarjih
The passage indicates that the 'chosen view' is catching the entire Fatihah, and the 'correct view' is catching the first rak'ah. Identify which is mufta bihi.
These two views are given preference by later scholars.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a latecomer joining at different points and determine which opinion would grant him the virtue.
The practical consequence differs depending on the opinion followed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف في إدراك فضل التحريمة على قولهما فقيل: إلى الثناء كما في الحقائق، وقيل: إلى نصف الفاتحة كما في النظم، وقيل في الفاتحة كلها، وهو المختار كما في الخلاصة، وقيل: إلى الركعة الأولى، وهو الصحيح كما في المضمرات، وقيل: بالتأسف على فوت التكبيرة مع الإمام ذكره القهستاني.

And it is said: until half of al-Fatihah as in al-Nazm. And it is said: in the entire al-Fatihah, and that is the chosen view as in al-Khulasa. And it is said: until the first rak'ah, and that is the correct view as in al-Mudmarat. And it is said: regret for missing the takbir with the imam, mentioned by al-Qahistani.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute about what constitutes catching the virtue (fadl) of the opening takbir when joining the imam late. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), there are several opinions: some say catching up to the thana' (glorification), some up to half of Fatihah, some the whole Fatihah (the chosen view in Khulasa), some the first rak'ah (the correct view in Mudmarat), and some say one should regret missing the takbir with the imam. The author does not decisively favor one, but notes the chosen and correct views.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that begins the prayer.

Salam Similar to Takbir in Joining the Imam
Ruling that salam has same joining rule as takbir, with dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when the follower gives salam and explain the dispute within the school.

Core Idea
The follower gives salam with the imam on the most correct Hanafi narration; a minority view says after.

This lesson examines whether the follower’s final salam should be simultaneous with the imam or delayed. The Hanafi school has two narrations from Abu Hanifa. The most correct view equates salam with the opening takbir, so the follower joins the imam. The minority view distinguishes because takbir initiates worship while salam concludes it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (the follower's salam) and the hukm level. The passage states that on the most correct narration, the follower gives salam with the imam; this is sunnah.
The default ruling for following the imam in salam is sunnah, not fard.
2
Locate the two narrations from Abu Hanifa
Identify the two narrations: (1) No difference between salam and takbir – follower gives salam with imam. (2) Follower gives salam after imam. Understand which is considered 'asahh' (most correct).
The first narration is from the Zahir al-Riwayah; the second is a nawadir narration.
3
Examine the reasoning for the difference
The second narration distinguishes because takbir is entering worship (hastening recommended) while salam is exiting (hastening not recommended). Recognise that this is a 'illah (cause) for the differing ruling.
Even though the second narration has a logical basis, it is considered weaker than the first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسلام مثل التحريمة من حيث المقارنة على أصح الروايتين عن الإمام فلا فرق، وفي رواية عنه: يسلم بعده، وعليها فالفرق بينه وبين التحريمة عنده أن التكبير شروع في العبادة، فيستحب فيه المبادرة والسلام خروج عنها، فلا يستحب فيه كما في التبيين.
And the salam is like the takbir in terms of joining [the imam] according to the most correct of the two narrations from the Imam, so there is no difference. And in one narration from him: he gives salam after him, and upon this there is a difference between it and the takbir according to him, that the takbir is entering into worship, so it is recommended to hasten in it, and salam is exiting from it, so it is not recommended to hasten, as in al-Tabyin.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage addresses whether the salam should be performed simultaneously with the imam or after. On the most correct narration from Abu Hanifa, the ruling is the same as the takbir: the follower should perform it alongside the imam. However, another narration says the follower should give salam after the imam, because takbir initiates worship (so hastening is recommended) while salam concludes it (so hastening is not recommended). The text notes the difference and the preferred view.

Key Terms

التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir of the prayer.

Sunnah of Hand Placement: Under the Navel for Men
Ruling on hand placement with internal dispute on method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah of hand placement after takbir and identify the preferred method (tahleq) with its evidence.

Core Idea
Hand placement is sunnah muakkadah; men under navel with ring, women on chest for modesty.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses the sunnah of hand placement after the opening takbir. It presents the ruling, describes the method, and resolves an internal dispute about the precise technique. Understanding this clarifies a practical aspect of salah and highlights how Hanafi scholars weigh conflicting narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what the passage rules on and the hukm level. The act is placing the right hand on the left after takbir; the ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
Not fard or wajib – omission does not invalidate salah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited. The hadith of Ali (narrated by Abu Dawud, authenticated by Ibn Khuzaymah and Ibn Hibban) is the primary evidence.
The hadith describes the Prophet's action.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the dalil proves the ruling. The Prophet's action (placing right on left, making a ring) indicates the sunnah method.
The description 'placed his right hand on the back of his left hand, the wrist and forearm' supports the ring formation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the disagreement. Some mashayikh consider the ring method contrary to sunnah, while many prefer it.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Determine the mufta bihi. Al-Mufid and many mashayikh choose the ring method, citing multiple narrations.
Ibn Amir Haj adds support from Abu Dawud's hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن (وضع الرجل يده اليمنى على اليسرى تحت سرته لحديث علي رضي الله عنه أن السنة وضع اليمنى على الشمال تحت السرة (وصفة الوضع أن يجعل باطن كف اليمنى على ظاهر كف اليسرى محلقاً بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ لأنه لما ورد أنه وضع الكف على الكف، فاستحسن كثير من المشايخ تلك الصفة عملاً بالحديثين وقيل: إنه مخالف للسنة. قوله: (فاستحسن كثير من المشايخ) قال في المفيد: وهو المختار، وقال ابن أمير حاج وربما يشهد له ما رواه أبو داود وصححه ابن خزيمة وابن حبان، ثم وضع يده اليمنى على ظاهر كفه اليسرى، والرسغ والساعد اهـ. قوله: (فينبغي أن يفعل الخ) قال في الشرح: لأن تلك الصفة ليس فيها حقيقة كلا المرويين تماماً، بل صفة ثالثة فيها جمع لهما لا على وجه التمام لكل منهما اهـ، وقد علمت ما عن المفيد قوله: ويسن وضع المرأة يديها على صدرها من غير تحليق لأنه أستر لها.
And it is sunnah for a man to place his right hand on his left under his navel, due to the hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that the sunnah is to place the right on the left under the navel. The description of placement is to make the palm of the right hand on the back of the left hand, making a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist, because it is reported as placing palm on palm. So many mashayikh found this description good, acting on both hadiths. And it is said: it is contrary to the sunnah. His statement: 'So many mashayikh found it good' – he said in al-Mufid: it is the chosen view. Ibn Amir Haj said: it is perhaps supported by what Abu Dawud narrated and Ibn Khuzaymah and Ibn Hibban authenticated: 'Then he placed his right hand on the back of his left hand, the wrist and the forearm.' His statement: 'So one should do...' – he said in al-Sharh: because that description does not contain complete reality of either of the two transmitted descriptions, but is a third description combining them, not in a complete manner for each. And you have known what is from al-Mufid. His statement: 'And it is sunnah for a woman to place her hands on her chest without making a ring because it is more concealing for her.'
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the sunnah of hand placement after the opening takbir. The base ruling: men place right hand on left under navel. The preferred method according to many scholars is to make a ring with the little finger and thumb around the wrist, with the palm on the back of the left hand, as it combines two narrations. However, some consider this innovation. The author then mentions the view from al-Mufid that this is the chosen method. He notes a hadith from Abu Dawud supporting it. Another view from al-Sharh suggests using both methods alternately. For women, the sunnah is to place hands on the chest without interlocking, for greater modesty.

Key Terms
تحليق (tahleq): Making a ring by the little finger and thumb around the wrist.
أستر (astar): More concealing, modest; reason for women's different placement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that men should place their right hand on left under navel with a ring formation, and women on chest without ring, based on the sunnah of the Prophet.

The Sunnah of Ta'awwudh: It Applies to All Recitation
Ruling on ta'awwudh before recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'awwudh and explain why it applies to any Quranic recitation, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah for recitation, not just for al-Fatihah.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on saying 'A'udhu billah' before reciting in prayer. While many assume it is only for al-Fatihah, the Hanafi school teaches that it is a sunnah of all Quranic recitation. This distinction has practical implications for how we pray.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling
The passage states that ta'awwudh is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
2
Identify the scope
The text specifies 'wa law ata bi-ghayr al-fatihah' meaning even if reciting other than al-Fatihah, because it is sunnah of recitation in general.
Key phrase: 'sunnat al-qira'ah'
3
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school restricts ta'awwudh to before al-Fatihah only. The Hanafi view is broader.
4
Recognize the authority
The commentator al-Sayyid affirmed this view.

This view is supported by al-Sayyid in his commentary. The ta'awwudh is said softly in silent prayers, and it is not obligatory.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): Saying 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' before recitation.

Women's Specific Postures in Prayer
Listing specific sunnan for women's prayer postures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific sunnah postures for women in salah and distinguish them from men's postures based on the principle of modesty (sitr).

Core Idea
A woman's prayer postures prioritize modesty: hands on chest without interlocking, slight ruku, mutawarrik sitting, no leading men, and no loud recitation.

The Hanafi school prescribes distinct postures for women in salah, rooted in the principle of modesty (sitr). This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi enumerates these sunnan, highlighting how women differ from men in hand placement, ruku, sujud, sitting, and congregational rulings. Understanding these differences ensures proper practice and respect for the madhhab's tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying principle
Recognize that all women-specific postures are justified by the principle of extra concealment (sitr) to maintain modesty.
This principle recurs throughout the passage.
2
Categorize each ruling by prayer position
Group the rulings into standing (hand placement, takbir), bowing (ruku), prostrating (sujud), sitting (qa'dah), and congregational aspects.
This helps organize the list for memorization.
3
Note the distinction from men's practice
For each posture, explicitly state how a woman's action differs from a man's (e.g., hands on chest vs. below navel).
This reinforces the unique sunnah for women.
4
Recognize the juridical rank
All listed postures are sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommended acts), not obligatory. Omission does not invalidate the prayer.
Missing a sunnah reduces reward but the prayer remains valid.
5
Identify exceptional rulings
Note that women do not lead men, their congregation (imam standing in middle) is makruh, and isfar (delaying Fajr) is not recommended for them.
These are not postures but related rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد علمت ما عن المفيد قوله : ويسن وضع المرأة يديها على صدرها من غير تحليق لأنه أستر لها. المرأة تخالف الرجل في مسائل منها هذه ومنها أنها لا تخرج كفيها من كميها عند التكبير، وترفع يديها حذاء منكبيها، ولا تفرج أصابعها في الركوع، وتنحني في الركوع قليلاً بحيث تبلغ حد الركوع، فلا تزيد على ذلك لأنه أستر لها وتلزم مرفقيها بجنبيها فيه، وتلزق بطنها بفخذيها في السجود، وتجلس متوركة في كل قعود بأن تجلس على أليتها اليسرى وتخرج كلتا رجليها من الجانب الأيمن وتضع فخذيها على بعضهما، وتجعل الساق الأيمن على الساق الأيسر كما في مجمع الأنهر ولا تؤم الرجال، وتكره جماعتهن ويقف الإمام وسطهن ولا تجهر في موضع الجهر ولا يستحب في حقها الأسفار بالفجر والتتبع ينفي الحصر.
And you have known what is from al-Mufid: his statement: It is sunnah for a woman to place her hands on her chest without interlocking because it is more concealing for her. A woman differs from a man in matters: among them this, and among them that she does not take out her hands from her sleeves when saying takbir, and she raises her hands to the level of her shoulders, and she does not spread her fingers in ruku', and she bends slightly in ruku' such that she reaches the limit of ruku', so she does not exceed that because it is more concealing for her, and she keeps her elbows attached to her sides in it, and she sticks her belly to her thighs in sujud, and she sits mutawarrika in every sitting by sitting on her left buttock and bringing out both her legs from the right side, and placing her thighs on each other, and making the right shin on the left shin as in Majma' al-Anhur, and she does not lead men, and their congregation is disliked, and the imam stands in their middle, and she does not raise her voice in a place of jahr, and al-isfar with fajr is not recommended for her, and investigation precludes enumeration.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the hashya commentary expanding on the matn's ruling for women. It enumerates the specific sunnan postures for women in prayer, distinguishing them from men. The key principle is modesty (sitr). Women place hands on chest without interlocking, do not remove hands from sleeves during takbir, raise hands to shoulders, keep fingers together in ruku', bend only slightly in ruku', keep elbows to sides, stick belly to thighs in sujud, sit mutawarrika (on left buttock with legs out to the right), do not lead men in prayer, and their congregation is makruh. The imam stands in the middle of the row for women. Also, they do not recite aloud in jahr prayers, and it is not recommended for them to pray fajr early (al-isfar). These rulings are specific to the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
متوركة (mutawarrikah): A sitting posture where a woman sits on her left buttock with both legs brought out to the right side.
أسفار (isfar): Delaying the fajr prayer until the sky is clearly light, which is recommended for men but not for women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) On her chest, with fingers interlocked
B) On her chest, without interlocking (not tahlil)
C) Below the navel, like men
D) On her shoulders

Key Takeaway
Women's prayer postures in the Hanafi school are distinguished from men's, all sunnah mu'akkadah, driven by the principle of modesty (sitr).

Sunnah of Thana' and Its Rulings
Expounding the sunnah of thana', its wording, and rulings for followers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on thana', including its timing, wording, and the follower's obligation, and apply the rules to congregational prayer scenarios.

Core Idea
Thana' is sunnah after takbir; omit 'wa jalla thana'uka' except in janazah.

In this lesson, we explore the opening supplication (thana') in prayer. The text provides the proof from the Prophet's practice, addresses a disputed phrase, clarifies the correct timing, and specifies the follower's role. Understanding these details ensures your prayer aligns with the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is thana'? What is its hukm (sunnah) according to the Hanafi school? Locate the explicit statement in the passage.
The text begins by citing the hadith and then discusses the ruling.
2
Examine the disputed phrase 'wa jalla thana'uka'
Why do Hanafis omit it? What is the evidence and the exception for janazah?
Follow the discussion from 'ليس عند المتقدمين' to the preferred view.
3
Determine the timing of thana'
When is thana' recited relative to the takbir? What is the position of Abu Yusuf and the relied-upon view?
Note the phrases 'قبل التكبير' and 'بعده' and the tarjih.
4
Apply the follower's ruling
For a muqtadi (follower), when does he stop reciting thana'? Does it matter if he is masbuq or mudrik, jahr or sirr?
Focus on the last sentence: 'فالمقتدي يأتي به ما لم يشرع الإمام في القراءة مطلقاً'.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
Summarize the intra-Hanafi disagreement and the tarjih authority. What is the mufta bihi?
Use the madhhab dispute map for clarity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (لما روينا) في شرح قوله رفع يديه للتحريمة من قوله لأن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان إذا افتتح الصلاة كبر، ثم رفع يديه حتى يحاذي بإبهاميه أذنيه يقول : سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك الخ، وليس عند المتقدمين قول في : وجل ثناؤك، وفي البحر والنهر عن المعراج قال مشايخنا لا يؤمر به ولا ينهى عنه وفي سكب الأنهر عن الحلبي : والأولى ترك وحل ثناؤك إلا في صلاة الجنازة اهـ ولعل وجه الفرق أن صلاة الجنازة يطلب فيها الدعاء فهو بحالها أليق ولا يأتي بدعاء التوجه مطلقاً لا قبل الشروع ولا بعده وهو قولهما، وهو الصحيح المعتمد كما في البحر، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يأتي به قبل التكبير، وفي رواية عنه بعده قال ابن أمير حاج والحق الذي يظهر أن قراءته قبل النية، أو بعدها قبل التكبير لم تثبت عن النبي ، ولا عن أصحابه فجعله مستحباً، أو أدباً من آداب الصلاة ليس بظاهر، بل غايته أنه بدعة حسنة أن قصد به المعونة على جمع القلب على النية وحضور القلب في الصلاة والترك أحسن كما هو ظاهر الرواية عن أصحاب المذهب أسوة بما كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه أن حضور القلب لا يتوقف على ذلك، وما رواه أبو يوسف مما يدل على طلبه، فمحمول على التهجد أو كان ونسخ، ثم أعلم إن الثناء يأتي به كل مصل فالمقتدي يأتي به ما لم يشرع الإمام في القراءة مطلقاً سواء كان مسبوقاً أو مدركاً في حالة الجهر أو السر.
His statement: (as we narrated) in the explanation of his statement 'he raised his hands for the opening takbir' from his statement: Because the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he opened the prayer, he said the takbir, then raised his hands until his thumbs were level with his earlobes, saying: Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika... etc. And among the early scholars there is no statement regarding 'wa jalla thana'uka'. In al-Bahr and al-Nahr from al-Mi'raj: Our shaykhs said: It is not commanded nor prohibited. In Saqb al-Anhar from al-Halabi: The preferable is to leave 'wa jalla thana'uka' except in janazah prayer. Perhaps the difference is that janazah prayer requires supplication, so it is more suitable to it. And he does not recite the du'a of turning to Allah (tawajjuh) at all, neither before starting nor after, which is the position of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). It is the correct and relied-upon position as in al-Bahr. From Abu Yusuf that he recites it before the takbir, and in a narration from him after it. Ibn Amir Haj said: The truth that appears is that reciting it before the intention or after it before the takbir has not been established from the Prophet nor from his Companions, so making it mustahabb or an adab from the adab of prayer is not apparent. Rather, at best it is a good innovation (bid'ah hasanah) if intended for assistance in gathering the heart for the intention and presence of heart in prayer. And leaving it is better as is the apparent narration from the companions of the madhhab, following the example of the Prophet and his Companions that presence of heart does not depend on that. And what Abu Yusuf narrated that indicates its desirability is interpreted as referring to tahajjud or it was abrogated. Then know that every worshipper recites the thana'; the follower recites it as long as the imam has not started the recitation absolutely, whether he is a masbuq or a mudrik in jahr or sirr prayer.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the ruling of thana' (opening supplication). It provides the proof from hadith that the Prophet recited 'Subhanaka Allahumma...' after takbir. It then discusses the phrase 'Wa jalla thana'uka': the earlier authorities did not mention it, and later scholars differ; the preferred view is to omit it except in janazah prayer because that prayer is more about du'a. Regarding the timing of thana', the relied-upon position (Sahibayn) is that it is recited after takbir, not before. Abu Yusuf has a narration that it can be before, but the stronger view is after, as the Prophet's practice was after takbir. The follower recites thana' only until the imam begins the qira'ah, regardless of whether the follower is masbuq or mudrik, in jahr or sirr. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
الثناء (al-thana'): The opening supplication in prayer, beginning with 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...'
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer who recites thana' only until the imam starts qira'ah.
التوجه (al-tawajjuh): The turning to Allah with supplication; here refers to thana' or similar du'a before prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Thana' is a sunnah after takbir; the follower recites it only until the imam begins qira'ah, and the phrase 'wa jalla thana'uka' is omitted except in janazah prayer.

Ta'awwudh: Sunnah of Recitation or Prayer?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'awwudh classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on ta'awwudh, identify the thamarah al-khilaf, and state the mufta bihi position for the muqtadi and masbuq.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is sunnah of recitation, not of prayer itself — the follower does not recite it.

The ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) before recitation in prayer might seem straightforward, but a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute exists about its legal classification. This passage clarifies that the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) ties it to recitation, while Abu Yusuf ties it to the prayer itself. Understanding this distinction determines whether the follower (muqtadi) recites it or not. We will walk through the reasoning and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the view of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad: ta'awwudh is sunnah of recitation (sunnat al-qira'ah), not of the prayer. The follower does not recite because he does not recite Qur'an.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf holds it is sunnah of the prayer itself, so even the follower is directly addressed by the command.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; Abu Yusuf is a major disciple.
3
Follow the opposing proof
Examine Abu Yusuf's dalil: general need to ward off shaytan during prayer, and that the Prophet recited ta'awwudh in prayer.
The need exists for all praying, not just reciters.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa counters that the command in the Qur'an (16:98) is conditional upon intending recitation. The muqtadi is not reciting, so the condition fails. The imam's recitation suffices for protection.
The response is based on textual linkage (ta'liq).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: the muqtadi does not recite ta'awwudh per Abu Hanifa, but does per Abu Yusuf. Also, if omitted, no sajda sahw is needed on the preferred view.
Know which ruling applies in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويسن) التعوذ) ولو أتى بغير الفاتحة لأنه سنة القراءة لا قراءة الفاتحة بخصوصها على الظاهر وإلى ذلك مال السيد في شرحه . قوله : (واختاره الهندواني) لموافقته القرآن واختاره من القراء حمزة. قوله: (فيأتي به المسبوق) إذا قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به، والأمام في صلاة العيد يأتي به بعد التكبيرات، ويتعوذ المسبوق عند الشروع في قول أبي يوسف. قوله : (لا المقتدى لأنه لا يقرأ، والأمر بها معلق بإرادة القراءة. قوله : (لدفع وسوسة الشيطان والمصلي أحوج إليه من القارىء فيلحق به اهـ من الشرح
His statement: (and it is sunnah) al-ta'awwudh, even if he recites other than al-Fatiha, because it is sunnah of recitation, not specifically of the recitation of al-Fatiha, according to the apparent view, and al-Sayyid inclined to this in his commentary. His statement: (and al-Hinduwani chose it) because it agrees with the Qur'an, and among the reciters Hamzah chose it. His statement: (the masbuq recites it) when he stands to make up what he missed, and the imam in 'id prayer recites it after the extra takbirs, and the masbuq recites ta'awwudh at the start according to Abu Yusuf's view. His statement: (not the muqtadi) because he does not recite (Qur'an), and the command is conditional upon intending recitation. His statement: (to repel the whisper of shaytan) and the one praying is more in need of it than the reciiter, so it is attached to it (the prayer). End of the explanation.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (critical refinement) regarding the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge). The text states it is sunnah for recitation (qira'ah) in general, not specifically for al-Fatiha, so it applies even if one recites another surah. Al-Hinduwani chose the wording 'a'udhu billah' because it directly quotes the Qur'an. The dispute arises between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: Abu Hanifa holds that ta'awwudh is sunnah for recitation, so the masbuq (latecomer) recites it when making up rak'ahs, and the muqtadi (follower) does not recite it because he does not recite Qur'an behind the imam. Abu Yusuf holds that ta'awwudh is sunnah for the prayer itself to ward off shaytan's whispers, so the muqtadi also recites it. The relied-upon position in the madhhab is that of Abu Hanifa (and Imam Muhammad): ta'awwudh is sunnah of qira'ah, not of prayer. Thus the muqtadi does not recite it, and the masbuq recites it when he begins his own recitation after the imam finishes. The difference is thamarah: for the muqtadi, one school says he recites it (Abu Yusuf), the other says no (Abu Hanifa).

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): Reciting 'a'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' before qira'ah in prayer.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): The latecomer who joins the congregation after the imam has started and completes missed rak'ahs after imam's salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The muqtadi and the imam
C) The imam, the munfarid, and the masbuq when he recites
D) Everyone including the muqtadi

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ta'awwudh is sunnah of recitation, so the follower does not recite it, but the masbuq recites it when making up his own recitation.

Tasmiyah in Prayer: Sunnah or Wajib?
Dispute on basmalah and ruling on tasmiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tasmiyah in prayer, explain the inter-madhhab dispute on basmala's Quranicity, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Basmala is a separate Quranic verse, yet reciting it in prayer is sunnah, not wajib.

This lesson examines the ruling on saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' before al-Fatiha in prayer. The Hanafi school considers it sunnah, but there is a sharp disagreement: does the basmala belong to the Qur'an? And is it obligatory to recite it? We will follow the text's argument, which weighs the evidence for obligation as weak.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that tasmiyah is sunnah. Note the exception: it is a specific wording, not any dhikr.
The text says 'wa tusannu al-tasmiyah' – the verb indicates recommendation.
2
Unpack the Quranicity dispute
Malik and others say basmala is not Qur'an. The Hanafi response: it is a separate verse, revealed for separation between surahs. This affects the ruling on reciting it in prayer.
If not Qur'an, it cannot be obligatory to recite in prayer. But even if it is Qur'an, the Hanafis do not make it wajib because the obligation is for the surah itself.
3
Analyse the evidence for obligation
The passage mentions intra-Hanafi dispute: some riwayat from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn say it is wajib. But the text declares the statement of obligation as weak (da'if).
Al-Zayla'i and al-Maqdisi affirmed the sunnah view.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon ruling is sunnah. Leaving it does not require sujud al-sahw, though some recommend it as precaution.
The text concludes: 'wal-qaul bi wujubihi da'if'.
5
Apply to ta'min
The passage ends by saying 'yasunnu al-ta'min' for both imam and follower – sunnah, not wajib.
This is added as a related sunnah act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتسن التسمية) أي باللفظ المخصوص لا مطلق الذكر كما في الذبيحة، والوضوء در وهي آية واحدة من القرآن، وقال مالك والأوزاعي، وبعض أهل المذهب أنها ليست من القرآن اهـ وأنزلت للفصل بين السور فكان يعرف فصل السور بها وكتبت في الفاتحة لأنها ليست أول ما نزل، ولم تكتب في سورة براءة لأنها نزلت بالتخويف، والبسملة آية رحمة وأمن، وليست من الفاتحة ولا من كل سورة، ولم تجز بها الصلاة عنده لأن فرض القراءة ثابت بيقين فلا يسقط بما فيه شبهة، ولم يكفر جاحد قرآنيتها لأنها وإن تواتر كتابتها في المصاحف لم يتواتر كونها قرآناً والمكفر الثاني لا الأول وفي القهستاني والأصح أنها آية في حرمة المس لا في جواز الصلاة وفي البحر وتحرم على ذي الحدث الأكبر إلا إذا قصد الذكر، والتيمن قوله : (والقول بوجوبها ضعيف) جزم الزيلعي في سجود السهو لا بوجوبها، وقدم القول بسجود السهو فيها، وصححه العلامة المقدسي شارح النظم، وفي معراج الدراية عن المعلي عن الإمام وجوبها وهو قولهما وفي رواية الحسن أنها لا تجب إلا عند إفتتاح الصلاة والصحيح أنها تجب في كل ركعة حتى لو سها عنها قبل الفاتحة يلزمه السهو، وعليه ابن وهبان اه ملخصاً من الشرح. ويسن التأمين للإمام والمأموم.
His statement: (and it is sunnah) al-tasmiyah, i.e., with the specific wording, not absolute dhikr like in dhabiha and wudu. And it is one verse of the Qur'an. Malik, al-Awza'i, and some of the people of the madhhab said it is not from the Qur'an. It was revealed for separation between surahs, so it was known to separate surahs by it, and it was written in al-Fatiha because it is not the first revealed, and it was not written in Surah Bara'ah because it was revealed with intimidation. The basmala is a verse of mercy and security, and it is not from al-Fatiha nor from any surah. Prayer is not valid with it according to him because the obligation of recitation is established with certainty, so it is not negated by what is doubtful. And one who denies it being Qur'an is not declared kafir because, although its writing in the mus'haf is mutawatir, its being Qur'an is not mutawatir, and takfir is by the second [type] not the first. In al-Qahistani and the most correct: it is a verse regarding the sanctity of touching [the mus'haf], not regarding the validity of prayer. In al-Bahr: it is haram for one in major impurity unless he intends dhikr and tayammum. His statement: (and the statement of its obligation is weak) al-Zayla'i asserted in sujud al-sahw that it is not obligatory, and he gave precedence to the statement that sujud al-sahw is required for leaving it, and al-Maqdisi, commentator of al-Nudhm, confirmed this. In Ma'raj al-Diraya from al-Ma'li from al-Imam: its obligation, and it is the position of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). In a narration from al-Hasan: it is not obligatory except at the opening of the prayer. The correct [view] is that it is obligatory in every rak'ah, such that if one forgets it before al-Fatiha, sujud al-sahw is required, and Ibn Wahban followed this. End of summary from the explanation. And it is sunnah to say amin for the imam and follower.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the ruling of tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim') before al-Fatiha in prayer. The text states it is sunnah, with a specific wording. It then discusses a major inter-madhab dispute: whether the basmala is part of the Qur'an. Imam Malik, al-Awza'i, and some Hanafis hold it is not part of the Qur'an; it is simply for separation between surahs. This has practical implications: if it is not part of the Qur'an, then reciting it in prayer is not obligatory (only sunnah), and denying its Quranicity does not constitute kufr. The Hanafi position (as preferred) is that it is a verse of the Qur'an but not part of any surah; it is a separate verse. This means it is part of the Qur'an but its recitation in prayer is still sunnah, not wajib, because the obligation of recitation is for a surah, not for the basmala specifically. The hadith: 'Every prayer in which the Umm al-Qur'an is not recited is invalid' does not require the basmala. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether tasmiyah is obligatory or sunnah: the text says the statement of obligation is weak. Al-Zayla'i and al-Maqdisi side with non-obligation, while a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa (via al-Hasan) suggests obligation only at the beginning of prayer, and the Sahibayn say it is obligatory in every rak'ah. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is sunnah, not wajib, and leaving it does not require sujud al-sahw, though some say sujud al-sahw is required as a precaution (ahwat). The passage ends with the ruling that tasmiyah is sunnah, and also adding 'amin' is sunnah for both imam and follower.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' before reciting al-Fatiha in prayer.
البسملة (al-basmalah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' considered as a verse of the Qur'an.
التأمين (al-ta'min): Saying 'Amin' after reciting al-Fatiha in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on leaving out the basmalah before al-Fatiha in prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) The prayer is valid but sujud al-sahw is required
C) The prayer is valid and no sujud al-sahw is required
D) The prayer is invalid only if done deliberately

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, basmalah is a separate Qur'anic verse, but reciting it in prayer is sunnah, not wajib; the claim of obligation is weak.

Ruling on Isti'adha in Prayer
Explanation of when isti'adha is said and for whom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who says isti'adha in prayer and explain the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Yusuf and the two regarding its purpose.

Core Idea
The ma'mum does not say isti'adha because he does not recite; the masbuq says it when starting his missed rak'ahs.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies the application of isti'adha in prayer. While the general rule is that isti'adha is said before recitation, there is a subtle difference: some scholars attach it to the prayer itself to repel whisperings. The passage also specifies the positions of the ma'mum (follower) and masbuq (latecomer).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is isti'adha (seeking refuge). The Hanafi ruling is that it is sunnah for the imam and the munfarid (individual pray-er) before recitation.
The sunnah status is established by the command in the Quran (16:98) and practice of the Prophet ﷺ.
2
Identify who is excluded
The ma'mum (follower) does not say isti'adha because he does not recite in prayer according to the Hanafi school. The command is attached to the intention of recitation.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two).
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf considers isti'adha a sunnah of the prayer itself, not just for recitation, because the pray-er needs protection from shaitan's whisperings. He thus would allow the ma'mum to say it, but the mufta bihi is the first view.
Some later sources (al-Khulasa, al-Dhakhira) regard Abu Yusuf's view as correct.
4
Apply to special cases
The masbuq (latecomer) says isti'adha when starting his missed rak'ahs, just like the imam. The imam in Eid prayer says isti'adha after the takbirs.
These applications follow from the principle that isti'adha is for recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرجيم، وهو ظاهر المذهب، أو أستعيذ الخ واختاره الهندواني (للقراءة) فيأتي به المسبوق كالإمام والمنفرد لا المقتدي لأنه تبع للقراءة عندهما وقال أبو يوسف تبع للثناء سنة للصلاة لدفع وسوسة الشيطان وفي الخلاصة والذخيرة قول أبي يوسف الصحيح ببسسم[؟] والقول[؟] دلالة[؟] قوله : (واختاره الهندواني) لموافقته القرآن واختاره من القراء حمزة. قوله: (فيأتي به المسبوق) إذا قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به، والأمام في صلاة العيد يأتي به بعد التكبيرات، ويتعوذ المسبوق عند الشروع في قول أبي يوسف. قوله : (لا المقتدى لأنه لا يقرأ، والأمر بها معلق بإرادة القراءة. قوله : (لدفع وسوسة الشيطان والمصلي أحوج إليه من القارىء فيلحق به اهـ من الشرح
The stoned one, and it is the apparent of the madhhab, or I seek refuge etc. and al-Hindwani chose it (for recitation). So the masbuq does it like the imam and the munfarid, not the muqtadi because it is a follower of recitation according to the two, and Abu Yusuf said it is a follower of the thana (initial praise), sunnah for the prayer to repel the whisper of the shaitan. And in al-Khulasa and al-Dhakhira, the statement of Abu Yusuf is correct. [unclear] His statement: (and al-Hindwani chose it) because it agrees with the Quran and it was chosen by the reciter Hamza. His statement: (so the masbuq does it) when he stands to make up what he was preceded in, and the imam in the Eid prayer does it after the takbirs, and the masbuq seeks refuge at the start according to the statement of Abu Yusuf. His statement: (not the muqtadi) because he does not recite, and the command is attached to the intention of recitation. His statement: (to repel the whisper of the shaitan) and the one praying is more in need of it than the reciter, so it is included with him. End from the Sharh.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Maraqi al-Falah. It addresses the ruling on isti'adha (seeking refuge) in prayer. The apparent position of the madhhab is that one says 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' (or 'Asta'idh') before recitation, as chosen by al-Hindwani. The masbuq (latecomer) says it like the imam and the munfarid, but the muqtadi (follower) does not because he does not recite; the command to say isti'adha is attached to the intention of recitation. Abu Yusuf considered it similar to the thana (initial praise) and a sunnah of the prayer to repel the whisperings of shaitan. Some sources (al-Khulasa, al-Dhakhira) regard Abu Yusuf's view as correct. The commentary then explains selected phrases: al-Hindwani's choice agrees with the Quran and the reciter Hamza; the masbuq says it when starting to make up missed rak'ahs; the imam in Eid says it after the takbirs; and the one praying is more in need of isti'adha than a reciter outside prayer, so it is attached to prayer.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): Seeking refuge with Allah from the accursed shaitan by saying 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joins the prayer late and has missed some rak'ahs.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): One who follows the imam in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The imam only
B) The imam and the munfarid
C) The imam and the ma'mum
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: isti'adha is sunnah before recitation for the imam and munfarid; the ma'mum does not say it, and the masbuq says it when starting his missed rak'ahs.

The Basmalah in Prayer: The Hanafi View and the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on basmalah's ruling and Quranic status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on basmalah before al-Fatihah and evaluate the proofs of the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
The basmalah is sunnah in Hanafi prayer, but the dispute over its status crosses madhhabs.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on saying 'Bismillah' before al-Fatihah in each rak'ah. We will explore why it is considered sunnah, not wajib, and how the Hanafi school's proof differs from that of the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to weigh legal evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that basmalah is sunnah before al-Fatihah in each rak'ah, not wajib.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school considers it a fard verse of al-Fatihah; the Maliki school says it is not Quranic.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i: basmalah is written in the mushaf and recited by the Prophet; therefore it is fard. Maliki: it was revealed only for separation between surahs, not as part of them.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: while the writing is mutawatir, its status as part of the surahs is not mutawatir; the Prophet's practice did not consistently show it as an obligation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Shafi'is must recite it; Hanafis may omit it without invalidation but should follow the precaution of sujud al-sahw if omitted.

And in Sharh al-Diya': the wording 'the fatwa is stronger than the chosen'; and what is in the Hashiya follows al-Kamal and his student Ibn Amir Haj, who favored that the difference is about sunniyyah, and there is no dispute that if one says it, it is good due to the difference of opinion about it being a verse of every surah. Then, is this specific to when one recites the surah from its beginning, or does it include when one recites from its middle verses, etc.? The apparent reasoning of their making it based on the difference about it being a verse of every surah supports the first possibility. This is investigated by some of the excelled scholars.

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of basmalah in prayer. The matn states that saying the basmalah (bismillah) at the beginning of each rak'ah before al-Fatihah is sunnah. However, there is a weak view that it is wajib. The commentary expands: the basmalah is a specific wording, not just any dhikr. There is a major disagreement on whether it is part of the Quran. Malik, al-Awza'i, and some Hanafis hold it is not Quranic; rather it was revealed to separate surahs. In the Hanafi school, although it is written in the mushaf with tawatur, its being Quran is not tawatur, so one who denies it is not a disbeliever. The relied-upon Hanafi view for prayer is that it is not part of al-Fatihah or any surah, so prayer with it alone is invalid because the fard of recitation is certain and cannot be dropped by something doubtful. However, for the prohibition of touching the mushaf, it is considered a verse. On the issue of obligation, the dominant Hanafi view (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that it is sunnah, not wajib; but some narrations from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn suggest it is wajib. The correct view according to many Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Zayla'i, al-Maqdisi) is that leaving it necessitates sujud al-sahw, not invalidation, which indicates it is wajib in the Hanafi sense (a necessary act whose omission requires compensation). The author says sujud al-sahw for leaving it is precautionary. Then a benefit (fa'idah): it is sunnah to say isti'adha and basmalah before reciting a complete surah; for a single ayah, only isti'adha is needed. Then a discussion on basmalah between al-Fatihah and a surah: there is disagreement on whether it is said. Some texts say it is sunnah in silent prayer only, others say it is good without dislike. The commentary points out that the fatwa is emphasized over the chosen, and the difference is about being sunnah, not about permissibility.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' before recitation in prayer.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness required for omitting a wajib act in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Sunnah, omission may require sujud al-sahw
C) Wajib, omission requires sujud al-sahw
D) Makruh, it is disliked

Key Takeaway
The basmalah in prayer is sunnah in the Hanafi school, with the precaution of sujud al-sahw, while Shafi'is consider it fard and Malikis do not recite it.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Is Basmalah Wajib or Sunnah? The Precautionary View
Intra-Hanafi dispute on basmalah's obligation and the precautionary ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the wajib and sunnah positions within the Hanafi school on basmalah and apply the precautionary ruling of sujud al-sahw.

Core Idea
Though the mufta bihi is sunnah, the intra-Hanafi dispute makes sujud al-sahw the cautious path.

In this lesson, we dive deeper into the Hanafi school itself, where there is a known dispute on whether basmalah is wajib or sunnah. We will trace the evidence from different narrations and understand why the later scholars recommended sujud al-sahw as a precaution. This exemplifies the Hanafi methodology of weighing conflicting riwayat.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The relied-upon view from Zahir al-Riwayah is that basmalah is sunnah.
2
Identify the variant view
Some narrations from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn consider it wajib in every rak'ah.
3
Analyse the evidence for the variant
These narrations rely on the Prophet's practice and the fact that it was always written in the mushaf.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The majority of later scholars (Zayla'i, Maqdisi) rejected the wajib view as weak, citing lack of consistent practice.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and precaution
The mufta bihi is sunnah, but the precaution (ihtiyat) is to perform sujud al-sahw if omitted, to exit the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) تسن (التسمية أول كل ركعة) قبل الفاتحة لأنه كان يفتتح صلاته الله الرحمن الرحيم بوجوبها ضعيف وإن صحح لعدم ثبوت المواظبة عليها قوله : (وتسن التسمية) أي باللفظ المخصوص لا مطلق الذكر كما في الذبيحة، والوضوء در وهي آية واحدة من القرآن، وقال مالك والأوزاعي، وبعض أهل المذهب أنها ليست من القرآن اهـ وأنزلت للفصل بين السور فكان يعرف فصل السور بها وكتبت في الفاتحة لأنها ليست أول ما نزل، ولم تكتب في سورة براءة لأنها نزلت بالتخويف، والبسملة آية رحمة وأمن، وليست من الفاتحة ولا من كل سورة، ولم تجز بها الصلاة عنده لأن فرض القراءة ثابت بيقين فلا يسقط بما فيه شبهة، ولم يكفر جاحد قرآنيتها لأنها وإن تواتر كتابتها في المصاحف لم يتواتر كونها قرآناً والمكفر الثاني لا الأول وفي القهستاني والأصح أنها آية في حرمة المس لا في جواز الصلاة وفي البحر وتحرم على ذي الحدث الأكبر إلا إذا قصد الذكر، والتيمن قوله : (والقول بوجوبها ضعيف) جزم الزيلعي في سجود السهو لا بوجوبها، وقدم القول بسجود السهو فيها، وصححه العلامة المقدسي شارح النظم، وفي معراج الدراية عن المعلي عن الإمام وجوبها وهو قولهما وفي رواية الحسن أنها لا تجب إلا عند إفتتاح الصلاة والصحيح أنها تجب في كل ركعة حتى لو سها عنها قبل الفاتحة يلزمه السهو، وعليه ابن وهبان اه ملخصاً من الشرح أقول مستعيناً بالله تعالى سجود السهو بتركها هو الأحوط خروجاً من هذا الخلاف . بالبسملة. فائدة : يسن لمن قرأ سورة تامة أن يتعوّذ ويسمى قبلها واختلف فيما إذا قرأ آية والأكثر على أنه يتعوذ فقط ذكره المؤلف في شرحه من باب الجمعة ثم أعلم أنه لا فرق في الإتيان بين الصلاة الجهرية والسرية وفي حاشية المؤلف على الدرر واتفقوا على عدم الكراهة في ذكرها بين الفاتحة ،والسورة بل هو حسن سواء كانت الصلاة سرية، أو جهرية، وينافيه ما في القهستاني أنه لا يسمي بين الفاتحة والسورة في قولهما وفي رواية عن محمد قال في المضمرات والفتوى على قولهما وعن محمد أنها تسن في السرية دون الجهرية لئلا يلزم الإخفاء بين جهرين، وهو شنيع واختاره في العناية والمحيط، وقال في شرح الضياء: لفظ الفتوى أكد من المختار وما في الحاشية تبع فيه الكمال وتلميذه ابن أمير حاج حيث رجحا أن الخلاف في السنية، فلا خلاف أنه لو سمي أ لكان حسناً لشبهة الخلاف في كونها آية من كل سورة، ثم هل يخص هذا بما إذا قرأ السورة من أولها أو يشمل ما إذا قرأ من أوسطها آيات مثلاً وظاهر تعليلهم كون الإتيان بها لشبهة الخلاف في كونها آية من كل سورة يفيد الأول كذا بحثه بعض الأفاضل
(And) it is sunnah (the basmalah at the beginning of every rak'ah) before al-Fatihah because he used to open his prayer with 'Allah al-Rahman al-Rahim'; the view of its obligation is weak, even if some consider it correct due to lack of proof of consistency upon it. His statement: (And the basmalah is sunnah) i.e. with the specific wording, not absolute dhikr, as in the case of slaughter and ablution. It is one verse of the Quran, but Malik, al-Awza'i, and some of the madhhab hold that it is not from the Quran. It was revealed to separate between surahs, so he knew the separation of surahs by it. It was written in al-Fatihah because it was not the first that was revealed, and it was not written in Surah Bara'ah because it was revealed with intimidation. The basmalah is a verse of mercy and security; it is not part of al-Fatihah nor of every surah. Prayer with it alone is not valid according to him because the obligation of recitation is established with certainty, so it cannot be dropped by what contains doubt. The one who denies its being Quran is not declared a disbeliever because, although its writing in the mushafs is mutawatir, its being Quran is not mutawatir; the one who denies is a second-level disbeliever, not the first. In al-Qahistani and the more correct view, it is a verse for the prohibition of touching [the mushaf] but not for the permissibility of prayer. In al-Bahr: it is forbidden for the one in major impurity unless he intends dhikr. And the reliance: his statement: (And the view of its obligation is weak). Al-Zayla'i affirmed in 'Sujud al-Sahw' that it is not obligatory, and he presented the view of sujud al-sahw for it, and this was declared correct by 'Allama al-Maqdisi, commentator of al-Nazm. In Mi'raj al-Dirayah from al-Mu'alla from the Imam: it is obligatory, and this is the view of the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]; and in a narration from al-Hasan that it is not obligatory except at the beginning of the prayer; the correct view is that it is obligatory in every rak'ah, so much so that if one forgets it before al-Fatihah, sujud al-sahw becomes necessary, and Ibn Wahban followed this. End, summarized from the Sharh. I say, seeking aid from Allah Almighty, that sujud al-sahw for leaving it is the most precautionary, exiting from this difference. With the basmalah. Benefit: It is sunnah for one who recites a complete surah to seek refuge and say basmalah before it; there is a difference if he recites one ayah, and the majority hold that he seeks refuge only. The author mentioned this in his commentary on the Friday prayer section. Then know that there is no difference in performance between loud and silent prayer. And in the author's Hashiya on al-Durar: they agreed that there is no dislike in mentioning it between al-Fatihah and the surah; rather it is good, whether the prayer is silent or loud. This is contradicted by what is in al-Qahistani that he does not say basmalah between al-Fatihah and the surah according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], and in a narration from Muhammad that it is sunnah in silent prayer but not in loud prayer to avoid hiding between two loud recitations, which is bad; this was chosen in al-'Inaya and al-Muhit. And in Sharh al-Diya': the wording 'the fatwa is stronger than the chosen'; and what is in the Hashiya follows al-Kamal and his student Ibn Amir Haj, who favored that the difference is about sunniyyah, and there is no dispute that if one says it, it is good due to the difference of opinion about it being a verse of every surah. Then, is this specific to when one recites the surah from its beginning, or does it include when one recites from its middle verses, etc.? The apparent reasoning of their making it based on the difference about it being a verse of every surah supports the first possibility. This is investigated by some of the excelled scholars.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of basmalah in prayer. The matn states that saying the basmalah (bismillah) at the beginning of each rak'ah before al-Fatihah is sunnah. However, there is a weak view that it is wajib. The commentary expands: the basmalah is a specific wording, not just any dhikr. There is a major disagreement on whether it is part of the Quran. Malik, al-Awza'i, and some Hanafis hold it is not Quranic; rather it was revealed to separate surahs. In the Hanafi school, although it is written in the mushaf with tawatur, its being Quran is not tawatur, so one who denies it is not a disbeliever. The relied-upon Hanafi view for prayer is that it is not part of al-Fatihah or any surah, so prayer with it alone is invalid because the fard of recitation is certain and cannot be dropped by something doubtful. However, for the prohibition of touching the mushaf, it is considered a verse. On the issue of obligation, the dominant Hanafi view (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that it is sunnah, not wajib; but some narrations from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn suggest it is wajib. The correct view according to many Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Zayla'i, al-Maqdisi) is that leaving it necessitates sujud al-sahw, not invalidation, which indicates it is wajib in the Hanafi sense (a necessary act whose omission requires compensation). The author says sujud al-sahw for leaving it is precautionary. Then a benefit (fa'idah): it is sunnah to say isti'adha and basmalah before reciting a complete surah; for a single ayah, only isti'adha is needed. Then a discussion on basmalah between al-Fatihah and a surah: there is disagreement on whether it is said. Some texts say it is sunnah in silent prayer only, others say it is good without dislike. The commentary points out that the fatwa is emphasized over the chosen, and the difference is about being sunnah, not about permissibility.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' before recitation in prayer.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness required for omitting a wajib act in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the precautionary Hanafi view, what should a person do if they forget to say basmalah in a rak'ah?
A) Nothing, it is optional
B) Repeat the rak'ah
C) Perform sujud al-sahw
D) Perform the prayer again

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon view is sunnah, but the presence of a wajib narration leads to the precautionary recommendation of sujud al-sahw.

The Ruling and Pronunciation of Amin After Al-Fatihah
Ruling and linguistic details of amin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for saying amin in prayer, identify the most eloquent pronunciation, and explain whether mispronunciation invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
Amin is sunnah, not Quran; its most eloquent form is with madd and takhfif.

Saying 'amin' after al-Fatihah is a well-known practice in prayer, but its ruling and pronunciation are often misunderstood. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies that it is sunnah for the imam, ma'mum, and munfarid, and provides linguistic and legal details on its pronunciation, meaning, and effect on prayer validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act this passage addresses and the legal status it assigns. The act is saying 'amin' after al-Fatihah. The ruling is sunnah (recommended) for all categories of worshipers.
The text explicitly states 'yusannu' (it is sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited for the sunnah ruling. The passage cites a hadith where Jibril taught the Prophet to say amin, and the command 'When the imam says amin, then say amin.'
The hadith about Jibril is narrated with a gharib chain per al-Zayla'i.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the dalil proves the ruling. The command in the hadith (amr) indicates recommended action (sunnah) in Hanafi usul, and the Prophet's own practice further supports it.
The text does not elaborate on usul, but the command implies sunniyyah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify differences of opinion mentioned. Some considered amin to be part of the Quran (from al-Mujtaba), and there are variant pronunciations (madd vs qasr, tashdid vs takhfif).
The author clarifies that the majority hold it is not Quran.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine which view is relied upon. The mufta bihi is that amin is sunnah, pronounced with madd and takhfif, and mispronunciations that are not found in the Quran may invalidate the prayer.
Fatwa leans toward not invalidating for madd with tashdid because 'aaman' appears in the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يسن (التأمين) للإمام والمأموم والمنفرد والقارىء خارج الصلاة للأمر به في الصلاة، وقال : «لقنني جبريل عليه السلام عند فراغي من الفاتحة آمين وقال : إنه كالختم على الكتاب، وليس من القرآن وأفصح لغاته المد والتخفيف والمعنى استجب دعاءنا قوله : (والمأموم) ولو سمعها في سرية، أو من مقتد مثله في صلاة جمعة، أو عيد، أو جماعة كثيرة. قوله : (للأمر به في الصلاة في قوله : «إذا أمن الإمام فأمنوا فإن من وافق تأمينه تأمين الملائكة غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه والمراد الموافقة من الجانبين في الزمان، فلا وجه لما في المستصفى من قوله : لم يرد به الموافقة في التلفظ بها في وقت واحد وإنما المراد الموافقة من حيث الإخلاص والثقة بالله تعالى قال الأزهري : غفر له دعا له، وغفره دعا عليه لأن الغفر هو الإعدام اهـ قال الرضي: إن آمين سرياني كقابيل لأنه ليس من أوزان كلام العرب وهو إسم فعل كصه للسكوت مبني على الفتح لخفته كأين، وكيف، لأن أسماء الأفعال مبنية بالاتفاق، وحكمه السكون حالة الوقف والتحريك بحركة البناء حالة الوصل لإلتقاء الساكنين قوله: (لقنني جبريل الخ ) قال الزيلعي المخرج، هو بهذا اللفظ غريب قوله (وليس) من القرآن حكي في الشرح عن المجتبى الخلاف في أنه القرآن . من قوله: (وأفصح لغاته الخ) قال ثعلب وغيره : هو بالمد والقصر مع التخفيف فيهما كلاهما فصيح مشهور وفي المصباح القصر لغة أهل الحجاز والمدلغة بني عامر والمد إشباع بدليل أنه يوجد في العربية كلمة على وزن فاعيل ،اهـ وحكي الواحدي عن حمزة والكسائي الإمالة فيها، ولو مد مع التشديد كان مخطئاً في المذاهب الأربعة، وهو من لحن العوام، ولا تفسد به الصلاة عند الثاني لوجوده في القرآن وعليه الفتوى ولو مدّ وحذف الياء لا تفسد عند الثاني أيضاً لوجوده في القرآن قال تعالى: ويلك آمن ولو قصر وحذف أو شدد معهما ينبغي الفساد لأنهما لم يوجدا في القرآن أفاده في التبيين. قوله: (والمعنى استجب دعاءنا هذا عند الجمهور، وروى الثعلبي في تفسيره بإسناده إلى الكلبي عن أبي صالح عن ابن عباس قال : سألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن معنى آمين فقال : افعل وقيل لا يخيب الله رجاءنا، وروى عبد الرزاق عن أبي هريرة بإسناد ضعيف أنه من أسماء الله تعالى أي يا آمين استجب فحذف منه حرف النداء وأقيم النداء مقامه فلذلك أنكر جماعة القصر فيه وقيل كنز من كنوز العرش، لا يعلم تأويله إلا الله تعالى
(And) it is sunnah (the amin) for the imam, the ma'mum, and the munfarid, and the reciter outside the prayer due to the command for it in prayer. And he said: 'Jibril عليه السلام taught me when I finished al-Fatihah: amin, and he said: It is like a seal on the book, and it is not from the Quran, and the most eloquent of its pronunciations is with madd and takhfif, and the meaning is: respond to our supplication.' His statement: (and the ma'mum) even if he hears it in silent prayer, or from a follower like him in Friday prayer, Eid, or a large congregation. His statement: (due to the command for it in prayer in his statement: 'When the imam says amin, then say amin, for whoever's amin coincides with the amin of the angels, his past sins are forgiven.') The intended meaning is concurrence from both sides in time, so there is no basis for what is in al-Mustasfa that it means concurrence in sincerity and trust in Allah, not in pronouncing it at the same time. Al-Azhari said: 'Ghafara' means 'He made a du'a for him' and 'Ghafara' means 'He made a du'a against him' because 'al-ghafr' is destruction. End. Al-Radi said: 'Amin' is Syriac like Qabil because it is not from the patterns of Arabic speech; it is an ism fi'l (verb-derived noun) like 'Sah' (for silence), built on fatha for lightness like 'ayna' and 'kayfa', because ism al-fi'l are built by agreement; its rule is sukun at the end in pause and movement with the vowel of construction in connection due to meeting of two quiescent letters. His statement: (Jibril taught me etc.) Al-Zayla'i said about the chain: it is gharib with this wording. His statement: (it is not from the Quran) It is related in the Sharh from al-Mujtaba that there is a difference of opinion about it being Quran. From his statement: (the most eloquent of its pronunciations) Tha'lab and others said: it is with madd and qasr with takhfif in both, both are eloquent and well-known. In al-Misbah: qasr is the language of the people of Hijaz and madd is the language of Banu 'Amir; madd is an extension, evidenced by the existence in Arabic of a word on the pattern of fa'ayil. End. Al-Wahidi narrated from Hamza and al-Kisa'i the imala (inclination) in it. If one prolongs (madd) with tashdid (doubling), he errs in the four schools, and it is a common mistake, and the prayer is not invalidated by it according to the second (Abu Yusuf? or Muhammad?) because it is found in the Quran; and the fatwa is upon that. Even if one prolongs and drops the ya, the prayer is not invalidated according to the second also because it is found in the Quran, Allah says: 'Waylaka aaman' [20:?]. If one shortens (qasr) and drops or emphasizes both, it likely invalidates because they are not found in the Quran; this is from al-Tabyin. His statement: (and the meaning is 'respond to our supplication') This is according to the majority. Al-Tha'labi narrated in his Tafsir with his chain to al-Kalbi from Abu Salih from Ibn 'Abbas who said: I asked the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم about the meaning of 'amin' and he said: 'Do.' And it is said: 'Allah does not disappoint our hope.' 'Abd al-Razzaq narrated from Abu Hurayra with a weak chain that it is one of the names of Allah, meaning 'O Amin, respond', so the call letter was omitted and the calling was substituted, therefore a group denied the qasr in it. And it is said: a treasure from the treasures of the Throne, whose interpretation is known only to Allah.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the sunnah of saying 'amin' after al-Fatihah. The matn states that amin is sunnah for the imam, ma'mum, and munfarid, and also for the reciter outside prayer due to the command. A hadith says Jibril taught the Prophet to say amin after al-Fatihah, describing it as a seal on the book. The commentary explains that the ma'mum says it even if he hears it in a silent prayer or from a fellow follower. The hadith about saying amin when the imam says it is interpreted as concurrence in time, not just spiritually. Linguistically, 'amin' is a Syriac word, an ism fi'l meaning 'respond'. Its pronunciation: the most eloquent is with madd (elongation) and takhfif (lightness). There is a difference of opinion whether it is from the Quran; the majority say it is not. If one elongates with tashdid (like 'ammeen'), it is a mistake but does not invalidate prayer because a similar pronunciation occurs in the Quran (e.g., 'aaman' in the story of Pharaoh). The text clarifies that if one pronounces it in a way not found in the Quran (e.g., qasr with tashdid), it likely invalidates the prayer. The meaning is 'respond to our supplication' or 'O Allah, do not disappoint our hope'. Some say it is a name of Allah.

Key Terms
التأمين (al-ta'min): Saying 'amin' after al-Fatihah in prayer.
آمين (amin): An ism fi'l meaning 'O Allah, respond' or 'accept our supplication'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling on saying 'amin' after al-Fatihah in prayer?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Saying amin after al-Fatihah is sunnah, not Quran, and the most eloquent pronunciation is with madd and takhfif; mispronunciations that are not in the Quran may invalidate the prayer.

Ruling on Tahmeed: Sunnah for Follower and Alone Worshiper
Concise ruling on tahmeed after ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tahmeed for each type of worshiper and explain that the munfarid says both tasmee' and tahmeed.

Core Idea
Tahmeed is sunnah for follower and alone worshiper; imam only says tasmee'.

In this lesson, we examine a brief but crucial ruling on the dhikr after rising from ruku'. The matn affirms that saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd' (tahmeed) is sunnah for the ma'mum and the munfarid by consensus. The commentary clarifies that the munfarid also says the tasmee' when rising, while the imam says only tasmee'. Understanding this distinction preserves the proper form of prayer agreed upon by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
The act is 'tahmeed' – saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd' after rising from ruku'. The text clearly states it is sunnah (يسن).
Sunnah here indicates recommended, not obligatory.
2
Determine who performs it
The text says it is sunnah for the ma'mum (follower) and the munfarid (alone worshiper) by consensus (اتفاقاً). The imam is not included; he only says tasmee'.
The consensus (ittifaq) is among the Hanafi school.
3
Distinguish the munfarid's additional dhikr
The commentary explains that the munfarid says both tasmee' when rising and tahmeed when lowering (or when straightening, according to some sources).
This differentiates the munfarid from the imam (who says only tasmee') and the ma'mum (who says only tahmeed).
4
Note the timing nuance
There is a slight difference of opinion on when exactly the tahmeed is said: when lowering from ruku' or when straightening. The text cites Majma' al-Anhur and al-Durar as sources.
Both timings are acceptable; the key is that it is said after rising.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يسن (التحميد) للمؤتم والمنفرد اتفاقاً قوله : (والمنفرد) أي مع التسميع، فيأتي بالتسميع حال الإرتفاع، وبالتحميد حال الإنخفاض وقيل حال الاستواء، كما في مجمع الأنهر، وجزم به في الدرر
(And) it is sunnah (the tahmeed) for the follower and the munfarid by consensus. His statement: (and the munfarid) i.e., with the tasmee', so he comes with tasmee' when rising, and with tahmeed when lowering, and it is said when straightening, as in Majma' al-Anhur, and it was decided upon in al-Durar.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a concise ruling statement on the sunnan of prayer. The matn states that saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd' (tahmeed) is sunnah for the ma'mum (follower) and munfarid (alone worshipper) by agreement. The commentary clarifies that the munfarid says both the tasmee' (Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah) when rising from ruku' and the tahmeed when bending down (or when straightening up, according to some). This is based on the cited sources.

Key Terms
التحمید (al-tahmeed): Saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd' after rising from ruku'.
التسميع (al-tasmee'): Saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' when rising from ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The ma'mum only
C) The munfarid only
D) The ma'mum and the munfarid

Key Takeaway
Tahmeed is sunnah for the follower and alone worshiper; the imam says only tasmee'.

Ruling on Saying 'Amin' in Prayer
Explanation of ruling on saying Amin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on saying 'Amin' in prayer for the imam, ma'mum, and munfarid, identify which pronunciations invalidate the prayer according to the Hanafi school, and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Amin is a recommended supplication after al-Fatiha, not a Quranic verse; mistaken pronunciations only invalidate the prayer if they produce unheard Arabic forms.

Saying 'Amin' after al-Fatiha is a well-known practice in prayer. But is it obligatory or recommended? And does the way you pronounce it affect the validity of your prayer? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on 'Amin', drawing on the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ and clarifying common errors in pronunciation. By the end, you will know precisely when your prayer remains valid and when it becomes invalid due to mispronunciation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
First, determine the legal status (hukm) of saying 'Amin' for each category: imam, ma'mum (follower), and munfarid (one praying alone). The text states it is sunna (recommended) for all three.
The text explicitly says it is sunna, not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the Dalil
Identify the proof cited: the hadith 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin...' and the statement that Jibril taught the Prophet to say Amin. Understand that the command 'Fa'minu' is interpreted as recommendation, not obligation, in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is the primary textual evidence (dalil naqli).
3
Analyze the Pronunciation Variants
The text discusses four aspects: lengthening (madd), shortening (qasr), lightening (takhfif), doubling (tashdid). Understand which combinations are allowed and which invalidate the prayer, based on whether the form exists in the Quran.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) opinion on invalidation follows Imam Abu Yusuf.
4
Identify the Ikhtilaf
Note the disagreement about whether 'Amin' is part of the Quran. Some early scholars held it was, but the Hanafi school and the consensus affirm it is not. The practical effect is that certain mispronunciations that exist in the Quran do not invalidate, while those that do not exist do invalidate.
The ikhtilaf is about its being a Quranic verse, not about its recommendation.

And he said: 'Jibril taught me when I finished al-Fatiha to say Amin, and he said: It is like a seal on the book, and it is not from the Quran, and the most eloquent of its pronunciations are with lengthening and lightening, and the meaning is: Answer our supplication.' And tahmid is recommended for the follower and the one praying alone by agreement. The fatwa is stronger than the chosen view, and what is in the hashya follows al-Kamal and his student Ibn Amir Haj, as they preferred that the difference is in the sunniyya, so there is no disagreement that if he were to name it, it would be good due to the semblance of disagreement about it being a verse from every sura. Then does this apply only if he recites the sura from its beginning, or does it include if he recites from its middle, for example? The apparent meaning of their reasoning that it is brought due to the semblance of disagreement about it being a verse from every sura indicates the first, as some virtuous ones researched. His saying: (and the follower) even if he heard it in a silent prayer, or from someone like him following in a Jumu'ah prayer, Eid, or a large congregation. His saying: (because of the command to do so in prayer) in his saying: 'When the imam says Amin, then say Amin, for whoever's Amin coincides with the Amin of the angels, his previous sins are forgiven.' What is meant is concurrence from both sides in time, so there is no basis for what is in al-Mustasfa: 'He did not mean concurrence in uttering it at the same time, but rather concurrence in sincerity and trust in Allah.' Al-Azhari said: 'Ghafara lahu means He answered his supplication; Ghaffara means He did not answer his supplication because al-ghufr is non-existence.' Ar-Radi said: 'Amin is Syriac like Qabil [؟] because it is not from the patterns of Arabic speech, and it is a verbal noun like Sah [for silence], built on fatha due to lightness, like Ayna and Kayfa, because verbal nouns are built by agreement. Its rule is sukun when stopping and movement with a building vowel when connected due to meeting two silent letters.' His saying: (Jibril taught me, etc.) Az-Zayla'i said: 'The narrator said: This wording is strange.' His saying: (and it is not) from the Quran. It was narrated in the Sharh from al-Mujtaba that there is disagreement about it being from the Quran. From his saying: (and the most eloquent of its pronunciations, etc.) Tha'lab and others said: 'It is with lengthening and shortening, both with lightening, both eloquent and well-known.' In al-Misbah: 'Shortening is the language of the people of Hijaz, and lengthening is the language of Banu Amir, and lengthening is excess, as evidence that in Arabic there is a word on the pattern Fa'ila.' And al-Wahidi narrated from Hamza and al-Kisa'i that there is imala in it. If one lengthens with doubling, he is mistaken according to the four schools, and it is from the common people's errors. The prayer is not invalidated by it according to the second [Abu Yusuf] because it exists in the Quran, and the fatwa is upon that. If one lengthens and drops the ya, it does not invalidate according to the second also because it exists in the Quran, as Allah said: 'Waylaka amin.' If one shortens and drops or doubles with them, it should invalidate because they are not found in the Quran, as stated in al-Tabyin. His saying: (and the meaning: Answer our supplication) This is according to the majority. And al-Tha'labi narrated in his tafsir with his chain to al-Kalbi from Abu Salih from Ibn Abbas who said: 'I asked the Messenger of Allah about the meaning of Amin, and he said: Do it.' And it was said: 'Allah will not disappoint our hope.' And Abd al-Razzaq narrated from Abu Hurairah with a weak chain that it is one of the names of Allah, meaning: O Amin, answer, so the call particle was dropped and the call stands in its place, therefore a group objected to shortening it. And it was said: 'It is a treasure from the treasures of the Throne, whose interpretation is not known except to Allah.'
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on saying 'Amin' in prayer. The author explains that Amin is recommended (sunna) for the imam, follower, and one praying alone, based on the hadith commanding it and the Prophet's statement that Jibril taught him to say it. It is not part of the Quran, contrary to some opinions. The most eloquent pronunciation is with lengthening (al-madd) and lightening (al-takhfif), but shortening is also permissible. The meaning is a supplication: 'Answer our prayer.' The text discusses the effect of different pronunciations on the validity of prayer: lengthening with lightening is fine; lengthening with doubling is a common error but does not invalidate according to Abu Yusuf because such a form occurs in the Quran (e.g., 'ayman'? actually 'amin' in the verse 'Waylaka amin' is different). Shortening and dropping the ya or doubling invalidates because such forms are not in the Quran. The entry also covers the follower's Amin, even if he hears it from an imam in a silent prayer or from a fellow follower in a large congregation. The hadith about agreeing with the angels' Amin is about temporal concurrence, not emphasis. The linguistic analysis treats Amin as a verbal noun (ism fi'l) built on fatha. The passage clarifies that the disagreement among scholars is about its being sunna, but all agree that saying it is good.

Key Terms
آمين (Amin): A verbal noun meaning 'O Allah, answer our supplication'; it is not from the Quran but is recommended to be said after al-Fatiha in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which pronunciation of 'Amin' invalidates the prayer?
A) Lengthening (madd) and lightening (takhfif)
B) Lengthening and doubling (tashdid)
C) Shortening (qasr) with dropping the ya and doubling
D) Shortening with lightening

Key Takeaway
Amin is a recommended supplication after al-Fatiha; only pronunciations that produce non-Quranic Arabic forms invalidate the prayer, and the mufta bihi view follows Abu Yusuf.
