Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Sunnah of Tasmi', Tahmid, and Standing Posture
Sunnah rulings for imam, follower, and munfarid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts (sunan) for the imam, follower, and one praying alone regarding tasmi', tahmid, and standing posture, and identify the mufta bihi position on whether the imam combines both tasmi' and tahmid.

Core Idea
The imam combines tasmi' and tahmid; the follower says only tahmid; alternating feet (tarawuh) is recommended for humility.

In this lesson, we explore several sunan (recommended acts) of prayer related to the adhkar after ruku' and the standing posture. These practices enhance humility and follow the prophetic example. We will focus on who says what during the transition from ruku' and how to stand with ease during long prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific sunan
List the sunan covered: tasmi' (saying Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah), tahmid (Rabbana lakal hamd), i'tidal at takbir, jahr for imam, spacing feet, tarawuh (alternating feet), and relaying takbir when needed.
These are sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory.
2
Distinguish the roles
Determine who says what: the imam says both tasmi' and tahmid (mufta bihi), the follower says only tahmid, and the one praying alone says both. The imam recites takbir and tasmi' aloud; the follower and munfarid recite silently.
The imam's jahr is for informing the congregation.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Hanifa held the imam says only tasmi', while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two disciples) held the imam combines both. Understand the evidence: hadith of Abu Hurayrah combining both and the hadith pointing to a division.
The mufta bihi follows the two disciples.
4
Apply the principle of tarjih
See why the view of the two disciples is preferred: the hadith evidence is stronger, and it is the relied-upon position in later texts like al-Durar and al-Qahistani.
Al-Qahistani declared it sahih (correct).
5
Examine the additional sunan
Understand the sunan related to standing: being balanced at takbir, spacing feet four fingers apart, and tarawuh (alternating weight). Recognize that tarawuh is recommended, not disliked, despite some reports.
Tarawuh is easier for long standing, especially in taraweeh.

لكثرتهم فمستحب فإن لم يقم مسمع يعرفهم بالشروع، والإنتقالات ينبغي لكل صف من المقتدين الجهر بذلك إلى حد يعلمه الأعمى ممن يليهم، ولا بد لصحة شروع الإمام في الصلاة من قصد الإحرام بتكبيرة الإفتتاح، فلو قصد الإعلام فقط لا يصح وإن ، فهو المطلوب منه شرعاً، وينال أجرين، وكذا جمع بين الأمرين، الحكم في المبلغ إن قصد التبليغ فقط، فلا صلاة له ولا لمن أخذ بقوله في هذه الحالة لأنه اقتدى بمن ليس في صلاة كما في عليه سهل قوله : ( وأمكن لطول القيام) قال السيد في شرحه وهذا هو محمل ما نقل عن الإمام
His saying: (and the one praying alone) meaning with tasmi', so he performs tasmi' while rising, and tahmid while bending, and it is said while straightening, as in Majma' al-Anhur, and it is certain in al-Durar. And for the imam according to the two also. (And) it is recommended (to conceal it in the thana' and what follows due to the traditions that have come about that). (And) it is recommended (to be balanced at the beginning of the tahrimah and its end, such that he performs it without lowering his head) as has come. (And) it is recommended (for the imam to recite aloud the takbir and tasmi') because of his need to inform of the start and transition, and there is no such need for the one praying alone or the follower. (And) it is recommended (to space the feet while standing about four fingers apart) because it is closer to humility, and al-tarawuh is better than standing with feet fixed. The explanation of al-tarawuh is that he leans on one foot sometimes and on the other sometimes, because it is easier and more conducive to long standing. (And) it is recommended that the sura be that which is guaranteed for the Fatiha. And it is the apparent answer, and it is correct as in al-Qahistani. His saying: (And for the imam according to the two also) due to the hadith of Abu Hurayrah that he used to combine both (tasmi' and tahmid) agreed upon, and because he prompts others, so he does not forget himself. And he has what Anas and Abu Hurayrah narrated that he said: 'When the imam says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, then say Rabbana lakal hamd' agreed upon, a division between them, and division precludes partnership. His saying: (due to the traditions that have come about that) from the Prophet's saying: 'The best remembrance is the hidden remembrance, and the best worship is the most hidden, and the best sustenance is what suffices.' His saying: (And it is recommended for the imam to recite aloud the takbir and tasmi', and likewise the salam). What is meant by takbir includes the takbir of the two Eids and the funeral. Know that takbir when there is no need for it, such that the imam's voice can reach them, is disliked. In al-Sira al-Halabiyya: The four imams agreed that relaying in this situation is a blameworthy innovation, i.e., disliked. But when there is need for it, such that the congregation's voice cannot reach the imam, either due to his weakness or their large number, it is recommended. If no relayer informs them of the start and transitions, each row of followers should recite aloud to the extent that the blind person near them knows. And for the validity of the imam's starting the prayer, he must intend the ihram with the opening takbir. If he only intends to inform, it is not valid, even if he intends both, that which is required from him legally, and he receives two rewards. The ruling for the relayer: if he intends only to relay, there is no prayer for him nor for the one who follows his statement in this case, because he followed someone not in prayer, as in Fatawa al-Ghazzi. As for tasmi' from the imam, and tahmid from the relayer, and the takbirs of transitions from both, intention of dhikr is not required for the validity of prayer but for reward. And it does not invalidate the prayer of the one who follows his statement because he is following someone in prayer, unlike the first case. This is from al-Sayyid and others. His saying: (And it is recommended to space the feet while standing about four fingers apart) It is stated in Kitab al-Athar from the Imam and no disagreement is reported. In al-Zahiriyya: It is reported from the Imam that al-tarawuh in prayer is more beloved to me than fixing the feet straight. As for what is in Munyat al-Musalli about the dislike of swaying right and left, it is interpreted as swaying consecutively without intermittent stillness, as some do during dhikr, not leaning on one foot for a while and then on the other similarly. Rather, it is sunna, as mentioned by Ibn Amir Haj. Likewise, what is in al-Hindiyya from al-Zahiriyya and in al-Binaya from al-Kashf about the dislike of al-tarawuh is interpreted as what preceded. Then, the specification is for one who has no excuse. But if he is fat or has a scrotal hernia and needs a wide spacing, the matter is easy for him. His saying: (and more conducive to long standing) Al-Sayyid said in his commentary: This is the interpretation of what is reported from the Imam.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage covers several sunan of the prayer related to the imam and the one praying alone. First, it discusses tasmi' (saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah') and tahmid (saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd'). The one praying alone says tasmi' while rising from bowing and tahmid while bending (or while straightening, as some say). The imam, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, also combines both tasmi' and tahmid, based on hadiths that show the Prophet and Abu Hurayrah did both. The imam is recommended to pronounce takbir and tasmi' aloud to inform the congregation of movements. The follower and the one praying alone should keep these dhikrs silent, based on a hadith that the best remembrance is hidden. The passage also addresses the case when the imam's voice does not reach the congregation: it is recommended to have someone relay the takbirs, but the relayer must intend prayer, not just relaying, otherwise his own prayer and that of those relying on him may be invalid. Another sunna is to be balanced (i'tidal) at the beginning and end of the opening takbir (tahrimah), without lowering the head. Further, the feet should be spaced about four fingers apart while standing, as this aids humility. The term 'al-tarawuh' refers to alternately shifting weight from one foot to the other, which is considered better than standing rigidly, especially for long prayers. However, swaying aimlessly is disliked. The spacing applies to those without excuse; those with physical needs may space wider.

Key Terms
التسميع (al-tasmi'): Saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' (Allah hears those who praise Him) by the imam or the one praying alone when rising from ruku'.
التحميد (al-tahmid): Saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd' (Our Lord, to You is all praise) after tasmi' or when straightening from ruku'.
التراوح (al-tarawuh): Alternating weight from one foot to the other while standing in prayer, considered better than standing on both feet fixed, especially for long prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, what does the imam say when rising from ruku’?
A) Only 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'
B) Only 'Rabbana lakal hamd'
C) Both 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and 'Rabbana lakal hamd'
D) Nothing, the follower says 'Rabbana lakal hamd'

Key Takeaway
The imam says both tasmi' and tahmid, the follower only tahmid, the munfarid both; tarawuh (alternating feet) is recommended for long standing.

Sunnah Recitations in the Five Daily Prayers
Describes the recommended surahs for each prayer time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah recitations for each prayer and identify the Hanafi position on reciting specific surahs in Fajr on Friday.

Core Idea
Reciting specific surahs is sunnah, not wajib; flexibility is allowed.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rulings on which surahs are recommended to recite in each of the five daily prayers. We'll see the division of the mufassal, the proofs from the Companions, and an important dispute with the Shafi'i school. The key takeaway is that these recitations are sunnah mu'akkadah—strongly recommended but not obligatory—and that necessity permits any surah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mufassal divisions
First, understand the three parts of the mufassal: long (ṭiwāl: al-Hujurat to 'Abasa), middle (awṣāṭ: al-Kawthar to al-Duha), and short (qiṣār: rest).
The exact boundaries vary; the passage gives a specific Hanafi classification.
2
Map surah lengths to prayer times
Based on the narration from 'Umar, the passage assigns long mufassal to Fajr and Zuhr, middle to 'Isha, and short to Maghrib. Note the reasoning: Fajr and Zuhr have spacious time.
Zuhr is also equated to 'Asr due to people's occupations, but the main sunnah is as narrated.
3
Analyze the Fajr Friday recitation
Read the hadith of Abu Hurairah about the Prophet reciting Surah al-Sajdah and al-Insan in Fajr on Friday. This is where the dispute arises.
Hanafis largely abandoned this practice; Shafi'is adhere to it.
4
Understand the Hanafi ruling on flexibility
The passage states that neither constant adherence nor total abandonment is recommended. The Prophet's recitation of the mu'awwidhatayn due to necessity shows that any surah suffices when needed.
Necessity includes hearing a child cry or being on a journey.
5
Learn the sunnah of lengthening the first rak'ah
It is sunnah by consensus to make the first rak'ah longer than the second in Fajr, preferably two-thirds and one-third. Imam Muhammad extends this to all prayers.
Lengthening the second over the first beyond two verses is disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

From Surat al-Hujurat to Surat 'Abasa, and its middle from Surat al-Kawthar to al-Duha, and the rest are short. Because it is narrated from 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he used to recite in Maghrib the short mufassal, in 'Isha the middle mufassal, and in Fajr the long mufassal. Zuhr is like Fajr due to equality in spaciousness of time, and it is reported that it is like 'Asr due to people's preoccupation with their tasks. It is narrated from Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to recite in Fajr on Friday 'Alif Lam Mim Tanzil' and 'Hal ata 'ala al-insan'. The Hanafis, except a few among them, have abandoned this sunnah, while the Shafi'is, except a few, adhere to it. So the ignorant of the two schools think that the prayer becomes invalid by doing it or leaving it. So neither leaving it nor constantly adhering to it is appropriate. And out of necessity, one may recite any surah he wishes. The Prophet (peace be upon him) recited the mu'awwidhatayn in Fajr, and when he finished, they said, 'Have you crossed over?' He said, 'I heard the crying of a child and feared that his mother would be tempted.' Likewise if he is traveling. Lengthening the first [rak'ah] in Fajr is sunnah by consensus, due to continuous practice from the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to our day: two-thirds in the first and one-third in the second, as recommended. Even if the disparity is great, it is acceptable. And his saying 'only' refers to Muhammad's statement: 'I prefer that the first be lengthened in all prayers.' And it is disliked to lengthen the second over the first by consensus, beyond two verses.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi discusses the sunnah recitations in the five daily prayers. It first defines the sections of the mufassal (the long, middle, and short parts) and then attributes to 'Umar the practice of reciting short surahs in Maghrib, middle in 'Isha, and long in Fajr. For Zuhr, it is like Fajr due to the time being spacious, and like 'Asr due to people's business. It then mentions the specific recitation in Fajr on Friday: Surah al-Sajdah and Surah al-Insan. The Hanafis largely abandoned this, while Shafi'is mostly adhere. The ignorant think it invalidates prayer, but the correct view is that neither complete abandonment nor constant adherence is required. Out of necessity, any surah suffices, as the Prophet once recited the mu'awwidhatayn in Fajr when hearing a child cry. Lengthening the first rak'ah in Fajr is sunnah by consensus, with recommended distribution of two-thirds and one-third. Imam Muhammad preferred lengthening the first in all prayers. Disliking to lengthen the second over the first is agreed upon, unless by a few verses.

Key Terms
المفصل (al-mufassal): The section of the Quran from Surah Qaf or al-Hujurat to the end, divided into long (ṭiwāl), middle (awṣāṭ), and short (qiṣār).
المعوذتين (al-mu'awwidhatayn): Surah al-Falaq and Surah al-Nas, recited for seeking refuge in Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is disliked because it resembles the Shafi'is.
D) It invalidates the prayer if recited.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, reciting specific surahs in each prayer is a sunnah with flexibility, not a rigid obligation.

Tasbih in Ruku and Sujud: The Minimum Number and Its Ruling
Explains the sunnah of tasbih and its minimum number.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of tasbih in ruku and sujud, identify the minimum number for sunnah perfection, and apply the rule when following an imam.

Core Idea
Three tasbihs is the minimum for sunnah reward; one suffices but reducing from three is disliked.

You know that tasbih in ruku and sujud is a sunnah of prayer. This passage clarifies exactly how many times you should say it and why. It also resolves the practical question: what if you are following the imam and he rises before you finish? The answer hinges on a subtle distinction between linguistic and moral minimum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that saying takbir for ruku and tasbih in ruku and sujud is sunnah. Recognize that the hukm level is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wajib.
Takbir for ruku is sunnah based on the Prophet's practice; tasbih is sunnah based on the hadith.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith: 'When one of you bows, let him say three times Subhana Rabbi al-'Azim…' is the proof. Note that it is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the imperative indicates recommendation (istihbab) according to Hanafi usul.
The hadith also prescribes three times for sujud: Subhana Rabbi al-A'la.
3
Distinguish the two minima
The passage says 'that is its minimum' and explains that it refers to the minimum of moral perfection (adna al-kamal al-ma'nawi), i.e., the actual attainment of sunnah reward. The linguistic minimum would be two (plural), but the moral perfection requires three.
Thus, three is the minimum to fully achieve the sunnah; saying one or two is valid but does not achieve the same reward.
4
Apply the follower scenario
If the imam rises before the follower completes three tasbihs, the correct view (as per the passage) is that the follower should follow the imam immediately. Some Hanafis held the follower should complete, but the relied-upon position is to follow.
The imam should also avoid prolonging tasbih to the point of wearying the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوافل الأمر أسهل (و) يسن ( تكبير الركوع) لأن النبي كان يكبر عند كل خفض ورفع سوى الرفع من الركوع فإنه كان يسمع فيه (و) يسن (تسبيحه) أي الركوع (ثلاثاً) لقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : إذا ركع أحدكم فليقل ثلاث مرات سبحان ربي العظيم، وذلك أدناه وإذا سجد فليقل سبحان ربي الأعلى ثلاث مرات وذلك أدناه أي أدنى كماله المعنوي وهو الجمع المحصل للسنة لا اللغوي، والأمر للاستحباب فيكره أن ينقص عنها ولو رفع الإمام قبل إتمام المقتدي ثلاثاً فالصحيح أنه يتابعه ولا يزيد الإمام على وجه يمل به القوم وكلما زاد
In supererogatory prayers, the matter is easier. And it is sunnah to say takbir for bowing, because the Prophet used to say takbir at every lowering and raising except rising from bowing, for he used to hear the tasmi'. And it is sunnah to recite tasbih in bowing three times, due to the Prophet's saying: 'When one of you bows, let him say three times: Subhana Rabbi al-'Azim. That is its minimum. And when he prostrates, let him say: Subhana Rabbi al-A'la three times. That is its minimum.' That is the minimum of its moral perfection, which is the actual attainment of the sunnah, not the linguistic minimum. The command is for recommendation, so it is disliked to reduce from that. If the imam raises before the follower completes three, the correct view is that he follows him. And the imam should not increase in a manner that wearies the congregation; and whenever he increases...
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage addresses the sunnah acts in ruku and sujud. It first notes that in non-obligatory prayers, the rules are more lenient. Then it states that saying takbir when going into ruku is sunnah, as the Prophet did so. The tasbih in ruku and sujud is also sunnah, and the minimum number is three times based on the hadith commanding it. The 'minimum' mentioned refers to the minimum of moral perfection (the attainment of sunnah reward), not the linguistic minimum (which would be two). The command indicates recommendation (istihbab), so it is disliked to reduce below three. If the imam rises before the follower completes three, the follower should follow the imam (this is the sound opinion; some say he should complete). The imam should not prolong to the point of wearying the congregation.

Key Terms
أدنى الكمال المعنوي (adna al-kamal al-ma'nawi): The minimum number (three) that achieves the moral perfection of the sunnah, i.e. the reward of following the sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Fard
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Tasbih in ruku and sujud is a sunnah muakkadah; three repetitions are the minimum for full reward, and following the imam takes precedence over completing them.

Takbir and Tasbih in Ruku' – Prescribed Actions
Ruling on sunnah actions during ruku' with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah actions in ruku', explain the hadith proof, and apply the ruling when following an imam.

Core Idea
The minimum tasbih in ruku' is three; the follower must follow the imam even if incomplete.

In this passage, al-Tahtawi explains the sunnah actions during ruku' in prayer. The Prophet's instruction to say tasbih three times is analysed to distinguish between the minimal linguistic plural and the spiritual perfection required for the sunnah. The ruling also addresses the follower's obligation when the imam rises early.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah actions
The passage states it is sunnah to say takbir when moving to ruku' and to say tasbih three times. Note that takbir is said at every lowering and raising except the raising from ruku', where tasmi' is said.
Takbir is general for movements; tasbih is specific to ruku' and sujud.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith cited uses an imperative (فليقل) but the phrase 'ذلك أدناه' indicates a recommended minimum, not an obligation. In Hanafi usul, an imperative is for recommendation when accompanied by a statement of minimum.
The command is for istihbab (recommendation).
3
Understand the minimum
Three is the minimum for spiritual perfection (adna kamaalihi al-ma'nawi). The linguistic minimum would be two (plural), but the sunnah requires three. Increasing to five, seven, etc. is better, ending on an odd number.
The phrase 'ذلك أدناه' is interpreted as the minimum of the sunnah's perfection.
4
Apply the follower's obligation
If the imam raises before the follower completes three tasbihs, the correct view is that the follower follows the imam. The follower does not complete the tasbihs.
The passage says 'فالصحيح أنه يتابعه' (the correct view is he follows).
5
Note the imam's conduct
The imam should not increase tasbih to the point of annoying the congregation. In supererogatory prayers, the matter is easier; increasing is not disliked if done with proper intention.
Intentions matter: if the imam intends to help a latecomer, it is commendable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسن تكبير الركوع لأن النبي ﷺ كان يكبر عند كل خفض ورفع سوى الرفع من الركوع فإنه كان يسمع فيه ويسن تسبيحه أي الركوع ثلاثاً لقول النبي ﷺ: إذا ركع أحدكم فليقل ثلاث مرات سبحان ربي العظيم وذلك أدناه وإذا ولا يزيد الإمام على وجه يمل به القوم وكلما زاد وهذا بالنسبة لغير ما وردت به السنة فلا يشكل بما أخرجه الشيخان أنه كان يقرأ في أولى الجمعة والعيدين بالأعلى وفي الثانية بالغاشية وهي أطول من الأولى بأكثر المعنوي الذي في الزيلعي أي أدنى كمال السنة والفضيلة فالضمير راجع إلى غير مذكور معلوم من المقام وفي البحر واختلف في قوله وذلك أدناه فقيل أدنى كمال السنة وقيل أدنى كمال التسبيح وقيل أدنى القول المسنون قال والأول أوجه فحينئذ الأولى للشارح أن يقول أي أدنى كمالها ليعود الضمير للسنة أو الفضيلة والمراد أن الكمال المعنوي له مراتب الثلاث والخمس والسبع مثلاً والثلاث أدناها فهي أدنى العدد المسنون فلو أتى بواحدة لا يثاب ثواب السنة وإن كان يحصل له ثواب آخر قال في البحر ما ملخصه أن الزيادة أفضل بعد أن يختم على وتر خمس أو سبع أو تسع الخبر الصحيحين: إن الله وتر يحب الوتر وفي منية المصلي: أدناه ثلاث وأوسطه خمس وأكمله سبع ومثله في المضمرات عن الزاد قوله وهو الجمع أي الكمال الجمع وهو حمل مجازي من الإسناد إلى السبب لأن الجمع هو السبب في الكمال والمراد الجمع الصادق بالثلاث والخمس والسبع قوله لا اللغوي عطف على المعنوي أي ليس المراد أدنى الكمال اللغوي أي أدنى كمال الجمع اللغوي فإن أدناه إثنان لما فيهما من الإجتماع فليس مراداً وإن كان صحيحاً في نفسه لأنه مفيد للأحكام للحقائق اللغوية. قوله فالصحيح أنه يتابعه وقال المرغيناني يتمه. قوله ولا يزيد الإمام الخ فلو زاد لإدراك الجاني قيل مكروه وقيل مفسد وكفر وقيل جائز إن كان فقيراً وقيل جائز إن كان لا يعرفه وقيل مأجور إن أراد القربة قهستاني عن الزاهدي وغيره وفي البحر والنهر ما حاصله أنه إن قصد به غير القربة فلا شك في كراهته وإن قصد به القربة فلا شك في عدم كراهته بل إستحسنه الفقيه أبو الليث لقوله تعالى: (وتعاونوا على البر والتقوى) [المائدة/ 5].
It is sunnah to say takbir for the ruku' because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to say takbir at every lowering and raising except for the raising from ruku' for which he used to say tasmi'. And it is sunnah to say tasbih in ruku' three times due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'When one of you bows, let him say three times: Subhana Rabbiyal Adheem. That is its minimum. And when he prostrates, let him say: Subhana Rabbiyal A'la three times. That is its minimum.' That is the minimum of its spiritual perfection, which is the combined [count] that achieves the sunnah, not the linguistic minimum. The command is for recommendation, so it is disliked to decrease from that. And if the imam raises before the follower completes three, the correct view is that he follows him. And the imam should not increase to the point of annoying the congregation, and every increase [beyond three] is for that which the sunnah did not specify. This regarding obligatory prayers; in supererogatory prayers the matter is easier. The meaning of 'minimum of its spiritual perfection' is the minimum of the sunnah's perfection. The spiritual perfection has levels: three, five, seven. Three is the minimum. If one says only one tasbih, he does not receive the reward of the sunnah, though he gets another reward. Increasing is better, ending on an odd number. The combined [count] means the sum that brings about perfection, which is three, five, or seven. The linguistic minimum is two, but that is not intended. The correct view is that the follower follows the imam even if he hasn't completed three. Regarding the imam increasing to catch up a latecomer, there are various opinions, but the gist is that if his intention is not for worship, it is disliked; if for worship, it is not disliked and even commended.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the sunnah actions in ruku'. The author begins by stating that it is sunnah to say takbir when moving to ruku' and to say tasbih three times. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet instructed saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal Adheem' three times. The phrase 'that is its minimum' is interpreted to mean the minimal level of spiritual perfection that fulfills the sunnah, not the linguistic minimum (which would be two). The command is for recommendation (istihbab), so decreasing below three is disliked. The follower must follow the imam even if he has not completed three tasbihs, according to the correct view. The imam should not prolong excessively to avoid annoyance. Increasing tasbih beyond three is better, ending on an odd number (e.g., five, seven, nine). In supererogatory prayers, the rulings are more lenient; it is not disliked to increase. The commentary then delves into the nuanced meaning of 'adna' (minimum) and the various scholarly interpretations. One key point: if a person says only one tasbih, he does not get the full reward of the sunnah, but still gets some reward. The passage also discusses the dislikedness of the imam increasing tasbih for non-worship purposes, but if his intention is to help a latecomer join the congregation, it is commendable based on the verse of cooperation in righteousness.

Key Terms
أدى كماله المعنوي (adna kamaalihi al-ma'nawi): The minimal level of spiritual perfection that achieves the sunnah, i.e., saying three tasbihs.
الجمع المحصل للسنة (al-jam' al-muhassil li al-sunnah): The combined count that brings about the sunnah, i.e., three, five, seven etc., as opposed to two which is the linguistic minimum of plural.

Ruling on Tashih in Ruku and Sujud: Hanafi Wajib vs. Shafi'i Permissibility
States tashih as wajib and refutes Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tashih in ruku and sujud, explain the evidence, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds tashih in ruku and sujud as wajib and prohibits extra dhikr in obligatory prayer.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on the prescribed glorifications (tasbihat) during bowing and prostration. The Hanafi school classifies them as wajib, meaning omission requires sajda al-sahw. This ruling is contested by the Shafi'i school, which considers them sunnah and permits additional supplications. We will explore the evidence and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling in Hanafi
State that the tashih (Subhana Rabbiyal Azeem, Subhana Rabbiyal A'la) and takbirs are wajib. Note the consequence: omission requires sajda al-sahw.
Wajib is distinct from fard; it is proven by zanni evidence.
2
Understand the Hanafi evidence
The primary evidence is the imperative form in the hadith commanding tashih. Hanafi usul takes al-amr yufidu al-wujub. Also, the phrase 'you will not perform any rukn' indicates it is not a pillar.
3
Identify the Shafi'i position and evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i allows extra dhikr such as 'Allahumma laka raka'tu' based on a hadith of Ali.
The Shafi'i school does not consider the tashih as wajib.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the hadith of Ali is specific to tahajjud (voluntary night prayer), not obligatory salah. The general command for tashih governs the obligatory prayer.
This is a takhsis of the general by context.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafis recite only the prescribed tashih and takbir; Shafi'is may add extra supplications. Hanafis must perform sajda al-sahw if tashih is omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل تسبيحات الركوع والسجود وتكبيرهما واجبات ولا يأتي في الركوع والسجود بغير التسبيح وقال الشافعي : يزيد في الركوع اللهم لك ركعت ولك خشعت ولك أسلمت وعليك توكلت وفي السجود سجد وجهي للذي وصوره وشق سمعه وبصره فتبارك الله أحسن الخالقين كما روي عن علي قلنا محمول على حالة التهجد (وقيل تسبيحات الركوع (الخ) أي فيجب بترك ذلك سجود السهو، وشذ أبو مطيع البلخي تلميذ الإمام بقوله تسبيح الركوع والسجود ركن تبطل الصلاة بتركه واختلف على قوله فظاهر الذخيرة أن الركن مرة وظاهر البدائع ثلاثة. قال ابن أمير حاج وكأن وجهه ظاهر الأمر في الحديث المتقدم. قوله : (ولك خشعت إنما ذكره بعد الركوع ليشير إلى أن المقصود بالركوع الخشوع فيحصل المعنى اللغوي في الشرعي قوله : وشق) سمعه وبصره) من عطف الخاص على العام لأن ذلك داخل في قوله : وصوره وإنما خصهما دون الذوق والشم لعظم النعمة بهما قوله: (أحسن الخالقين أي المصورين فيندفع الإشكال أو المقدرين فإن الخلق يأتي بمعنى التقدير، ومميز أحسن محذوف للعلم به أي أحسن الخالقين خلقاً. قوله: (على حالة التهجد المراد التنقل أعم من كونه ليلاً، أو نهاراً.
And it is said that the glorifications of bowing and prostration and their takbirs are obligations, and one does not recite other than the glorification in bowing and prostration. Al-Shafi'i said: 'Add in bowing: O Allah, to You I bowed, to You I humbled, to You I surrendered, and upon You I relied. And in prostration: My face prostrated to the One who created it and formed it, and split its hearing and sight. So blessed is Allah, the best of creators,' as narrated from Ali. We said: It is interpreted as applying to the case of tahajjud. (And it is said: the glorifications of bowing etc.) meaning, so abandoning that necessitates the prostration of forgetfulness. And Abu Mut'i al-Balkhi, the student of the Imam, deviated by saying that the glorification of bowing and prostration is a pillar, invalidating the prayer if abandoned. There is disagreement on his statement: the apparent of al-Dhakhira is that the pillar is one, and the apparent of al-Bada'i is three. Ibn Amir Hajj said: And it seems his face is the apparent command in the aforementioned hadith. His statement: 'And to You I humbled' – he mentioned it after bowing to indicate that the purpose of bowing is humility, so the linguistic meaning is achieved in the legislative. His statement: 'And split its hearing and sight' is a joining of the specific to the general, because that is included in His statement: 'and formed it', and he specified them without taste and smell due to the greatness of the blessing in them. His statement: 'the best of creators' meaning the formers, so the objection is repelled, or the determiners, for creation comes in the meaning of determination, and the distinguishing noun of 'best' is omitted for known reason: i.e., the best of creators in creation. His statement: 'on the case of tahajjud' meaning supererogatory, general whether it is night or day.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the recitation in bowing and prostration. The Hanafi school holds that the prescribed glorifications (Subhana Rabbiyal Azeem and Subhana Rabbiyal A'la) and the takbirs for moving are obligatory (wajib). It is not permissible to add any other dhikr in the obligatory prayer. Al-Shafi'i allows extra supplications based on a hadith of Ali. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Ali applies specifically to tahajjud (voluntary night prayer), not to the obligatory prayer. The hashia further explains that this is the relied-upon position, and the view of Abu Mut'i al-Balkhi that the tashih is a pillar (rukn) is considered irregular (shadh). The commentary also clarifies the wording of the Shafi'i supplication and the linguistic points.

Key Terms
تسبيحات (tasbihat): The prescribed glorifications in ruku and sujud (Subhana Rabbiyal Azeem and Subhana Rabbiyal A'la)
واجب (wajib): A duty required by zanni evidence; omission requires sajda al-sahw
تهجد (tahajjud): Voluntary night prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the tashih (glorifications) in ruku and sujud?
A) Sunnah muakkadah
B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds tashih in ruku and sujud as wajib; omission requires sajda al-sahw, and extra dhikr is not allowed in obligatory prayer.

The Sunnah Acts of Ruku and Their Evidence
Enumeration of sunnah acts in ruku with prophetic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of ruku, cite the hadith evidence for finger spreading, and explain the gender difference in application.

Core Idea
The Prophet’s ruku had specific sunnan: spreading fingers, straightening legs, flattening back, and aligning head with posterior.

In this lesson, we explore the sunnah (recommended) acts within the ruku posture as detailed in the Hanafi fiqh text. These acts enhance the quality of prayer and are derived from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The text also clarifies a common misunderstanding regarding women’s posture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Listed Sunan
Read the Arabic matn to recognize each recommended action: taking the knees, spreading fingers, straightening legs, flattening back, leveling head with posterior.
The text uses the phrase 'ويسن' to introduce each sunnah.
2
Connect Each Sunnah to Its Dalil
Note the hadith of Anas (ra) quoted for finger spreading: 'When you bow, place your palms on your knees and spread your fingers.' Other sunnan are supported by transmitted practice (tawaruth) and prophetic habit.
The hadith is ahad, giving zanni evidence, hence the ruling is sunnah not wajib.
3
Note the Gender Distinction
Observe that spreading fingers is for men only; women do not spread because their state is based on concealment.
This is stated explicitly: 'والمرأة لا تفرجها لأن مبنى حالها على الستر'.
4
Recognize the Hashia's Refinements
Review the commentary on leg bending (makruh tanzih) and the definition of 'ajuz. These clarify the precise application.
The hashia notes that complete finger spreading is only in ruku, complete closing only in sujud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن (أخذ ركبتيه بيديه حال الركوع (و) يسن (تفريج أصابعه) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم الأنس رضي الله عنه : إذا ركعت فضع كفيك على ركبتيك وفرج بين أصابعك وارفع يديك عن جنبيك ولا يطلب تفريج الأصابع إلا هنا ليتمكن من بسط الظهر (والمرأة لا تفرجها لأن مبنى حالها على الستر (و) يسن (نصب ساقيه لأنه المتوارث واحناؤهما شبه القوس مكروه (و) يسن (بسط) ظهره) حال ركوعه لأنه كان إذا ركع يسوي ظهره حتى لو صب عليه الماء استقر وروي أنه كان إذا ركع لو كان قدح ماء على ظهره لما تحرك لاستواء ظهره (و) يسن (تسوية رأسه بعجزه) العجز بوزن رجل من كل شيء مؤخره ويذكر ويؤنث والعجيزة للمرأة خاصة، وقد تستعمل للرجل وأما العجز فعام ما بين الوركين من الرجل والمرأة لأن النبي لو كان إذا ركع لم يشخص رأسه، ولم يصوبه ولكن بين ذلك قوله : (ولا يطلب تفريج الأصابع إلا هنا) أي التفريج التام كما أنه لا يطلب الضم التام إلا في السجود، فيما عدا هذين يبقيها على خلقتها . قوله: (ليتمكن من بسط الظهر) الأولى أن يقول : ليتمكن من الأخذ، فإن التفريج لا دخل له في البسط بالتجربة قوله : ( واحناؤهما شبه القوس مكروه أي تنزيهاً لأنه في مقابلة ترك السنة. قوله: (العجز بوزن رجل) وكتف، وسكون الجيم مع تثليث العين، والفعل كسمع، وضرب أفاده في القاموس قوله : (وهو ما بين الوركين الخ) الوركان فوق الفخذين، وما بينهما هو الذكر، والخصيتان أو فرج المرأة، وليس العجز لأنه المؤخر، وهما الإليتان، فلو قال : هو الإلية لكان أولى قوله : (لم يشخص رأسه) أي لم يرفعه من الإشخاص، وهو الرفع، قوله: (ولم يصوبه) أي لم يخفضه كما في الصحاح، والمصباح فلو خفض رأسه قليلاً يصوبه ولكن بين ذلك أي لم يرفع رأسه ولم يخفضه
(And) it is sunnah (to take his knees with his hands during ruku), and it is sunnah (to spread his fingers) because of his saying, peace be upon him, to Anas, may Allah be pleased with him: 'When you bow, place your palms on your knees, spread your fingers, and raise your hands from your sides.' And complete spreading of fingers is only required here to enable the flattening of the back. (And the woman does not spread them because her state is based on concealment.) (And) it is sunnah (to straighten his legs) because it is inherited, and bending them like a bow is disliked. (And) it is sunnah (to flatten his back) during his ruku because he, peace be upon him, would level his back when he bowed, such that if water were poured on it, it would settle. And it is narrated that when he bowed, if a cup of water were on his back, it would not move due to the levelness of his back. (And) it is sunnah (to level his head with his posterior). 'Al-ajuz' (posterior) is the rear of everything; it is masculine and feminine; 'al-ajizah' is specifically for a woman, though it may be used for a man. As for 'al-ajuz', it is general for the area between the two hips of both man and woman. Because the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he bowed, would not raise his head nor lower it, but between that. His statement: (And complete spreading of fingers is only required here) meaning complete spreading, just as complete closing is only required in prostration; apart from these two, he leaves them as they are. His statement: (to enable the flattening of the back) – it would be better to say: to enable the grasping, for spreading has no role in flattening by experience. His statement: (And bending them like a bow is disliked) meaning as a tanzih (reprehensible) because it opposes leaving the sunnah. His statement: (al-ajuz is of the measure of rajul) – and katif, with sukun of the jim and three vowels of the ain, the verb is like sami'a and daraba, as stated in al-Qamus. His statement: (It is what is between the two hips) – the hips are above the thighs, and what is between them is the male organ and testicles, or the female's private part. But al-ajuz is the rear, and that is the two buttocks. So if he said 'it is the buttocks', it would be better. His statement: (did not raise his head) meaning he did not lift it; 'ishkhas' is lifting. His statement: (and did not lower it) meaning he did not lower it, as in al-Sihah and al-Misbah. So if he lowered his head a little, he would lower it, but between that, i.e., he did not raise his head nor lower it.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage enumerates the sunnah (recommended) acts within the ruku (bowing) posture. The first is placing the hands on the knees with spread fingers for men, based on the hadith of Anas. Women are exempt from spreading fingers. Other sunan include straightening the legs, flattening the back so it is level, and aligning the head with the posterior. The hashia explains details: complete finger spreading is only in ruku; complete finger closing only in sujud. Bending legs like a bow is makruh tanzih. The commentary also clarifies the definition of 'ajuz (posterior) and its linguistic variants.

Key Terms
تفريج (tafriaj): Spreading the fingers apart
نصب الساقين (nasb al-saqayn): Straightening the legs (not bending the knees) during ruku
بسط الظهر (bast al-dhahr): Flattening the back during ruku so it is level

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Bending the legs like a bow
B) Spreading the fingers for both men and women
C) Flattening the back
D) Raising the head above the back

Key Takeaway
The sunnah acts of ruku enhance the prayer and are based on the prophetic practice; they are recommended but not obligatory.

Sunnah Acts in Rising, Sujud, and Transitions – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of rising from ruku, and sunnah order of transitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi views on the ruling of rising from ruku (fard vs wajib vs sunnah), state the mufta bihi, and apply the sunnah order of transitions in sujud and rising.

Core Idea
Rising from ruku: the mufta bihi is wajib, but Abu Yusuf holds it as fard; the sunnah order of limbs in sujud and rising is established by practice.

This lesson examines the sunnah acts in the transitions of prayer—rising from ruku, standing with tranquility, and the order of placing limbs when going into sujud and rising. It also delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal status of completing the ruku: is it sunnah, wajib, or fard?

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on rising from ruku
The matn states that it is sunnah to rise from ruku and stand with tranquility. However, the hashia clarifies that this is the correct view according to the zahir al-riwayah, but there is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
The matn uses 'yusannu' indicating sunnah.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
According to Abu Yusuf, completing the ruku (including rising) is fard. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is wajib. The mufta bihi is that it is wajib.
The hashia quotes al-Nahr and Ibn Amir Hajj supporting the wajib view.
3
Follow the evidence for the sunnah order of limbs
The hadith of the Prophet states that when prostrating he placed his knees before his hands, and when rising he raised his hands before his knees. This is used to derive the sunnah order.
The hadith is from the Prophet's practice, not a direct command.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the dispute
Later authorities like Ibn Amir Hajj prefer the wajib view for rising from ruku, supported by the principle that completing every pillar is wajib. The sunnah order for limbs remains sunnah.
The consequence of omitting a wajib is sajda al-sahw.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If one omits the rising from ruku entirely or fails to stand with tranquility, the prayer requires sajda al-sahw (according to the wajib view), whereas if it were merely sunnah, no compensation would be needed.
Intentional omission may invalidate the prayer according to some scholars.

عن المجتبى معز بالصدر القضاة إتمام الركوع وإكمال كل ركن واجب عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف فرض وكذلك رفع الرأس من الركوع والإنتصاب والقيام والطمأنينة فيه فيجب أن يكمل الركوع حتى يطمئن كل عضو منه، وكذا السجود، والأولى حذفه لتصريح المصنف به بعد قوله بأن يرفع وجهه، ثم يديه) أي، ويضعهما على ركبتيه، وينهض على صدور قدميه، وبكره تقديم إحدى رجليه عند النهوض قوله: (فيفعل ما إستطاع) أي في الهبوط، والنهوض قوله : (ويستحب الهبوط باليمين أي بالركبة بأن يقدمها على اليسرى شيئاً قليلاً، وكذا يستحب النهوض باليسار أولا . قوله : (لأن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الخ) لا ينهض دليلاً على كل المدعي ويحتمل أنه دليل على ما عنه) ونص التبيين يوافقه، وهو على ما نقله الحموي وضع اليدين حذاء المنكبين أدب .اهـ. قوله: (وقال بعض المحققين) هو الكمال رضي الله تعالى عنه وقوله : وهو أن يفعل تفسير للجمع، و في نسخة وهو قوله : وإن كان بين الكفين أفضل لما فيه من تحصيل المجافاة المسنونة ما ليس في شيء غيره ولأنّ آخر الركعة معتبر بأولها فكما يجعل رأسه بين كفيه عند الإحرام في أول الركعة فكذا.
(And) it is sunnah (to rise from ruku) according to the correct view, and it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that the rising from it is fard, and it has preceded. (And) it is sunnah (to stand after it), i.e., after rising from ruku, (with tranquility) due to transmission. (And) it is sunnah (to place his knees) first on the ground, (then his hands, then his face) when descending (for prostration), and he prostrates between them. (And) it is sunnah (the opposite for rising) to stand by lifting his face, then his hands, then his knees if he has no excuse. But if he is weak or wearing khuffs, he does what he can. And it is recommended to descend with the right (knee) and rise with the left. Because the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he prostrated, placed his knees before his hands, and when he rose, he lifted his hands before his knees. (And) it is sunnah (the takbir of prostration) as we have narrated. (And) it is sunnah (the takbir of rising from it) as narrated. (And) it is sunnah (that prostration be made between his hands), i.e., placing his face between his palms. Because he, peace be upon him, when he prostrated, placed his face between his hands, narrated by Muslim. And in Bukhari, when he prostrated, he placed his hands parallel to his shoulders. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, said that. And some researchers said to combine, and that is to do both. His statement: (And it is sunnah to rise from ruku etc.) in al-Nahr from al-Mujtaba, attributed to al-Sadr al-Qudat: completing the ruku and completing every pillar is wajib according to them (the two), and according to Abu Yusuf it is fard. Similarly, raising the head from ruku, standing upright, and tranquility therein, so he must complete the ruku until every limb is tranquil, and likewise the prostration. If he omits anything from that forgetfully, sajda al-sahw is required. Ibn Amir Hajj said: That is correct, as mentioned by al-Sayyid. His statement: (then his face) – he begins by placing the nose. His statement: (when descending) is connected to everything preceding; his statement: 'and he prostrates between them' means between his hands, but it would be better to delete it because the author explicitly states after that: 'by lifting his face, then his hands', i.e., and he places them on his knees, and rises on the balls of his feet, and it is disliked to advance one foot when rising. His statement: (he does what he can) i.e., in descending and rising. His statement: (and it is recommended to descend with the right) i.e., with the knee, by advancing it slightly over the left, and likewise it is recommended to rise with the left first. His statement: (because the Messenger of Allah etc.) does not serve as proof for everything claimed; it is possible it is only proof for what is in the matn, and that is apparent. His statement: (as we have narrated) that the Prophet, peace be upon him, would say the takbir at every lowering and raising except the rising from ruku, for he would say 'sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'. His statement: (and al-Shafi'i said) – the text of al-Tabyin agrees with him, and according to what al-Hamawi transmitted, placing the hands parallel to the shoulders is a good deportment. His statement: (and some researchers said) – he is al-Kamal, may Allah be pleased with him, and his statement 'and that is to do' is an interpretation of the combination, and in some copies: 'and it is said: although placing between the hands is better, because it achieves the recommended separation [of arms] which is not present in anything else, and because the end of the rak'ah is connected to its beginning, so just as he places his head between his hands at the beginning of the rak'ah, so too at the end.'
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage covers the sunnah actions related to transitioning between positions in prayer. It is sunnah to rise from ruku (though some narrations say fard according to Abu Hanifa, but the correct view is sunnah). Standing with tranquility after rising is sunnah. When going into sujud, the sunnah order is knees, then hands, then face. When rising, the opposite: face, hands, then knees, unless one has an excuse. It is recommended to descend with the right knee and rise with the left. Takbir is said at every movement except rising from ruku. The hashia notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Yusuf, completing the ruku and standing is fard; others say wajib. The most important sunnah is placing the face between the hands during sujud. There is a dispute with Shafi'i, who places hands shoulder-width. Some Hanafi scholars combine both by placing hands such that the face is between them and the hands are near the shoulders, but the preferred view is between the hands.

Key Terms
الرفع من الركوع (al-raf min al-ruku'): Rising from the bowing position
الطمأنينة (al-tuma'ninah): Tranquility, pausing after movements
وضع الركبتين (wad' al-rukbatayn): Placing the knees on the ground

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the sunnah order when going into sujud?
A) Hands, knees, face
B) Knees, hands, face
C) Face, hands, knees
D) Knees, face, hands

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that completing the ruku (including rising) is wajib, and the sunnah order for sujud is knees, then hands, then face.

Hand Placement During Sujud – Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on hand placement during sujud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on hand placement during sujud, identify the evidence for each, and apply the Hanafi view (face between hands) with the option of combination.

Core Idea
Prophetic practice differs: face between hands (Muslim) vs hands shoulder-width (Bukhari); Hanafi prefers between hands, but combination is possible.

The positioning of hands during prostration is a point of inter-madhhab difference between Hanafis and Shafi'is. This lesson examines the respective proofs and shows how the Hanafi school chooses the placement of the face between the palms, with a view that it is better for achieving arm separation.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that it is sunnah to place the face between the palms (بين الكفين) during sujud. This is based on the hadith from Muslim.
The matn explicit says 'كون السجود بين كفيه'.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it is sunnah to place the hands parallel to the shoulders (حذو المنكبين), based on the hadith in Bukhari.
The passage states 'وبه قال الشافعي'.
3
Follow each proof
Hanafi proof: Muslim reports that when the Prophet prostrated, he placed his face between his hands. Shafi'i proof: Bukhari reports that he placed his hands parallel to his shoulders.
Both are sahih ahadith, so the difference is in preference.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school does not reject the hadith of Bukhari but prefers the hadith of Muslim because it achieves the recommended arm separation (mujafah) and is consistent with the beginning of the rak'ah (placing hands near the face during takbir).
Some Hanafi scholars (like al-Kamal) suggest combining both positions: placing hands so that the face is between them and the hands are near the shoulders.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis place their face between their hands; Shafi'is place their hands shoulder-width. The difference is in the recommended sunnah, not in validity.
Both positions are valid and do not affect the validity of the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(And) it is sunnah (to rise from ruku) according to the correct view, and it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that the rising from it is fard, and it has preceded. (And) it is sunnah (to stand after it), i.e., after rising from ruku, (with tranquility) due to transmission. (And) it is sunnah (to place his knees) first on the ground, (then his hands, then his face) when descending (for prostration), and he prostrates between them. (And) it is sunnah (the opposite for rising) to stand by lifting his face, then his hands, then his knees if he has no excuse. But if he is weak or wearing khuffs, he does what he can. And it is recommended to descend with the right (knee) and rise with the left. Because the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he prostrated, placed his knees before his hands, and when he rose, he lifted his hands before his knees. (And) it is sunnah (the takbir of prostration) as we have narrated. (And) it is sunnah (the takbir of rising from it) as narrated. (And) it is sunnah (that prostration be made between his hands), i.e., placing his face between his palms. Because he, peace be upon him, when he prostrated, placed his face between his hands, narrated by Muslim. And in Bukhari, when he prostrated, he placed his hands parallel to his shoulders. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, said that. And some researchers said to combine, and that is to do both. His statement: (And it is sunnah to rise from ruku etc.) in al-Nahr from al-Mujtaba, attributed to al-Sadr al-Qudat: completing the ruku and completing every pillar is wajib according to them (the two), and according to Abu Yusuf it is fard. Similarly, raising the head from ruku, standing upright, and tranquility therein, so he must complete the ruku until every limb is tranquil, and likewise the prostration. If he omits anything from that forgetfully, sajda al-sahw is required. Ibn Amir Hajj said: That is correct, as mentioned by al-Sayyid. His statement: (then his face) – he begins by placing the nose. His statement: (when descending) is connected to everything preceding; his statement: 'and he prostrates between them' means between his hands, but it would be better to delete it because the author explicitly states after that: 'by lifting his face, then his hands', i.e., and he places them on his knees, and rises on the balls of his feet, and it is disliked to advance one foot when rising. His statement: (he does what he can) i.e., in descending and rising. His statement: (and it is recommended to descend with the right) i.e., with the knee, by advancing it slightly over the left, and likewise it is recommended to rise with the left first. His statement: (because the Messenger of Allah etc.) does not serve as proof for everything claimed; it is possible it is only proof for what is in the matn, and that is apparent. His statement: (as we have narrated) that the Prophet, peace be upon him, would say the takbir at every lowering and raising except the rising from ruku, for he would say 'sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'. His statement: (and al-Shafi'i said) – the text of al-Tabyin agrees with him, and according to what al-Hamawi transmitted, placing the hands parallel to the shoulders is a good deportment. His statement: (and some researchers said) – he is al-Kamal, may Allah be pleased with him, and his statement 'and that is to do' is an interpretation of the combination, and in some copies: 'and it is said: although placing between the hands is better, because it achieves the recommended separation [of arms] which is not present in anything else, and because the end of the rak'ah is connected to its beginning, so just as he places his head between his hands at the beginning of the rak'ah, so too at the end.'

This passage covers the sunnah actions related to transitioning between positions in prayer. It is sunnah to rise from ruku (though some narrations say fard according to Abu Hanifa, but the correct view is sunnah). Standing with tranquility after rising is sunnah. Some Hanafi scholars combine both by placing hands such that the face is between them and the hands are near the shoulders, but the preferred view is between the hands.

Key Terms
بين الكفين (bayn al-kaffayn): Placing the face between the hands during sujud
حذو المنكبين (hidha al-mankibayn): Hands level with the shoulders
المجافاة (al-mujafah): Separation of the arms from the sides during sujud

Raising from Ruku': Sunnah or Fard? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on raising from ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on raising from ruku', explain the intra-Hanafi differences, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Raising from ruku' is sunnah on the correct view, but some early authorities considered it fard — a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

The act of raising from ruku' (al-raf' min al-ruku') may seem straightforward, yet its legal status is debated within the Hanafi school. The base text of Maraqi al-Falah declares it sunnah, but the hashiya reveals a narration from Abu Hanifa himself calling it fard, and Abu Yusuf holding it as fard. This lesson unpacks the evidence and clarifies the relied-upon position for practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act in question is raising the head and torso from the bowing position (ruku') in prayer.
2
State the ruling in the base text
The base text of Maraqi al-Falah states it is sunnah, as indicated by 'يسن'.
3
Recognize contradictory transmissions
A narration from Abu Hanifa considers it fard, and Abu Yusuf also holds it as fard.
4
Understand the mufta bihi
The correct (sahih) view is that it is sunnah, but forgetful omission requires sajda sahw, indicating a level of emphasis.
This is a critical refinement: the ruling appears relaxed but practical effect includes compensation.
5
Cross-madhhab comparison
The Shafi'i school considers raising from ruku' a pillar (fard), whereas the Hanafi school on the correct view considers it sunnah.

الصلاة على الأرض أفضل، ثم على ما أنبتته ذكره المرغيناني، وغيره لأن الصلاة سرها التواضع، والخشوع وذلك في مباشرة الأرض أظهر وأتم إلا لضرورة حر، أو ،برد أو نحوهما، ويلحق بها ما أنبتته لهذا المعنى ذكره ابن أمير حاج . قوله : (لأن الرفع) في مجمع الأنهر عن المطلب الصحيح من مذهب الإمام أن الإنتقال فرض، والرفع سنة . قوله : ( وتسن الجلسة بين السجدتين المراد بها الطمأنينة في القومة، وتفترض عند أبي يوسف، ومقدار الجلوس عندنا بين السجدتين مقدار تسبيحة، وليس فيه ذكر مسنون ا في السراج، وكذا ليس بعد الرفع من الركوع دعاء، وما ورد فيهما محمول على التهجد الأنهر قوله : (كما فعله النبي بحيث تكون أطراف أصابعه على حرفي كما كما في مجمع
He corrects it, but that means he did not raise his head nor lower it. And it is sunnah (raising from ruku') according to the correct view, and it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that raising from it is fard, and it has preceded. And it is sunnah (standing after it) i.e. after raising from ruku' (with tranquility) for transmission. And it is sunnah (placing his knees) first on the ground (then his hands then his face) when descending (for prostration), and he prostrates between them. And it is sunnah (the opposite for rising) for standing: that he raises his face then his hands then his knees if there is no excuse. But if he is weak or wearing khuffs, he does what he can. And it is recommended to descend with the right and rise with the left, because the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم when he prostrated placed his knees before his hands, and when he arose he raised his hands before his knees. And it is sunnah (the takbir of prostration) due to what we have narrated. And it is sunnah (the takbir of rising from it) due to what is reported. And it is sunnah (the prostration being) i.e. making the prostration between his palms, because he when he prostrated placed his face between his palms - narrated by Muslim, and in Bukhari: when he prostrated he placed his palms level with his shoulders. And al-Shafi'i رضي الله عنه said the same. And some scholars said to combine: that he does this once and that once, although between the palms is better, and it is good. And it is sunnah (his tasbih in prostration) i.e. he says: Subhana Rabbi al-A'la (three times) due to what we narrated. And it is sunnah (the man holding his belly away from his thighs and his elbows away from his sides) and holding his forearms away from the ground) except in crowding, guarding against forbidden harm, because he when he prostrated held away so that if a young goat wanted to pass between his arms it would pass, and he would incline so much that the whiteness of his armpits would be seen. And he عليه السلام said: 'Do not spread like a beast spreads, and support on your palms, and expose your upper arms, for if you do that, every limb of yours prostrates.' And it is sunnah for a woman to lower herself and stick her belly to her thighs, because he عليه السلام passed by two women praying, and said: 'When you prostrate, press some flesh to some flesh, for a woman is not like a man in that, as she is a concealed 'awrah.' And the qawma (standing after prostration) is sunnah, i.e. completing it, because rising from prostration is fard up to near sitting, so completing it is sunnah. And the jalsah (sitting) between the two prostrations is sunnah, and placing the hands on the thighs during the sitting between the two prostrations is sunnah, so that it is like the state of tashahhud as the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم did, and he does not grab the knees. Its end is a proof. His saying: (i.e. he did not raise) is an interpretation on the way of ordered publication as you know, and it is sunnah to distance [?] from his sides and stick his heels therein and face his toes toward the qibla, i.e. the toes of his feet, as in al-Qahistani from al-Zahidi. His saying: (and it is sunnah to raise from ruku' etc.) in al-Nahr from al-Mujtaba attributed to al-Sadr al-Qada: completing ruku' and perfecting every pillar is wajib according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Abu Yusuf it is fard, and similarly raising the head from ruku', and standing upright, and standing, and tranquility therein, so one must complete ruku' until every limb of it is at rest, and likewise prostration. If one leaves something of that forgetfully, sajda sahw is required. Ibn Amir Hajj said: that is correct; mentioned by al-Sayyid. His saying: (then his face) and he begins by placing the nose. His saying: (when descending) is connected to all before it. His saying: and he prostrates between them, i.e. between his hands; it is better to omit it because the author stated it later in his saying: that he raises his face then his hands, i.e., and he places them on his knees and rises on the balls of his feet, and it is disliked to advance one foot when rising. His saying: (he does what he can) i.e., in descending and rising. His saying: (and it is recommended to descend with the right) i.e., with the knee by putting it forward a little before the left, and likewise rising with the left first. His saying: (because the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم etc.) does not serve as evidence for all that is claimed; it is possible it is evidence only for what is in the work, and that is apparent. His saying: (because we narrated) that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم used to say takbir at every lowering and raising except the raising from ruku', for he used to say tasmi' in it. And his saying for the reported: it is this very one. His saying: (and al-Shafi'i رضي الله عنه said the same) and the text of al-Tabyin agrees with him, and it is as al-Hamawi transmitted: placing the hands level with the shoulders is proper. His saying: (and some scholars said) is al-Kamal رضي الله عنه, and his saying: 'he does' is an interpretation of combining, and in a copy: 'he said: although between the palms is better because it achieves the sunnah of holding away in a way not present in other positions, and because the end of the rak'ah is considered like its beginning, so just as he places his head between his palms at the takbir in the beginning of the rak'ah, so too.' His saying: (and his tasbih is sunnah) and directing the fingers of his hands and feet toward the qibla. His saying: (except in crowding) is connected to his saying: and holding his elbows away from his sides; as for holding the forearms away, it does not cause harm in crowding. His saying: (if a young goat wanted) with damm of the unified and fatha of the ha, diminutive of bahma (with fatha then sukun) - it is correct in the narration: a sheep's offspring after it is a sakhla, for its mother first gives birth to a sakhla, then it becomes a bahma. His saying: (until the whiteness of his armpits is seen) i.e., it is seen from behind him as clarified in the narration of al-Tahawi. His saying: (and support on your palms) i.e., rely. His saying: (and expose your upper arms) with a hamza qat', and al-dhib'an is dual of dhib' with fatha of the daad and sukun of the baa, plural adhba' like farakh and afrakh as in al-Misbah and al-Sihah, and it means the whole arm, or its middle, or its inner part; as for with damm of the baa, it is the predatory animal and the drought; some said the former is also with damm as in al-Qahistani etc. His saying: (For if you do that etc.) is an explanation of the wisdom of what was mentioned, because then every limb appears by itself and does not rely on another in performing worship, and because it is more like humility and more effective in placing the forehead on the ground and further from the postures of the lazy. Sub-issue: praying on the ground is best, then on what it produces, as mentioned by al-Marghinani etc., because the secret of prayer is humility and khushu', and that is more apparent and complete in direct contact with the ground, except for a necessity like heat, cold, or the like; what it produces is attached to it for this meaning, as mentioned by Ibn Amir Hajj. His saying: (because the raising) in Majma' al-Anhur from al-Matlab: the correct view in the madhhab of the Imam is that moving is fard and raising is sunnah. His saying: (and the jalsah between the two prostrations is sunnah) is meant to be tranquility in the qawma, and it is fard according to Abu Yusuf. The amount of sitting between the two prostrations according to us is the amount of a tasbiha, and there is no mention of a sunnah dhikr in it in al-Siraj; similarly there is no du'a after raising from ruku', and what is reported about them is carried on tahajjud as in al-Anhar. His saying: (as the Prophet did) so that the tips of his fingers are on the edges as in Majma'.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage from Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah details the sunan (recommended acts) related to ruku' and sujud in prayer. It is a critical refinement of the base text, expanding on proofs and noting intra-Hanafi differences. The passage begins by stating that it is sunnah (on the correct view) to raise from ruku', despite a narration from Abu Hanifa considering it fard. The hashiya adds that according to Abu Yusuf it is fard, and according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, completing ruku' perfectly is wajib. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that it is sunnah, but leaving it forgetfully requires sajda sahw according to Ibn Amir Hajj. Following this, the passage lists various sunan: standing with tranquility after ruku', placing knees before hands before prostrating, the opposite for rising, saying takbir when going into and rising from sujud, placing the face between the palms during sujud (a Hanafi preference, while Shafi'i holds palms level with shoulders; some scholars recommend alternating), the tasbih three times, holding the belly away from thighs and elbows from sides, the woman's different posture (pressing flesh together due to concealment), the qawma (standing after prostration) and jalsah (sitting between prostrations) being sunnah with a brief sitting duration of one tasbiha. The hashiya clarifies that no specific dhikr is prescribed between prostrations, and du'a after ruku' is only for tahajjud. Overall, the text emphasizes the distinction between obligatory and recommended acts, supported by hadith and scholarly consensus within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الرفع من الركوع (al-raf' min al-ruku'): Raising the head and torso from the bowing position in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on raising the head from ruku'?
A) Fard
B) Sunnah
C) Wajib
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Raising from ruku' is sunnah in the Hanafi school, but its omission forgetfully requires sajda sahw.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Sunnah Acts of Sujud: Takbir, Tasbih, and Posture
Lists sunan of sujud with proofs and a cross-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of sujud, explain the Hanafi preference for hand placement, and describe the difference in posture for men and women.

Core Idea
Prostration includes several sunnah acts: takbir, tasbih, proper hand placement, and mujafaat for men, with a distinct posture for women.

Sujud is a central part of prayer, and the Hanafi school emphasizes several recommended acts (sunan) to perfect it. These include saying takbir when going into and rising from sujud, reciting tasbih three times, placing the face between the palms (a Hanafi preference), holding the arms away from the ground (mujafaat) for men, and a more compact posture for women. This lesson examines the evidence for these practices and a cross-madhhab difference on hand placement.

Guided Path
1
List the sunan of sujud
Identify the recommended acts: takbir at the start and end of sujud, tasbih (Subhana Rabbi al-A'la) three times, placement of face between palms, mujafaat (holding belly and arms away) for men, and the woman's compact posture.
2
Examine the proof for each sunnah
Each sunnah is supported by hadith. For example, the tasbih is proven by what we narrated (the Prophet said it). The takbir is proven by the practice of the Prophet (Sallallahu alayhi wa sallam).
3
Analyze the hand placement dispute
The Hanafi school prefers placing the face between the palms (based on Muslim), while the Shafi'i school prefers palms level with shoulders (based on Bukhari). Some Hanafi scholars recommend alternating.
This is a cross-madhhab ikhtilaf.
4
Describe the posture of men vs. women
Men are to hold the belly away from thighs and elbows from sides (mujafaat). Women are to keep the body close, pressing the belly to the thighs, as they are 'awrah.
