على حرفي كما كما في مجمع
He corrects it, but that means he did not raise his head nor lower it. And it is sunnah (raising from ruku') according to the correct view, and it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that raising from it is fard, and it has preceded. And it is sunnah (standing after it) i.e. after raising from ruku' (with tranquility) for transmission. And it is sunnah (placing his knees) first on the ground (then his hands then his face) when descending (for prostration), and he prostrates between them. And it is sunnah (the opposite for rising) for standing: that he raises his face then his hands then his knees if there is no excuse. But if he is weak or wearing khuffs, he does what he can. And it is recommended to descend with the right and rise with the left, because the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم when he prostrated placed his knees before his hands, and when he arose he raised his hands before his knees. And it is sunnah (the takbir of prostration) due to what we have narrated. And it is sunnah (the takbir of rising from it) due to what is reported. And it is sunnah (the prostration being) i.e. making the prostration between his palms, because he when he prostrated placed his face between his palms - narrated by Muslim, and in Bukhari: when he prostrated he placed his palms level with his shoulders. And al-Shafi'i رضي الله عنه said the same. And some scholars said to combine: that he does this once and that once, although between the palms is better, and it is good. And it is sunnah (his tasbih in prostration) i.e. he says: Subhana Rabbi al-A'la (three times) due to what we narrated. And it is sunnah (the man holding his belly away from his thighs and his elbows away from his sides) and holding his forearms away from the ground) except in crowding, guarding against forbidden harm, because he when he prostrated held away so that if a young goat wanted to pass between his arms it would pass, and he would incline so much that the whiteness of his armpits would be seen. And he عليه السلام said: 'Do not spread like a beast spreads, and support on your palms, and expose your upper arms, for if you do that, every limb of yours prostrates.' And it is sunnah for a woman to lower herself and stick her belly to her thighs, because he عليه السلام passed by two women praying, and said: 'When you prostrate, press some flesh to some flesh, for a woman is not like a man in that, as she is a concealed 'awrah.' And the qawma (standing after prostration) is sunnah, i.e. completing it, because rising from prostration is fard up to near sitting, so completing it is sunnah. And the jalsah (sitting) between the two prostrations is sunnah, and placing the hands on the thighs during the sitting between the two prostrations is sunnah, so that it is like the state of tashahhud as the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم did, and he does not grab the knees. Its end is a proof. His saying: (i.e. he did not raise) is an interpretation on the way of ordered publication as you know, and it is sunnah to distance [?] from his sides and stick his heels therein and face his toes toward the qibla, i.e. the toes of his feet, as in al-Qahistani from al-Zahidi. His saying: (and it is sunnah to raise from ruku' etc.) in al-Nahr from al-Mujtaba attributed to al-Sadr al-Qada: completing ruku' and perfecting every pillar is wajib according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Abu Yusuf it is fard, and similarly raising the head from ruku', and standing upright, and standing, and tranquility therein, so one must complete ruku' until every limb of it is at rest, and likewise prostration. If one leaves something of that forgetfully, sajda sahw is required. Ibn Amir Hajj said: that is correct; mentioned by al-Sayyid. His saying: (then his face) and he begins by placing the nose. His saying: (when descending) is connected to all before it. His saying: and he prostrates between them, i.e. between his hands; it is better to omit it because the author stated it later in his saying: that he raises his face then his hands, i.e., and he places them on his knees and rises on the balls of his feet, and it is disliked to advance one foot when rising. His saying: (he does what he can) i.e., in descending and rising. His saying: (and it is recommended to descend with the right) i.e., with the knee by putting it forward a little before the left, and likewise rising with the left first. His saying: (because the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم etc.) does not serve as evidence for all that is claimed; it is possible it is evidence only for what is in the work, and that is apparent. His saying: (because we narrated) that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم used to say takbir at every lowering and raising except the raising from ruku', for he used to say tasmi' in it. And his saying for the reported: it is this very one. His saying: (and al-Shafi'i رضي الله عنه said the same) and the text of al-Tabyin agrees with him, and it is as al-Hamawi transmitted: placing the hands level with the shoulders is proper. His saying: (and some scholars said) is al-Kamal رضي الله عنه, and his saying: 'he does' is an interpretation of combining, and in a copy: 'he said: although between the palms is better because it achieves the sunnah of holding away in a way not present in other positions, and because the end of the rak'ah is considered like its beginning, so just as he places his head between his palms at the takbir in the beginning of the rak'ah, so too.' His saying: (and his tasbih is sunnah) and directing the fingers of his hands and feet toward the qibla. His saying: (except in crowding) is connected to his saying: and holding his elbows away from his sides; as for holding the forearms away, it does not cause harm in crowding. His saying: (if a young goat wanted) with damm of the unified and fatha of the ha, diminutive of bahma (with fatha then sukun) - it is correct in the narration: a sheep's offspring after it is a sakhla, for its mother first gives birth to a sakhla, then it becomes a bahma. His saying: (until the whiteness of his armpits is seen) i.e., it is seen from behind him as clarified in the narration of al-Tahawi. His saying: (and support on your palms) i.e., rely. His saying: (and expose your upper arms) with a hamza qat', and al-dhib'an is dual of dhib' with fatha of the daad and sukun of the baa, plural adhba' like farakh and afrakh as in al-Misbah and al-Sihah, and it means the whole arm, or its middle, or its inner part; as for with damm of the baa, it is the predatory animal and the drought; some said the former is also with damm as in al-Qahistani etc. His saying: (For if you do that etc.) is an explanation of the wisdom of what was mentioned, because then every limb appears by itself and does not rely on another in performing worship, and because it is more like humility and more effective in placing the forehead on the ground and further from the postures of the lazy. Sub-issue: praying on the ground is best, then on what it produces, as mentioned by al-Marghinani etc., because the secret of prayer is humility and khushu', and that is more apparent and complete in direct contact with the ground, except for a necessity like heat, cold, or the like; what it produces is attached to it for this meaning, as mentioned by Ibn Amir Hajj. His saying: (because the raising) in Majma' al-Anhur from al-Matlab: the correct view in the madhhab of the Imam is that moving is fard and raising is sunnah. His saying: (and the jalsah between the two prostrations is sunnah) is meant to be tranquility in the qawma, and it is fard according to Abu Yusuf. The amount of sitting between the two prostrations according to us is the amount of a tasbiha, and there is no mention of a sunnah dhikr in it in al-Siraj; similarly there is no du'a after raising from ruku', and what is reported about them is carried on tahajjud as in al-Anhar. His saying: (as the Prophet did) so that the tips of his fingers are on the edges as in Majma'.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage from Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah details the sunan (recommended acts) related to ruku' and sujud in prayer. It is a critical refinement of the base text, expanding on proofs and noting intra-Hanafi differences. The passage begins by stating that it is sunnah (on the correct view) to raise from ruku', despite a narration from Abu Hanifa considering it fard. The hashiya adds that according to Abu Yusuf it is fard, and according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, completing ruku' perfectly is wajib. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that it is sunnah, but leaving it forgetfully requires sajda sahw according to Ibn Amir Hajj. Following this, the passage lists various sunan: standing with tranquility after ruku', placing knees before hands before prostrating, the opposite for rising, saying takbir when going into and rising from sujud, placing the face between the palms during sujud (a Hanafi preference, while Shafi'i holds palms level with shoulders; some scholars recommend alternating), the tasbih three times, holding the belly away from thighs and elbows from sides, the woman's different posture (pressing flesh together due to concealment), the qawma (standing after prostration) and jalsah (sitting between prostrations) being sunnah with a brief sitting duration of one tasbiha. The hashiya clarifies that no specific dhikr is prescribed between prostrations, and du'a after ruku' is only for tahajjud. Overall, the text emphasizes the distinction between obligatory and recommended acts, supported by hadith and scholarly consensus within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المجافاة (al-mujafaat): Holding the arms and body away from the ground and sides during prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which position for the hands during sujud is preferred?
A) Palms level with shoulders
B) Face between the palms
C) Hands on the ground in front
D) No specific position

Key Takeaway
The sunan of sujud include takbir, tasbih, face between palms (Hanafi), mujafaat for men, and a compact posture for women.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
The Qawmah and Jalsah: Standing and Sitting Between Prostrations
Rulings on qawmah and jalsah with intra-Hanafi difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the qawmah (standing after prostration) and jalsah (sitting between prostrations) in the Hanafi school, including the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the jalsah.

Core Idea
The qawmah and jalsah are sunnah in the Hanafi school, though Abu Yusuf considered jalsah fard — a difference with practical implications.

After prostrating, the worshipper stands up (qawmah) and later sits briefly between the two prostrations (jalsah). The Hanafi school generally regards these as sunnah, but there is a known intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf held that the jalsah (sitting) is fard. This lesson clarifies the rulings, the evidence, and the practical consequence of these positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
The qawmah is the standing after the first prostration, and the jalsah is the sitting between the two prostrations.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on each
Both are sunnah according to the relied-upon view. The qawmah is sunnah because the obligatory part is just the initial rising; completing the standing is sunnah. The jalsah is sunnah with a brief duration of one tasbiha.
3
Note Abu Yusuf's opposition on jalsah
Abu Yusuf considers the jalsah (sitting between prostrations) to be fard, which would make its omission invalidate the prayer.
4
Understand the evidence
The text cites that the Prophet (Sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) performed these acts consistently, and they were transmitted. The mufta bihi is sunnah.

على حرفي كما كما في مجمع
He corrects it, but that means he did not raise his head nor lower it. And it is sunnah (raising from ruku') according to the correct view, and it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that raising from it is fard, and it has preceded. And it is sunnah (standing after it) i.e. after raising from ruku' (with tranquility) for transmission. And it is sunnah (placing his knees) first on the ground (then his hands then his face) when descending (for prostration), and he prostrates between them. And it is sunnah (the opposite for rising) for standing: that he raises his face then his hands then his knees if there is no excuse. But if he is weak or wearing khuffs, he does what he can. And it is recommended to descend with the right and rise with the left, because the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم when he prostrated placed his knees before his hands, and when he arose he raised his hands before his knees. And it is sunnah (the takbir of prostration) due to what we have narrated. And it is sunnah (the takbir of rising from it) due to what is reported. And it is sunnah (the prostration being) i.e. making the prostration between his palms, because he when he prostrated placed his face between his palms - narrated by Muslim, and in Bukhari: when he prostrated he placed his palms level with his shoulders. And al-Shafi'i رضي الله عنه said the same. And some scholars said to combine: that he does this once and that once, although between the palms is better, and it is good. And it is sunnah (his tasbih in prostration) i.e. he says: Subhana Rabbi al-A'la (three times) due to what we narrated. And it is sunnah (the man holding his belly away from his thighs and his elbows away from his sides) and holding his forearms away from the ground) except in crowding, guarding against forbidden harm, because he when he prostrated held away so that if a young goat wanted to pass between his arms it would pass, and he would incline so much that the whiteness of his armpits would be seen. And he عليه السلام said: 'Do not spread like a beast spreads, and support on your palms, and expose your upper arms, for if you do that, every limb of yours prostrates.' And it is sunnah for a woman to lower herself and stick her belly to her thighs, because he عليه السلام passed by two women praying, and said: 'When you prostrate, press some flesh to some flesh, for a woman is not like a man in that, as she is a concealed 'awrah.' And the qawma (standing after prostration) is sunnah, i.e. completing it, because rising from prostration is fard up to near sitting, so completing it is sunnah. And the jalsah (sitting) between the two prostrations is sunnah, and placing the hands on the thighs during the sitting between the two prostrations is sunnah, so that it is like the state of tashahhud as the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم did, and he does not grab the knees. Its end is a proof. His saying: (i.e. he did not raise) is an interpretation on the way of ordered publication as you know, and it is sunnah to distance [?] from his sides and stick his heels therein and face his toes toward the qibla, i.e. the toes of his feet, as in al-Qahistani from al-Zahidi. His saying: (and it is sunnah to raise from ruku' etc.) in al-Nahr from al-Mujtaba attributed to al-Sadr al-Qada: completing ruku' and perfecting every pillar is wajib according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Abu Yusuf it is fard, and similarly raising the head from ruku', and standing upright, and standing, and tranquility therein, so one must complete ruku' until every limb of it is at rest, and likewise prostration. If one leaves something of that forgetfully, sajda sahw is required. Ibn Amir Hajj said: that is correct; mentioned by al-Sayyid. His saying: (then his face) and he begins by placing the nose. His saying: (when descending) is connected to all before it. His saying: and he prostrates between them, i.e. between his hands; it is better to omit it because the author stated it later in his saying: that he raises his face then his hands, i.e., and he places them on his knees and rises on the balls of his feet, and it is disliked to advance one foot when rising. His saying: (he does what he can) i.e., in descending and rising. His saying: (and it is recommended to descend with the right) i.e., with the knee by putting it forward a little before the left, and likewise rising with the left first. His saying: (because the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم etc.) does not serve as evidence for all that is claimed; it is possible it is evidence only for what is in the work, and that is apparent. His saying: (because we narrated) that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم used to say takbir at every lowering and raising except the raising from ruku', for he used to say tasmi' in it. And his saying for the reported: it is this very one. His saying: (and al-Shafi'i رضي الله عنه said the same) and the text of al-Tabyin agrees with him, and it is as al-Hamawi transmitted: placing the hands level with the shoulders is proper. His saying: (and some scholars said) is al-Kamal رضي الله عنه, and his saying: 'he does' is an interpretation of combining, and in a copy: 'he said: although between the palms is better because it achieves the sunnah of holding away in a way not present in other positions, and because the end of the rak'ah is considered like its beginning, so just as he places his head between his palms at the takbir in the beginning of the rak'ah, so too.' His saying: (and his tasbih is sunnah) and directing the fingers of his hands and feet toward the qibla. His saying: (except in crowding) is connected to his saying: and holding his elbows away from his sides; as for holding the forearms away, it does not cause harm in crowding. His saying: (if a young goat wanted) with damm of the unified and fatha of the ha, diminutive of bahma (with fatha then sukun) - it is correct in the narration: a sheep's offspring after it is a sakhla, for its mother first gives birth to a sakhla, then it becomes a bahma. His saying: (until the whiteness of his armpits is seen) i.e., it is seen from behind him as clarified in the narration of al-Tahawi. His saying: (and support on your palms) i.e., rely. His saying: (and expose your upper arms) with a hamza qat', and al-dhib'an is dual of dhib' with fatha of the daad and sukun of the baa, plural adhba' like farakh and afrakh as in al-Misbah and al-Sihah, and it means the whole arm, or its middle, or its inner part; as for with damm of the baa, it is the predatory animal and the drought; some said the former is also with damm as in al-Qahistani etc. His saying: (For if you do that etc.) is an explanation of the wisdom of what was mentioned, because then every limb appears by itself and does not rely on another in performing worship, and because it is more like humility and more effective in placing the forehead on the ground and further from the postures of the lazy. Sub-issue: praying on the ground is best, then on what it produces, as mentioned by al-Marghinani etc., because the secret of prayer is humility and khushu', and that is more apparent and complete in direct contact with the ground, except for a necessity like heat, cold, or the like; what it produces is attached to it for this meaning, as mentioned by Ibn Amir Hajj. His saying: (because the raising) in Majma' al-Anhur from al-Matlab: the correct view in the madhhab of the Imam is that moving is fard and raising is sunnah. His saying: (and the jalsah between the two prostrations is sunnah) is meant to be tranquility in the qawma, and it is fard according to Abu Yusuf. The amount of sitting between the two prostrations according to us is the amount of a tasbiha, and there is no mention of a sunnah dhikr in it in al-Siraj; similarly there is no du'a after raising from ruku', and what is reported about them is carried on tahajjud as in al-Anhar. His saying: (as the Prophet did) so that the tips of his fingers are on the edges as in Majma'.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage from Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah details the sunan (recommended acts) related to ruku' and sujud in prayer. It is a critical refinement of the base text, expanding on proofs and noting intra-Hanafi differences. The passage begins by stating that it is sunnah (on the correct view) to raise from ruku', despite a narration from Abu Hanifa considering it fard. The hashiya adds that according to Abu Yusuf it is fard, and according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, completing ruku' perfectly is wajib. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that it is sunnah, but leaving it forgetfully requires sajda sahw according to Ibn Amir Hajj. Following this, the passage lists various sunan: standing with tranquility after ruku', placing knees before hands before prostrating, the opposite for rising, saying takbir when going into and rising from sujud, placing the face between the palms during sujud (a Hanafi preference, while Shafi'i holds palms level with shoulders; some scholars recommend alternating), the tasbih three times, holding the belly away from thighs and elbows from sides, the woman's different posture (pressing flesh together due to concealment), the qawma (standing after prostration) and jalsah (sitting between prostrations) being sunnah with a brief sitting duration of one tasbiha. The hashiya clarifies that no specific dhikr is prescribed between prostrations, and du'a after ruku' is only for tahajjud. Overall, the text emphasizes the distinction between obligatory and recommended acts, supported by hadith and scholarly consensus within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
القومة (al-qawmah): The standing posture after rising from prostration before descending for the second prostration.
الجلسة بين السجدتين (al-jalsah bayn al-sajdatayn): The sitting posture between the two prostrations in each rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is the ruling on the sitting between the two prostrations (jalsah)?
A) Fard
B) Sunnah
C) Wajib
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The qawmah and jalsah are sunnah in the Hanafi school, with the jalsah being the subject of an intra-Hanafi difference where Abu Yusuf held it as fard.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Sunan of Sajdah: Tasbih, Mujaafat, and Women's Posture
Describes the sunnan acts of prostration with their evidence from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunan acts of sajdah, explain their evidence, and distinguish between the postures of men and women.

Core Idea
Mujafaat in sajdah is sunnah mu'akkadah for men, but women must keep limbs close for modesty.

In this lesson, we explore the recommended acts (sunan) of prostration as taught by the Hanafi school. The passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi details the tasbih, the separation of body parts for men, and the contrasting posture for women, all supported by Prophetic practice and hadith. Understanding these sunan helps perfect one's prayer and embody humility before Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan of sajdah
List the three main sunan mentioned: saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' three times, mujafaat (separating belly from thighs, elbows from sides, forearms from ground) for men, and women lowering and pressing limbs together.
Tasbih is common to all, while mujafaat applies only to men.
2
Examine the evidence for each act
For tasbih, the general practice of the Prophet is cited. For mujafaat, the hadith 'Do not spread like a dog' and the report that a small animal could pass under him are used. For women, the hadith 'press some flesh together' is mentioned.
The hadith evidence is from ahad (single) narrations, giving zanni thubut but qati dalala.
3
Understand the wisdom behind mujafaat
The hadith explains that every limb prostrates when the arms are separated. The commentary adds that this shows humility and helps place the forehead firmly on the ground, avoiding lazy postures.
Mujafaat is not for women due to modesty; they are awrah and should compress.
4
Distinguish between men and women
Men are instructed to separate limbs widely, while women should keep their limbs close and stick their bellies to their thighs. The difference is based on the Prophet's directive for women to 'press some flesh together' because they are covered awrah.
This distinction is specific to Hanafi fiqh and is considered sunnah mu'akkadah.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
Practicing mujafaat in sajdah is recommended but not obligatory. Omitting it does not invalidate the prayer, but following it completes the sunnah and brings greater reward.
Praying directly on the ground is superior to mats unless needed for heat/cold.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن (تسبيحه) أي السجود بأن يقول : سبحان ربي الأعلى (ثلاثاً) لما روينا (و) يسن (مجافاة الرجل) أي مباعدته (بطنه عن فخذيه و مجافاة مرفقيه عن جنبيه (و) مجافاة ذراعيه عن الأرض) في غير زحمة حذرا عن الإيذاء المحرم لأنه كان إذا سجد جافى حتى لو شاءت بهيمة أن تمر بين يديه لمرت، وكان يجنح حتى يرى وضح إبطيه أي بياضهما وقال عليه السلام : «لا تبسط بسط السبع وادعم على راحتيك وأبد ضبعيك فإنك إذا فعلت ذلك سجد كل عضو منك» (و) يسن انخفاض المرأة ولزقها بطنها بفخذيها لأنه عليه السلام مر على امرأتين تصليان، فقال : إذا سجدتما فضما بعض اللحم إلى بعض فإن المرأة ليست في ذلك كالرجل لأنها عورة مستورة آخرها برهان قوله : (ويسن تسبيحه وتوجيهه أصابع يديه وأصابع رجليه نحو القبلة . قوله : (في غير زحمة مرتبط بقوله ومجافاة مرفقيه عن جنبيه، وأما مجافاة الذراعين عن فلا تؤذي في الإزدحام. قوله : (لو شاءت بهيمة) بضم الموحدة، وفتح الهاء تصغير بهمة بفتح فسكون، وهو الصواب في الرواية ولد الشاة بعد السخلة فإنه أول ما تضعه أمه سخلة، ثم يكون بهيمة . قوله : ( حتى يرى وضح أبطيه) أي يراه من خلفه كما جاء التصريح به في رواية الطحاوي قوله: (وادعم على راحتيك أي إعتمد قوله : (وأبد ضبعيك) بهمزة قطع والضبعان تثنية ضبع بفتح الضاد المعجمة وسكون الباء الموحدة لا غير والجمع أضباع كفرخ وأفراخ على ما في المصباح، والصحاح والعضد كله، أو وسطه، أو بطنه، وأما بضم الباء فهو الحيوان المفترس، والسنة المجدبة، وقيل في الأول بالضم أيضاً كما في القهستاني، وغيره . قوله : (فإنك إذا فعلت ذلك الخ) بيان لحكمة ما ذكر، وذلك لأنه حينئذ يظهر كل عضو بنفسه، ولا يعتمد على غيره في أداء العبادة، ولأنه أشبه بالتواضع وأبلغ في تمكين الجبهة من الأرض وأبعد عن هيئات الكسالى فرع الصلاة على الأرض أفضل، ثم على ما أنبتته ذكره المرغيناني، وغيره لأن الصلاة سرها التواضع، والخشوع وذلك في مباشرة الأرض أظهر وأتم إلا لضرورة حر، أو ،برد أو نحوهما، ويلحق بها ما أنبتته لهذا المعنى ذكره ابن أمير حاج .
And it is sunnah to say his tasbih, meaning of sajdah, by saying: Subhana Rabbiyal A'la (three times) due to what we have narrated. And it is sunnah for the man to separate, meaning to distance, his belly from his thighs, and to separate his elbows from his sides, and to separate his forearms from the ground, except in crowding, guarding against prohibited harm, because when he prostrated he would separate so much that if a small animal wanted to pass between his arms it would pass, and he would spread so that the whiteness of his armpits could be seen. And he said peace be upon him: 'Do not spread like a dog spreads, and support yourself on your palms, and expose your upper arms, for if you do that, every limb prostrates.' And it is sunnah for the woman to lower herself and stick her belly to her thighs, because he peace be upon him passed by two women praying and said: 'When you prostrate, press some flesh together, for the woman in that is not like the man, because she is a covered awrah.' The end of its proof is his statement: 'And it is sunnah his tasbih and directing the fingers of his hands and the toes of his feet towards the qibla.' His statement: 'except in crowding' is connected to his statement 'and to separate his elbows from his sides', and as for separating the forearms from the ground, that does not cause harm in crowding. His statement: 'if a small animal wanted' with dammah on the muwahhidah and fatha on the ha, diminutive of bahmah (with fatha then sukun), which is correct in the narration, meaning the young of a sheep after it is a lamb, for initially its mother gives birth to a lamb, then it becomes a bahmah. His statement: 'until the whiteness of his armpits could be seen' meaning it can be seen from behind him, as clarified in the narration of al-Tahawi. His statement: 'support yourself on your palms' meaning rely. His statement: 'expose your upper arms' with hamzat qat', and al-dhaba'an is the dual of dhab' (with fatha on the dad and sukun on the ba, no other), plural adhba' like farakh and afrakh as in al-Misbah and al-Sihah, meaning the entire arm, or its middle, or its inner side; as for with dammah on the ba, it is the predatory animal and the severe year of drought, and it is said in the first also with dammah as in al-Qahistani and others. His statement: 'for if you do that etc.' is an explanation of the wisdom of what was mentioned, because then every limb appears by itself and does not rely on another in performing worship, and because it is more like humility and more effective in placing the forehead on the ground, and further from the postures of the lazy. A branch: prayer on the ground is best, then on what it produces, mentioned by al-Margheenani and others, because the secret of prayer is humility and submissiveness, and that is more apparent and complete in direct contact with the earth, except for necessity of heat, cold, or the like, and what it produces is included for this meaning, mentioned by Ibn Amir Hajj.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah discussing the sunan (recommended acts) of sajdah (prostration). It begins by stating that saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' three times in sajdah is sunnah, supported by the general practice of the Prophet. Then it details the mujafaat (separation of body parts) for a man: keeping the belly away from the thighs, elbows from sides, and forearms from the ground. The hadith 'Do not spread like a dog' and the report that a small animal could pass under him are cited as evidence. Women are instructed to keep their limbs close together for modesty, as reported in a hadith. The commentary further explains the linguistic points and the wisdom behind these actions, emphasizing humility. The final branch ruling states that praying directly on the ground is superior to praying on a mat, as it enhances humility, unless there is a necessity like extreme heat or cold.

Key Terms
مجافاة (mujāfāt): The act of keeping body parts apart during prostration; specifically belly from thighs, elbows from sides, forearms from ground.
بهيمة (bahīmah): In this context, a small animal such as a lamb or young sheep.
وضح إبطيه (waḍḥ ibṭayhi): The whiteness (visible skin) of the armpits.
تسبيح (tasbīḥ): The act of saying 'Subhana Rabbiyal A'la' in sajdah.
انخفاض المرأة (inkhifāḍ al-marʼah): The woman lowering herself and pressing her limbs together in sajdah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling for a man to keep his belly away from his thighs during sajdah?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Mujafaat is a sunnah mu'akkadah for men, while women must keep limbs close; these acts are based on Prophetic practice and hadith, and omitting them does not invalidate the prayer but reduces its perfection.
